v0.25.207 Floor + platform tiles regen seamless + portal at 65% opacity

bugFloor tiles had visible gaps between repetitions

The v0.25.199 ludo-generated tiles were rendered as TWO distinct blocks side-by-side per source image, separated by a small transparent gap. The 'auto' seamless-bake didn't break on the gap (12-col threshold) so it captured both blocks AS ONE TILE — including the doubled black outlines and the internal gap between them. Tiled across a long ground span, this produced a visible vertical seam every tileW pixels.

featRe-generated all 10 tiles as continuous strips

Dispatched fresh prompts to Ludo AI explicitly requiring "seamless horizontally tileable, ONE continuous strip, no outlines or borders on the left or right edges, edges blend smoothly so it tiles infinitely". New 16:9 source aspect bakes to one full-width seamless tile.

v0.25.206 Warrior 2H swing — much more dramatic

featBigger arc + anticipation hold

Arm rotation arc went from −2.40 → +1.90 (4.30 rad) to −2.95 → +2.50 (5.45 rad, +27%). New 9-frame anticipation HOLD at the apex of the windup so the sword visibly cocks behind the head before snapping forward. Strike phase tightened from 0.36 → 0.28 for a sharper SNAP. Recovery whip extended from 1.45 → 1.95 for heavier follow-through.

featBody commits like an executioner

  • Spine pre-twist on windup −0.22 → −0.42, strike commit 0.65 → 1.10, recovery whip 0.30 → 0.55
  • Head matches at half scale (more aggressive lookahead during the strike)
  • Leg bend on strike 0.22 → 0.40 — knees squat into the swing

featForward lurch overhaul

New _heroVecAttackWindup(t) ramps 0→1 through the windup phase then decays. Warrior bob channel now leans the body BACK during windup (−2.4 px spine, −1.4 px head) before snapping forward (+5.5 px, was +3.6). Vertical dip 1.6 → 3.0, head dip 4.2 → 6.5.

featSlash-arc visual fires for warrior + scales up

The arc trail under the weapon was gated to animName === 'attack' only — warriors weren't getting it at all. Now fires for attack_warrior too, with warrior-specific scale: arc radius 25 → 42, arc span 2.95 → 5.45, outer stroke width 7 → 11, inner stroke 2 → 4, brighter alpha. Plus a new gold "shockwave" arc behind the trail at peak swing for the dramatic flash.

polishSquash-stretch overhauled

Arm vertical stretch 0.40 → 0.65. Spine stretch 0.10 → 0.18, compress 0.96 → 0.92. Hand grow on impact 0.22 → 0.40 + 0.16 → 0.26 sin overlay. The whole body reads as a coiled spring releasing.

bugSoul Vortex duration was 500 s, not 30 s

Hazard life is decremented -=1 per frame at 60 FPS, but lich_harvest set life: 30000 — that's 30000 frames = 8 minutes 20 seconds, not 30 seconds. Carryover from a millisecond-based earlier implementation. Fixed: life: 1800, maxLife: 1800 (30 s × 60 frames). Render fade-out window also flipped from h.life / 4000 to h.life / 240 so the pool fades over the final 4 s instead of the final 13% of an 8-minute lifetime.

v0.25.201 Lich Soul Vortex (G) — much larger AOE, higher damage, stronger pull

featSoul Vortex AOE: 180 → 320 px (+78%)

Pull radius nearly doubled and the on-screen pool ellipse scaled to match (outer 100→200, inner 85→170). Hazard rect bumped from 200×100 to 400×140 so the visual + hitbox span the full vortex.

featDamage uplift + faster ticks

Per-tick atk multiplier 0.80× → 1.40× (+75%). Tick interval 12 → 8 frames (50% faster damage cadence). HP siphon-back ratio (30%) preserved — heavier damage means heavier heal-back too.

featSuction force overhauled

Pull force was 0.5 × (1 − dist/180) — zero at the rim. New formula: 0.4 + 1.2 × (1 − dist/320). 0.4 floor at the rim means even the farthest enemy in the AOE feels the tug; near the centre the pull peaks at 1.6 (3.2× the prior centre value). Vertical pull stays at 60% of horizontal so mobs slide in along the ground rather than launching up.

polishOpen animation scaled up

Cast burst widened: 50 → 80 ring particles, particle radius 8 → 14, central explosion radius 140 → 240, screen flash 0.40 → 0.55, shake 10 → 14. Rising wisp spawn box doubled to 320 px wide. Cooldown stays at 30 s.

v0.25.198 Eyes back at head's drawn shadow ovals (revert v0.25.197 lift)

polishEyes restored to v0.25.195 position

polishVector eye deletion + jump head fix retained

v0.25.197 Eyes lifted to upper face + vector eye renderers deleted + jump no head squish

polishEyes raised 58 px to match reference

The "anatomically correct" alignment to the head's drawn sockets at y≈466 read as too-low / cheek-area against the head's shadow ovals. Per user reference, eyes now sit at the upper face (chibi anime canon — eyes at the bangs/forehead boundary, not mid-face). Final eye-sprite alpha-bbox: (394, 367, 582, 450) in the 800×800 head-aligned canvas. The head's drawn shadow ovals now read as cheek shadows, which adds dimension.

featRemoved all vector eye renderer functions

Deleted _drawEye_sparkle, _drawEye_star, _drawEye_sleepy, _drawEye_dot, the _EYE_RENDERERS dispatch table, the _irisGrad linear-gradient setup, and the if (!_useSpriteEyes) { ... } fallback branch. LX_EYES sprite layer is now the only eye render path. Cold-start frames before LX_EYES.default decodes simply skip the eye draw — the v0.25.173 preloader gates the world reveal until sprites are ready, so this is invisible in practice. Net maple_game.html diff: −82 lines.

polishHead stays circular during jump

The jump deform on the spine bone (sx: 0.92, sy: 1.12 on rise, sx: 1.08, sy: 0.92 on apex/fall) was inherited by the head bone, making the head squish horizontally. Added a counter-deform on the head bone (1/0.92, 1/1.12 on rise, 1/1.08, 1/0.92 on apex/fall) so the head's inherited transform resolves back to (1, 1). Torso still gets the body squash/stretch for the "weight transfer" cue, but the head sprite keeps proper round proportions through the entire jump.

v0.25.196 Sprite layers are canonical default everywhere

polishStudio preview passes full sprite-layer set

renderCharStudio now passes eyeId + mouthId in lookCustom alongside skinIdx/hairId. Previously the studio fell through the internal 'default' resolver which worked but didn't preview alternate LX_EYES/LX_MOUTH picks until you hit Apply. Studio is now pixel-identical to the in-game render.

polishCanonical default IDs

CHAR_STUDIO.hairId default flipped from legacy 'anime' → 'flow'. Same render result (legacy ids still migrate via _migrateHairId) but the canonical sprite key is now the explicit default — no more "what does 'anime' mean" confusion when reading state.

polishSprite-first eye/mouth dispatch

Tightened _drawVectorHero's eye-renderer fallback. The procedural _EYE_RENDERERS map (sparkle/star/sleepy/dot) is no longer reachable from a custom lookCustom.eyeId — those legacy ids coerce to 'default' and pull the LX_EYES sprite. The procedural sparkle renderer remains as a single emergency fallback for cold-start frames before LX_EYES.default decodes (the v0.25.173 preloader normally gates the world reveal, so this path rarely runs).

featRender contract

Sprite layers (LX_HEAD / LX_HAIR / LX_EYES / LX_MOUTH) are now the canonical default render path for the hero in every visible context: in-world drawPlayer, idle bake cache, Q-key Character Studio preview, and any _drawVectorHero callsite that supplies its own _ctx. Procedural drawing remains only as a pre-decode safety net.

polishPer-eye reposition based on master head webp

Previous attempts uniformly shifted the whole eye sprite — close but not exact, since the user-supplied sprite had eyes spaced ~115 px apart while the head's sockets are ~120 px apart. Switched to per-eye reposition: extracted left + right eye blobs (with surrounding eyebrow/lash padding) from the user's original sprite, then placed each eye's centroid at the exact socket coordinate read from Sprites/character/head/Head master copy.webp — left socket (430, 469), right socket (550, 463), in the 800×800 reference frame. v0.25.194 Per-class attack animations + eye realignment

featWarrior — wide 2-handed slash

New attack_warrior anim. Both arms grip the hilt and swing together through a ~30%-wider arc than the generic attack: windup raises the sword overhead-back to −2.40 rad, strike sweeps across the body to +1.90 rad, recovery returns to guard. Mirror-coupled armR/armL rotations keep both hands locked on the handle. Bigger spine twist + head commit + heavier forward lurch in the bob channel for a real "weight transfer" feel.

featMage — raise staff at the sky

New attack_mage anim. Front arm sweeps from neutral up to ~vertical (−1.80 rad), holds for the channel/cast moment with a small magical tremor, then lowers back. Body leans back and head tilts up to "look at" the staff tip. Off-hand drifts low as a counterweight. The orb tip on the v0.25.191 staff geometry naturally points skyward at the apex of the raise.

polishArcher — bow stays realistic, no rotation while aiming

Tightened _heroVecArcherFrontArm: the bow stabilises in 0.10 t instead of 0.20 t, then locks dead-still through the entire draw + release window. Added a tiny recoil shudder (±0.06 rad) on the release frame instead of a sudden return. Back arm timing rebalanced so the longer steady window has a longer string-pull. Result: the bow looks held, not whipped.

polishEye sprite realigned to head's actual sockets

The v0.25.193 shift (+13 right, −34 up) was based on a wrong reading of the head's eye-socket position. The two ovals I detected at y≈210 in the 367×370 cropped head were upper-face contours, not eye sockets — the real sockets sit at y≈250 (matching the v0.25.189 eye sprite that already worked with this head). Restored the user-supplied sprite (undid the bad shift) and applied the correct nudge: −2 left, +9 down. Final alpha-bbox (399, 428, 582, 504) — pupils slot into the head's drawn sockets and eyebrows trace the upper curve.

polishDispatcher + time-norm updated

_heroVecAnimFor dispatches per-class: archer→attack_archer, warrior→attack_warrior, mage→attack_mage, all others→attack (rogue + default). _heroVecTimeNorm recognises all four attack-variant names so the shared timer drives them identically.

v0.25.192 New head base with eye sockets

featUpdated head sprite (eye sockets baked in)

User-supplied 800×800 head replaces Sprites/character/head/flow.webp. Same alpha bbox as before (245, 215, 612, 585) so cropped to 367×370 via the existing v0.25.188 workflow. polishTinted-head cache invalidation on hot-reload

The v0.25.191 _LX_TINTED_HEAD_CACHE bakes one variant per skin tone using the sprite at first-render time. When a new flow.webp hot-reloads (via cache bust or repo update), the cache would have stale entries baked from the OLD sprite. Extended the LX_HEAD.flow.onload handler to wipe both the v0.25.176 idle bake cache AND the v0.25.191 tinted-head cache. Now any future head swap takes effect on the next idle frame without manual intervention.

v0.25.191 Skin tone tints head + mage staff lower + archer bow attack

featSkin tone picker now tints the head sprite

The Q-key Skin Tone picker tinted procedural body parts (legs / arms / torso) but the v0.25.182 sprite-based head had its baked-in cream skin colour locked. New _lxGetTintedHead(skinIdx) bakes a per-tone variant via a 3-step composite pipeline:

  1. drawImage(headSprite) onto an offscreen canvas
  2. globalCompositeOperation = 'multiply' + fillRect with the SKIN.base colour
  3. globalCompositeOperation = 'destination-in' + drawImage(headSprite) to clip the multiply layer back to the sprite alpha

multiply preserves the sprite's tonal range (shadow stays darker than base) so the result reads as natural skin shading across all 8 tones. Cached forever — one ~30 KB canvas per skinIdx, ~240 KB total worst case. The head drawImage in drawBone('head', ...) now uses _lxGetTintedHead(skinIdx) || rawSprite.

polishMage staff held lower

The wizard staff was held with the glowing orb at hand-local y=-25, which translated to world y=-47 — right inside the head bbox. User feedback: "make the holding of the staff lower so that it doesn't block the head so much." Entire staff geometry shifted +14 in y: shaft y=-22..4 → y=-8..18, orb y=-25 → y=-11. Orb now sits below the chin (world y=-33 vs head bottom at world y=-38). Length and proportions unchanged.

featArcher attack: pull bowstring → release

Per user request: "for archer class the attacking animation should involve the character pulling the bow and releasing to shoot arrow." Previously the archer used the warrior swing animation. New class-specific attack_archer animation:

  • Windup (t=0..0.20): Both arms rise to forward-up. Front arm holds the bow steady at -1.15 rad; back arm matches at +1.25 rad.
  • Draw (t=0.20..0.55): Back arm rotates further back (+1.90 rad) — visibly pulling the string.
  • Release (t=0.55..0.62): Back arm snaps forward in 7% of the timeline — quick string release.
  • Recovery (t=0.62..1.0): Both arms ease back to neutral.

Spine + head leans are 1/3 the size of the warrior swing's body lurch (no big windup needed for an archer). Two new helpers _heroVecArcherFrontArm + _heroVecArcherBackArm; new attack_archer entries in HERO_VEC_ANIMS, HERO_VEC_DEFORM, HERO_VEC_BOB; _heroVecAnimFor dispatches archer to the new anim, _heroVecTimeNorm uses the same attack timer.

  • Procedural smirk path is skipped
  • Eye sprite drawn at (-58, -52, 108, 108) — same rect as the head sprite for canvas alignment

Two hair sprite formats now coexist:

  • Legacy ~500×410 — prince, spike. Older format with content filling the canvas; renders at the existing rect (-32, -25, 64, 54).

Dispatch on sprite.naturalWidth >= 700. New hair sprites should be authored at 800×800 head-aligned format going forward; the legacy branch can be removed once prince + spike are re-authored.

v0.25.188 New head base + aspect-ratio fix

featNew head base sprite (cropped + properly centred)

User dropped Head master copy.webp (800×800) into Sprites/character/head/. The head silhouette occupied only the right-half of the canvas with a large transparent margin on the left, which would have rendered the head off-centre on the player. Cropped to its alpha bounding box (245, 215, 612, 585) → final size 367×370, properly centred on the sprite canvas. Saved as flow.webp, overwriting the previous head base.

bugdrawImage now preserves sprite aspect ratio (no squish)

Previous code: drawImage(_headSprite, -24, -23, 48, 50) — hardcoded 48 wide × 50 tall. Source ratio 1:1.008 was being squished to 0.96 (about 4% horizontal compression). New head emphasised the chin curvature so the squish was newly visible. Replaced with proportional sizing:

const _headH = 50;
const _headW = _headH * (sprite.naturalWidth / sprite.naturalHeight);
const _headDx = -_headW / 2;     // centre on head bone
ctx.drawImage(_headSprite, _headDx, -23, _headW, _headH);

Future head swaps with any aspect ratio (taller, wider, off-square) will now render proportionally without manual coord tuning.

v0.25.186 Hair fitted to head frame

polishHair drawImage shifted down 9 px so all hairstyles sit on the head

User feedback: "the hairstyles all do not fit nicely into the head frame, shift it vertically down". The hair sprites (Flow / Spike / Prince) were floating above the head — their bottom edge sat at y=20 while the head's top is at y=-23 and the head's chin at y=27. Result: hair drew over the upper head but didn't reach the face area where the chin nub peeks through.

  • Hair top: y=-25 (2 px above the head top at y=-23)
  • Hair bottom: y=29 (2 px below the head chin at y=27)

The hair now wraps the head from crown to chin, with bangs hanging into the face area and the cream face peeking through the hair sprite's intentional transparent gap. Same coords for all three sprite-backed hairstyles since they share one drawImage call.

The v0.25.176 hero idle bake cache regenerates fresh on next page load, so the new positioning takes effect immediately on reload — no manual cache invalidation needed.

v0.25.183 4 eye styles + Q-key picker

featFour distinct chibi eye styles

The single chibi eye (gradient iris + dilated pupil + top-left catchlight) became one of four hot-swappable styles, all sharing the same (ctx, cx, irisGrad) signature so dispatch is a single map lookup:

  • Sparkle ✨ — the existing default. Gradient iris, dilated pupil, single big top-left white catchlight.

v0.25.182 Sprite-based head (Flow)

featUser-supplied chibi head PNG replaces the procedural silhouette + shading

Per user direction "Use exactly this for the head". Saved at Sprites/character/head/flow.webp (366×369). The procedural head pipeline that drew per-frame:

  1. Cream silhouette fill (HERO_VEC_PARTS.head path)
  2. Warm-brown shadow ellipse clipped to head
  3. Upper-right highlight ellipse clipped to head
  4. Bold black outline stroke
  5. Specular pip

...is now replaced with a single drawImage(LX_HEAD.flow, -24, -23, 48, 50). The sprite has the silhouette, base colour, soft brown side shadow, and bold outline all baked in — the canvas only renders the specular pip and the face features (eyebrow, eyes, mouth) on top.

featLX_HEAD registry + bake-cache invalidation

Mirrors the v0.25.178 LX_HAIR pattern: module-scope registry, async load, onload callback that wipes _LX_HERO_IDLE_BAKE_CACHE so the v0.25.176 idle bake doesn't lock in a vector-rendered first frame before the sprite decoded. Falls back to the procedural pipeline (kept inline) when the sprite is missing — rare since the v0.25.173 preloader blocks the world reveal until everything is hot.

perf~5 fewer canvas-state mutations per hero idle frame

The procedural head was fill + save + clip + 2× ellipse + fill + restore + save + stroke + restore = ~10 canvas-state ops. Replaced by 1 drawImage. Combined with the v0.25.176 idle bake-cache, the steady-state hero render path is now extremely cheap.

const _bossAttacking = m.patternState && m.patternState !== 'idle';
if (_bossAttacking && BOSS_ATTACK_SPRITES[m.type]) {
  _drawBossSprite(attackImg, m, sx, sy, true);
} else if (BOSS_SPRITES[m.type]) {
  _drawBossSprite(neutralImg, m, sx, sy, false);
}

Every boss already tags itself with a patternState like 'volley', 'beam', 'leap', etc. on entering an attack and clears back to 'idle' when the pattern finishes — so the attack pose stays up for the entire windup + release window. _drawBossSprite got a new _isAttack flag so it looks up the right bbox-bottom meta for floor anchoring (the attack poses have different bbox shapes than the neutral ones).

v0.25.180 Codex moved to Y — N is now solely interact

Per user request: N no longer falls through to the Codex when no NPC is in range. N is now solely the interact key:

  • Nearby chest → open it

Pressing N while an NPC dialog is open still closes the dialog. The Codex stays bound exclusively to Y (already there since v0.25.121). This eliminates the surprise of N opening the Codex when the player meant to interact with something that wasn't quite in range.

v0.25.179 Face features: wider, higher, more toward facing

polishEye spacing widened, face raised, facing bias bumped

Three coordinated tweaks to the chibi face per user feedback ("position the face features more horizontally side and shift it upwards a little" + "shift the eyes towards the facing side horizontally by 5 px"):

  • Eye spacing: ±6.5 → ±9.0 in head-local X. Eyes now push further toward the temples for that wide-eyed chibi look.
  • Vertical lift: every face element raised 3 px — eyebrow path, iris ellipse, pupil ellipse, catchlight, iris gradient stops, and the mouth curve. Net effect: the entire face block sits higher under the bangs of the new sprite hair (v0.25.178) instead of crowding the chin.
  • Facing bias FACE_DX: 2 → 7. Since the canvas is mirror-flipped when player.facing < 0, this constant always pushes features toward whichever side the hero is looking, giving a much more pronounced 3/4-view feel.

All coordinates re-tuned in lockstep so the iris gradient, eyebrow arc, and mouth curve all stay in their original geometric relationship to each other.

v0.25.178 Sprite-based hair (Flow)

featUser-supplied chibi hair PNG replaces the vector goo/path render

The user supplied a hand-drawn chibi anime hairstyle (black with glossy white sheen, chunky bangs over the forehead, side strands, side-cheek peek-through). Saved at Sprites/character/hair/flow.webp. The vector pipeline (Path2D back-wrap + cubic-bezier front cowlicks + sharp L-bang fangs from v0.25.164) now skipped entirely for the flow hairId — replaced with a single drawImage at the head bone:

// In drawBone('head', ...) after head fill, before eyes:
ctx.drawImage(LX_HAIR.flow, -32, -34, 64, 54);

Sprite native ratio is 508×427 (≈1.19w). Mapped to head-units 64w × 54h so it slightly overhangs the head bbox (head spans ~48 wide, top reaches y=-22). Centred so the bulk sits over the upper head + bangs hang to roughly chin level. Drawn AFTER the head fill (so the cream skin shows where the sprite has alpha — face peeks through naturally) and BEFORE the eyes/mouth (so face features render on top of any hair that overlaps).

featLX_HAIR registry + automatic bake-cache invalidation

New LX_HAIR registry next to LX_MOB_PROJ / LX_MOB_CAST. The onload callback on the hair image clears _LX_HERO_IDLE_BAKE_CACHE — without this, the first idle frame baked BEFORE the sprite decoded would render the vector hair and stay cached forever, so the sprite would never appear. Now the cache invalidates the moment the sprite is ready, the next idle frame re-bakes with the sprite, and stays sprite-cached forever after.

featSpike hair preserved + preloader manifest +1

The spike hairId still uses the v0.25.164 cluster-pair goo blob renderer — it has no entry in LX_HAIR, so the dispatch falls through to HAIR_GOO.front. Mixed mode: sprite for flow, blobs for spike. Preloader manifest grown 36 → 37 to include flow.webp.

v0.25.177 Monster attack-cast aura sprites

feat4 painterly cast-aura VFX sprites generated via ludo.ai

Per-element burst sprites that flash over the monster body for ~280 ms when they fire a projectile. Adds clear "this monster just attacked you" feedback without changing combat timing. Saved at Sprites/projectiles/cast/:

  • mdark — swirling violet shadow burst with magenta core (for archon-type casters)
  • msplinter — pale-blue crystalline starburst (for ice / treant / horny shooters)
  • mspore — golden-yellow pollen explosion (for mushroom / cookie shooters)
  • mtoxic — acid-green bubbling ooze burst (for frog / venom shooters)

featRender pipeline: stamp + fade overlay

New LX_MOB_CAST registry next to LX_MOB_PROJ. fireMonsterProjectile stamps m._castFlashT = game.time + m._castFlashSkill on the monster the moment the projectile is pushed into game.projectiles. drawMonster reads those fields after the body sprite renders and overlays the matching aura with:

  • Alpha fade — (1 - t) * 0.85 where t = elapsed / 280 ms
  • Growth scale — 0.6 → 1.1 over the same window so it pops outward
  • Composite — 'lighter' additive blend so the aura layers brightly over both light and dark monsters
  • Auto-cleared after expiry so subsequent frames skip the elapsed-time check

Layered before the HP bar so the aura sits over the monster body but doesn't obscure HP / name labels.

polishPreloader manifest +4

The 4 cast sprites added to REQUIRED in _wireLoadingScreen, bringing the total blocking-load manifest from 32 → 36. Hard fallback timeout (6 s) unchanged — the aura sprites are tiny (~180-360 KB each) and decode quickly.

v0.25.176 Bake-cache hero idle frame

perfIdle player renders via 1 drawImage instead of full Path2D pipeline

_drawVectorHero ran a full skeletal walk + Path2D fills + cel-shading + face elements + hair-goo pipeline EVERY FRAME. For an idle player, the rendered pixels are nearly identical between frames — only a sub-pixel sin-wave bob on head + spine.

New _LX_HERO_IDLE_BAKE_CACHE bakes one idle frame at animTime=0.5 (bob midpoint) per unique (cls, skinIdx, hairId) tuple into a 100×100 offscreen canvas. The new wrapper _drawVectorHeroCached(sx, sy):

  1. If _heroVecAnimFor() returns anything other than 'idle' (walk / attack / jump) → falls through to live _drawVectorHero
  2. If MSX sprite is active → falls through
  3. Otherwise → cache-hit drawImage + facing-flip mirror around player centre

Cache invalidates implicitly: skin / hair / class swap creates a new tuple key → one-time re-bake on the next idle frame, then steady-state hits forever.

featopts.forcedFacing now honoured by entry transform

The function's entry-transform was reading player.facing directly. The Character Studio (v0.25.93) and the new bake helper both pass forcedFacing: 1 — that flag now actually controls the scale-flip. Net: cleaner studio preview + stable bake regardless of which way the live player is facing.

perfQuantified savings on a stationary boss frame

Boss arena, player standing still while monitoring HP, vector hero active:

  • Before: per-frame call into _drawVectorHero → 6 bone walks → ~24 Path2D fills + strokes + 2 hair-goo bake-cache lookups + 8 face elements + cel-shading shifts. Roughly 60+ canvas operations.
  • After: 1 drawImage(cachedCanvas, dx, dy). ~98% reduction in canvas-operation count for the hero on idle frames.

Combined with v0.25.160 (hair-goo bake), v0.25.171 (impact-burst gating), v0.25.174 (mob-projectile sprite swap), and v0.25.175 (backdrop-filter mobile drop) the mobile idle-hover frame budget should now be comfortable headroom on most phones.

v0.25.175 Drop backdrop-filter: blur on mobile

perf4 mobile-expensive blur'd surfaces stripped on touch devices

backdrop-filter: blur(...) forces the browser to re-blur the underlying canvas every frame for that element's bounding box — expensive on mobile GPUs even when the player isn't interacting with the element. Each of the four UI surfaces below was blurring the live game canvas behind it 60 times a second:

  • #skill-bar (v0.25.167 dock surface)
  • #dialog (v0.25.168 NPC dialog card)
  • .modal (v0.25.168 modal panel)
  • #char-studio-overlay (v0.25.93 Q-key character studio)

Added a single @media (pointer: coarse), (max-width: 900px) override block that sets backdrop-filter: none !important on all four. Desktop hover-pointer devices keep the blur (it's free on hardware GPUs there). Same reasoning as the long-standing rule on .mc-btn from mobile-controls v5 — we never used backdrop blur on the touch buttons for exactly this reason.

v0.25.174 Monster projectiles: vanilla path now uses painterly sprites

perf+feat4 monster projectile archetypes wired into the default vanilla renderer

The painterly mob-projectile sprites generated in v0.25.148 (mdark, msplinter, mspore, mtoxic) were only being used in the Phaser opt-in path (?phaser=1). Default vanilla play was still drawing 4-7 procedural arc / fill stacks per mob projectile per frame — expensive on AoE-heavy maps where 30+ mob projectiles can be on screen.

New LX_MOB_PROJ image registry (parallel to LX_VFX / LX_WORLD) loads the four webps eagerly. drawProjectiles now prefers a single drawImage per mob projectile when the asset has decoded, with the original procedural draw kept inline as a first-frame fallback. The splinter shard rotates to track velocity (it has a clear pointed tip); the other three render axis-aligned.

Per-projectile cost on the vanilla path:

  • mspore — was 3 arc + fill calls + 3 fillStyle changes → 1 drawImage
  • mdark — was 3 arc + fill calls + 3 fillStyle changes → 1 drawImage
  • msplinter — was 4 fillRect + 1 polygon path + rotate → 1 rotated drawImage
  • mtoxic — was 3 arc calls (compound path) + 4 fillStyle changes → 1 drawImage

Worst case (30 mob projectiles in flight): ~120 fewer canvas-state mutations per frame on mobile. Sprite preload is already in the v0.25.173 manifest, so the painterly path is hot from frame one.

v0.25.173 Sprite preloader: wait for everything

featAll critical sprites now block the loading reveal

Per user feedback: "ensure all sprites loaded before running the game". The v0.25.114 fast-boot path only gated on 4 critical sprites, then prefetched the rest in the background — so players saw flat-coloured fallbacks pop into proper sprites a beat or two after spawn.

The REQUIRED manifest in _wireLoadingScreen grew from 4 entries to 32 — every runtime asset the first minute of play touches:

  • 10 hero animation sprites (idle, walk, jump, attack, hit, death, warrior swing, rogue stab, mage cast, archer shot)
  • 3 MSX chibi character skins (default, warrior, mage)
  • 6 starting-town NPCs (Elspeth, Brok, Amnesiac, Sage Mira, Old Arlen, Caravan Yara)
  • 10 VFX sprites (fireball, ice_spike, magic_bolt, meteor, slash, portal, death, level_up, frost_beam, gravity_well)
  • 4 monster projectile sprites (mdark, msplinter, mspore, mtoxic)
  • 1 world prop (portal.webp)

polishHard-fallback timeout 1.2 s → 6 s

The fast-boot timeout was 1.2 s — intended to reveal the world even if a single sprite 404s. With 32 sprites blocking, that's too aggressive. Bumped to 6 s. If anything genuinely fails, the per-sprite if (ready) guards in the renderers (e.g. _lxVfxReady, _lxWorldReady) still draw procedural fallbacks so a missing asset never crashes the screen.

Progress bar still increments per asset so the loading time is visible. Background prefetch loop removed (no longer needed — everything is in REQUIRED now).

v0.25.172 Painterly portal sprite

featMap portals replaced with a hand-painted ludo.ai sprite

Generated a runestone-framed portal via ludo.ai — vertical oval with gold filigree trim, embossed mystic runes around the edge, swirling violet-cyan vortex with star particles being pulled inward. Committed at Sprites/world/portal.webp.

perfProcedural portal renderer simplified ~60%

The old drawPortals body was a 117-line procedural canvas stack: outer halo radial gradient, translucent stone frame ellipse with destination-out cutout, soft shadow wedge, magical swirl interior with multiple alpha-blended ellipses, light rays, sparkle particles, and the label. Replaced with a single drawImage of the painterly sprite + the gentle bob + a soft halo + 4 drifting sparkles (gated by _perfLowFx()). Net diff: −117 / +73 lines in the function body. Loads via the new LX_WORLD sprite registry; falls back to a tinted ellipse for the first ~50 ms while the webp decodes so the portal is never invisible.

v0.25.171 Attack-monster lag fix

perfFrame-coalesce hit audio

AoE skills that strike many monsters in one frame were calling audio.play('hit') once per monster. Each call spawns a fresh oscillator with no internal debounce — so a 10-mob AoE fired 10 overlapping hit sounds (audio clips, expensive on mobile, sounds like noise rather than impact). Added a game._lastHitSoundFrame guard inside hitMonster: only the first hit per frame plays audio, with a same-frame "upgrade" rule so a regular-then-crit chain still hears the crit cue.

perfImpact-burst particle count gated by _perfLowFx()

Each on-hit was pushing 8 particles for normal / 14 for crit. AoE × N mobs blew past MAX_PARTICLES and dragged frame time on mobile. Now gated — on low-FX (mobile / slow hardware after the v0.25.160 _perfTick wire-up flips it on), the burst drops to 3 for normal / 5 for crit. Sparkle still reads, but doesn't dominate the budget. Desktop high-FX visuals untouched.

perfQuantified savings on a busy AoE frame

Example: Warrior rampage spinning AoE hits 8 mobs over one tick.

  • Before: 8 × audio.play('hit') = 8 oscillator allocations + 8 × 8 = 64 particles + the per-hit damage numbers / shake / hit-stop (already coalesced).
  • After: 1 × audio.play('hit') + 8 × 3 = 24 particles on low-FX (vs 64 before, ~62% cut).

v0.25.170 Boon rate harder (~1 per 5 min)

balanceBoon drops cut ~4x to target ~1 per 5 min of play

Per user feedback: "make it harder to obtain boons, usually 1 boon in 5 minutes." The drop chances and the mini-boss guarantee were both tightened:

  • Regular monster orb chance: 0.02 → 0.005 (~75% cut)
  • Elite (tier 1) monster orb chance: 0.12 → 0.03 (~75% cut)
  • Mini-boss "guaranteed epic orb" → 35% chance with a fresh rarity roll (rare / epic / legendary). Mini-bosses respawn every 60-90 s, so this alone was previously yielding 3-5 boons per 5 min.
  • Boss kills (tier 2) untouched — they still trigger showPowerupChoice() + drop loot. Bosses are one-shot events per map, not a rate concern.

Boons should now feel like a real reward when they drop instead of routine.

v0.25.169 All jobs −25% cooldown

balanceGlobal cooldown reduction across every class + job

New JOB_CD_MUL = 0.75 constant in the balance-knob block (next to PLAYER_ATK_MUL, GLOBAL_SKILL_DMG_MUL, etc). Applied at the two cooldown-consumption sites:

  • castSkill() — multiplied into the existing cdMul chain so it stacks with the mage 0.70x, archer Quick-Draw, and WIS-driven CDR.
  • Basic-attack hold-repeat in updatePlayer — player.attackCooldown = found.def.cd * JOB_CD_MUL.

Net effect: every job's skill cooldowns + basic-attack repeat rate are 25% faster. Single tuning knob — flip to 1.0 to revert. Doesn't touch the SKILLS dict so the canonical "design intent" cd values stay readable.

polishHover + active feedback + tighter typography

v0.25.166 Mobile dev button + D-pad lock-down

featOne-tap mobile developer-mode button

Added a discreet wrench (🛠) button in the top-right corner of the mobile HUD — just below the existing hide-controls toggle. One tap opens the dev console (level setter, class chain, mobile-unlock button, teleport, etc). The long-press on the version tag from v0.25.161 still works as a fallback, but the button is more discoverable. Hidden on desktop via the surrounding mobile @media query. pointerup handler with synthetic-click suppression so iOS Safari doesn't double-fire.

bugD-pad arrows: NOT normal selectable elements anymore

User reported the Up direction button getting accidentally highlighted. Even after v0.25.165's tap-suppress bundle on the dpad container, the 4 arrow buttons inside were still bare <button> elements that browsers happily focus / select / drag.

Locked them down: pointer-events: none promoted to !important in the CSS so the parent .mc-btn rule's auto override can't win, plus the buttons get explicit cursor: default and a re-asserted user-select / touch-callout / tap-highlight bundle. Belt-and-suspenders on the DOM: each arrow now ships with tabindex="-1" (out of keyboard tab order), draggable="false" (no long-press drag), and aria-hidden="true" (the parent dpad container handles accessibility — the visual buttons are decoration). All four arrows + the dev button itself get the same lockdown.

v0.25.165 D-pad accidental highlight fix

bugKill OS-level touch highlights on mobile D-pad + action buttons

Mobile players reported the direction-pad arrows getting "highlighted" accidentally during play. The cause: iOS / Android's default touch behaviours were leaking through the existing button styles — the gray-blue tap flash, the long-press text-selection rectangle, and the iOS context-menu callout were all firing on the D-pad. When the user dragged between arrows the highlight would stick because the underlying touch was still active.

Applied the standard mobile-touch-suppress bundle to .mobile-deck .mc-btn, .mobile-ctrl .mc-btn, AND the .mobile-deck .mc-dpad container (which is the actual touch target — the 4 arrow buttons inside have pointer-events:none):

  • -webkit-tap-highlight-color: transparent — kills the tap flash
  • -webkit-touch-callout: none — suppresses the iOS long-press menu
  • -webkit-user-select / user-select: none — no text-selection rectangle when drag-tracking
  • outline: none on both :focus and :focus-visible — some Android browsers leave the button in :focus state until another tap elsewhere, which made the highlight feel sticky
  • -webkit-user-drag: none — prevents the button from being draggable on long-press

Used !important throughout so they win against the existing !important visual-style rules above.

v0.25.164 Hair V2 — sharper bangs + cone spikes

featFlow V2: sharp bangs, sweeping cowlicks (Path2D)

The flow silhouette gets a sharper edge: bezier curves for the cowlick bumps + crisp L "snap-back" returns between each lobe so the bangs read as distinct angular fangs instead of soft ripples. Three top cowlicks (left, centre tall, right) and three bang sections (right tip, centre short, left long sweep). Back path also revised with two sharp returns to read as cleanly tapered nape strands instead of a smooth blob.

featSpike V2: cluster-pair directional cones (Goo Blob)

New trick: each spike is a cluster pair — one big base blob + one tiny tip blob a few units away. The SVG goo filter merges the pair into a smoothly tapered cone, no Bezier control points needed. 5 cone clusters in front (top-centre, top-left, top-right, side-left, side-right) plus 3 bang clusters and a core mass. Back: 3 base blobs + 2 tail cone clusters. Total 7 back blobs + 16 front blobs (was 5 + 11), and the silhouette now reads as a proper shounen spike halo.

v0.25.163 Pupil + catchlight + limb tuning

polishPupil dilated further (2.5×3.5 → 3.2×4.5)

The dilated pupil now fills ~70% of the iris area, pushing the chibi gaze deeper into "owo" anime territory. Iris stays at 4.5×5.2; the bigger pupil leaves only a thin gradient ring of iris visible around the edge.

polishSecondary catchlight removed

Dropped the small r=0.8 bottom-right reflection that v0.25.162 brought back. Only the primary massive top-left catchlight (r=1.8) remains — cleaner read, more focused gleam.

polishLimbs slightly shorter (tip y=18 → y=15, ~17% reduction)

The unified limb Path2D's tip pulls in from y=18 to y=15. Rig follows: legL/legR/spine y move from -18 to -15 so feet still touch the ground; handR moves from y=18 to y=15 so weapon overlays anchor at the new arm tip. Arm + head bones stay in spine-local coords so they ride along automatically. Net effect: chibi proportions read more squat / cute, character is ~3 units shorter overall, hands sit slightly higher on the body.

v0.25.162 Coordinated character vector overhaul

featFresh user-supplied parts spec — symmetric head + top-anchored torso + unified limb

Three new HERO_VEC_PARTS shapes shipped together:

  • Head — symmetric soft chibi, wider at the top, soft rounded chin. Width 48, height 46.
  • Torso — pear shape, narrow shoulders to wider hips. Origin at the TOP (neck) for clean rotation pivots. Height 28.
  • Limb — single teardrop shape used for BOTH arms and legs. Origin at the top joint. Height 18.

The legacy arm + leg Path2D pair are gone — both routes now reference the unified limb. The legacy hair Path2D from HERO_VEC_PARTS (unused since the v0.25.155 split) is also gone.

featRig retuned + torso translate to honor the new top-anchored convention

The 18-tall limb means leg bones move from y=-10 → y=-18 so feet still land at y=0. Spine moves to the new hip line at y=-18; arm bones move to x=±12, y=-22 (deeper shoulders for the wider torso); head bone moves to y=-50 for the bigger silhouette; handR updates to y=18 so weapon overlays anchor at the new arm tip. The torso's top-anchored origin requires a local ctx.translate(0, -28) inside the spine bone draw so the torso bottom lands at the hip line; chest accents shift +8 in y to compensate for the spine bone moving up.

featTwo hairstyles only: Flow + Spike (Wave + Crop retired)

Replaced HERO_VEC_HAIR_GOO with the new spec. Flow ✨ is a Path2D-mode style with a back nape sweep + front cowlick + asymmetrical bangs. Spike ⚡ is the goo-blob mode with 5 back blobs + 11 front spikes/bangs. Wave + Crop are gone; legacy save IDs all migrate to flow via the updated HERO_VEC_HAIR_LEGACY_MAP.

featNew eye anatomy — heavier eyelash, bigger iris/pupil, double catchlight

_drawChibiEye rebuilt to user spec: signature is (ctx, cx, irisGrad) for explicit context passing. Eyelash thickened to 3.5 px (was 2.4) and lowered so it rests on the iris top instead of floating above. Iris ellipse 4.5×5.2 (was 3.4×4.2) for a bigger, deeper anime gaze. Pupil dilated to 2.5×3.5. Two catchlights are back: a primary r=1.8 top-left + a tiny secondary r=0.8 bottom-right reflection (Catchlight B from v0.25.156 restored).

cleanupEars removed + _vecSize scaled 0.9 → 0.62

The new symmetric chibi head doesn't need ear bumps — deleted the 4 ear-related fill+stroke lines from the head bone draw. The new spec is ~43% taller overall (limb 18 vs 12, torso 28 vs 20), so the renderer's _vecSize scale drops from 0.9 to 0.62 to keep the on-screen character footprint roughly equivalent. The player.h hitbox still matches the visible silhouette and feet still touch the floor.

v0.25.161 Mobile dev unlock

featLong-press the version tag to open dev console (mobile entry point)

The desktop dev console opens via 1+2+3 held together — impossible without a keyboard. Added a 700 ms long-press handler on the top-right #version-tag. Triggers navigator.vibrate(30) for haptic feedback when the threshold is crossed so the player feels the unlock fire.

feat"🎁 Lv 50 + ALL SKILLS" one-tap setup button

New top section in the dev console: a single big purple button labelled Lv 50 + ALL SKILLS. One tap runs devMobileUnlock, which:

  • Auto-picks Warrior class if none chosen yet (so the unlock works on a fresh save).
  • Auto-picks the first available job + master in the class chain.
  • Jumps to level = 50 via the existing devSetLevel path (HP / MP / SP all bump correctly).
  • Walks the class's SKILL_TREE tier-by-tier and unlocks every node, granting the SP cost back each loop so prereqs land first and the apply hooks all fire.
  • Adds 10 leftover skill points + 50 000 Lumens + full HP / MP refill so the kit is immediately playable.

Idempotent — safe to tap repeatedly. Toast + dev log line confirm the unlock fired.

v0.25.160 Mobile perf debug

bugWire _perfTick into the game loop (CRITICAL fix)

The adaptive-perf monitor _perfTick(dt, time) has existed since v0.25.86 to flip LX_PERF.lowFx on when frame time spikes past 28 ms — but the call site was never added to the main loop. Result: LX_PERF.lowFx stayed false forever, so every _perfLowFx()-gated optimisation (ambient particle cap from v0.25.147, projectile-trail frustum-cull, low-FX hair fallback below) was dead code on mobile. Now wired in at the top of loop(); mobile / slow hardware adapts in <1 second once frame time spikes.

perfGoo-filter hair: cache the bake (3 filtered passes → 1 plain drawImage)

The v0.25.157 SVG goo hair did three filtered drawImage calls per frame per character (outline + colour + cel highlight, each routed through ctx.filter = 'url(#goo)'). On mobile where SVG filter is software-rendered, that was the single biggest per-frame cost. The blob coordinates don't change between frames, so I moved the renderer to bake the full 3-pass composite into a cached offscreen canvas keyed by (group, hairColor, hairHi, lowFx) at module scope. Steady-state per-frame cost: 1 plain drawImage. Cache invalidates only when the player changes hair pick or class — at most ~8 entries ever exist.

perfSkip cel-highlight pass on low-FX

The third goo pass (the bright halo across the upper third of the hair silhouette) is now skipped when _perfLowFx() is true. Saves the bake cost on mobile entirely; the hair still has the dark outline + colour fill so it reads correctly, just without the cel highlight band.

perfSkip additive glow pass in drawParticles on low-FX

drawParticles ran a 'lighter'-composite glow halo pass for every bright particle, then a crisp core pass. The glow pass is the GPU-expensive one. Now gated behind !_perfLowFx(); mobile gets only the crisp-core pass (particles still visible, just without the soft halo). Combat-heavy moments with 80+ particles benefit most.

v0.25.159 Eyebrow raised

polishEyebrow lifted 2.5 px above the iris

The heavy upper-lid arc (the "eyebrow" of the chibi face) was sitting low — endpoints at y = 7.8 grazed the top of the iris. Raised the whole arc 2.5 px upward: endpoints now y = 5.3, peak y = 2.1. The brow now sits clearly above the iris and reads as an actual eyebrow rather than a fused upper-lid. Cleaner expression, more lift / personality on the face.

v0.25.158 Figma reference hair as new default

feat"Flow" hair re-traced from a Figma design reference (Path2D mode)

User supplied a .fig file as the design source. The Figma fig-kiwi binary is not directly readable, but the embedded thumbnail PNG showed a clear silhouette: an asymmetric anime hairstyle with 4 sharp upward spikes on the crown (the third one near centre is the tallest, peaking at y = -40), smooth curving sides that wrap behind the head, and 3 sharp downward bang fangs + 1 side-strand fang at the bottom. The PNG is committed at Sprites/character/refs/figma_hair_design.png as the design source-of-truth.

The defining feature of this design is the SHARP tips — the SVG goo filter would round them off, so this style switches back to a Path2D rendering. The registry entry now carries { path: Path2D } instead of { blobs: [...] }. A new dispatch helper _drawHairGroup picks the right renderer based on entry shape: blobs → goo, path → _drawHairPath. The other three styles (Spike / Wave / Crop) keep their goo-blob clusters; mixing modes is fine.

feat_drawHairPath renderer with cel-halo gradient + thick outline

Mirrors the goo highlight pass aesthetic but in a single fill: vertical linearGradient with stop pattern HAIR_SHD → HAIR_HI → C.hair → HAIR_SHD (dark roots → bright cel band → base color → dark tips), then a 2.5 px rgba(0,0,0,0.85) stroke with lineJoin="round" for a crisp cel-art outline. The path is split into back (the U-wrap that draws behind the head) and front (the spiky top + bangs that draw in front), preserving the layered z-order.

v0.25.157 Hair → SVG Gooey-Filter blob technique

featHair rebuilt as overlapping circle/ellipse blobs merged via SVG goo filter

Replaced the cubic-bezier Path2D hair pipeline with the SVG metaballs / "gooey filter" technique. Each hairstyle is now a cluster of 15-22 overlapping <circle> and <ellipse> blobs (radii 6-18 in head-space units) split into back (drawn before the head silhouette) and front-bangs (drawn after head shading). At render time the blobs are painted to a 96×96 offscreen canvas with flat fills, then drawn back to the main canvas with ctx.filter = 'url(#goo)' — the in-document <filter id="goo"> applies a Gaussian blur (stdDeviation=8) → steep alpha-threshold colour matrix (0 0 0 18 -7) → atop-composite, merging the blobs into one smooth organic silhouette. No bezier control points to calculate.

featThree-pass rendering: outline → fill → cel highlight

The _drawHairGoo helper makes three offscreen-and-goo passes per group:

  1. Outline pass — same blobs with radii expanded by +1.6 px, filled #1a0818. After goo, the merged silhouette is slightly larger than the colored silhouette so a thin black ring peeks out around the edge — cel-art outline without any stroke ops.
  2. Color pass — blobs at normal radii, filled with the class hair color. Goo merges them into the smooth main silhouette.
  3. Cel-highlight pass — blobs scaled to 55% radii and offset upward 4 px, filled with HAIR_HI at globalAlpha = 0.55. Goo merges these into a soft halo across the upper third of the silhouette so the hair still reads as cel-shaded volume, not a flat blob.

cleanupRemoved HERO_VEC_HAIR_LAYERED + _hairCelGrad + _drawHairLockGroup

The old 4-lock cubic-bezier registry, vertical cel-halo gradient builder, and per-lock fill-and-stroke helper from v0.25.155 are all gone (~50 fewer lines in the hot draw path). New helpers _drawBlobsOnCanvas + _drawHairGoo replace them, sharing one cached 96×96 offscreen canvas across the back + front passes.

v0.25.156 Eye polish

polishCatchlight B removed — single white pip per eye

The strict chibi face anatomy from v0.25.154 used two catchlights per eye (large pip top-right + small pip mid-left). Per user request, the small mid-left pip is gone — just the large white circle stays at (cx + 0.9, 9.1) with r=0.95. Reads cleaner at small scales and matches typical anime convention of one dominant gleam.

v0.25.155 Hair simplified to 4-lock template + 4 new styles

feat4 brand-new hairstyles built from a unified 4-lock cubic-bezier template

The 7-lock "flow" silhouette from v0.25.154 was over-engineered for a chibi head. Simplified the layered template to 1 back lock + 3 front locks = 4 cubic-bezier paths total, then used that template to generate four chibi-friendly hairstyles. Every style follows the same z-order (back lock → head shading → 3 front locks) and the same fill (cel-halo gradient + 2.5 px black stroke):

  • Flow ✨ — soft anime swept hair (default). Full nape mass + left/centre/right crown sweep with chunky middle bang.
  • Spike ⚡ — angular shounen pointed hair. Tight nape + three tall pointed crown spikes (centre is tallest at y = -34). Still pure cubic-bezier, no L-zigzag fringe.
  • Wave 🌊 — flowing curly hair. Long back lock with bottom curl + long wavy left/right side strands falling past the chin + flowing centre wave bang.
  • Crop ✂️ — short cropped hair. Tight close-to-skull nape + three short tucked bangs sitting just above the eyes.

cleanupLegacy single-Path2D hair pipeline + _useLayeredHair branch deleted

The old HERO_VEC_HAIR registry (anime / short / spike / bowl / bun / pigtails as single Path2D shapes) is gone. _drawVectorHero no longer carries the HAIR_PATH variable, the _useLayeredHair flag, or the legacy else branch with its three-pass fill + clip + stroke + highlight strokes. Net: ~30 fewer lines in the hot draw path, every hair style takes the same code route, and the renderer is simpler to reason about.

featSave migration: legacy hairId → closest new style

Existing saves with player.lookCustom.hairId values from the deleted styles get auto-remapped via _migrateHairId: anime/bun → flow; short/bowl → crop; pigtails → wave; spike → spike. Unknown ids fall back to flow. No save corruption, no missing-style fallback render.

v0.25.154 Layered hair + strict chibi face

feat"Flow ✨" hair — strict SVG-spec layered cubic-bezier renderer

New top-of-list hair style Flow ✨ follows a strict SVG rendering spec: the silhouette is split into back-hair (drawn behind the head — nape mass + tail wisp, 2 locks) and front-hair-bangs (drawn after head shading — left/centre/right crown chunks + 4 chunky overlapping bang locks, 5 locks). All seven locks use cubic Bezier (C) commands only — no polygons, no jagged L-zigzag fringe. They overlap intentionally to read as 3D volume. Fill is a shared cel-halo linearGradient (dark roots → sharp cel-band transition → bright halo middle → back to base → dark tips), mimicking the SVG <linearGradient> with stop offsets at 0.34→0.36 and 0.55→0.57. Outline is a thick rgba(0,0,0,0.85) stroke at 2.5 px with rounded line joins, matching the strict stroke-linejoin="round" requirement. Pick it from Q → Hair → Flow.

featStrict chibi face anatomy — 5-element eyes + zero nose + minimal smirk

Replaced the old simple oval-pupil eyes + nose-hint + smile with a chibi/anime-style spec face. Each eye is now a stack of 5 layered z-elements drawn in this exact order:

  1. Heavy upper eyelash line — a thick black quadratic-curve path stroked at 2.4 px with round caps.
  2. Iris ellipse — large, filled with a vertical linearGradient running deep navy at top → mid blue → bright cyan-blue at bottom (anime cel-shaded depth).
  3. Pupil — solid dark ellipse centred slightly off the iris.
  4. Catchlight A — pure white #ffffff circle, larger size, top-right of the pupil.
  5. Catchlight B — pure white smaller circle, mid-left of the pupil.

Eyes spaced wide at x = ±6.5 + FACE_DX (was ±5) to enforce the chibi look. Both centred at y = 10.4 — squarely in the bottom 40% of the head bbox (head spans y ∈ [-21, 22]; bottom 40% starts at y ≈ 4.6). Zero nose: the previous SKIN.deep nose-hint stroke is removed entirely — not drawn, not coded. Minimal mouth: a single shallow quadratic curve at y = 16, just 3.2 px wide, reading as a tiny confident smirk. The whole face block is wrapped in a structural comment marking it as the face-elements group.

v0.25.153 Strip always-on screen FX

perfDepth fog + sky-life cloud/bird overlays gated off by default

Two atmospheric passes were running on every outdoor / bitmap-bg frame regardless of the _ART_FX_ENABLED flag — drawWorldArtOverlay step 1 (mid-ground depth-fog gradient painted over the bottom 62% of the screen) and drawSkyLifeOverlay (12 parallax cloud wisp gradients + 7 flapping birds drawn with bezier curves and shifting alpha each frame). User reported them as ugly + laggy. Both moved behind _ART_FX_ENABLED: drawWorldArtOverlay early-returns when the flag is off, and the bitmap-background path skips drawSkyLifeOverlay entirely. Default is now a clean painted scene with zero per-frame overlay cost.

bugStale localStorage opt-in dropped

Previously _ART_FX_MODE would read localStorage.getItem('levelx_art_fx') as a fallback after URL param parsing — meaning anyone who toggled the FX on months ago via the (long-removed) studio toggle would still get the heavy pass on every page load forever. The localStorage read is gone; URL param is now the only opt-in path: ?artfx=soft, ?artfx=vivid, or ?artfx=noir to enable, omit / ?artfx=0 to keep the clean default.

docsREADME updated

The README claim that "outdoor maps now include a built-in art pass" + "bitmap backgrounds also get an animated sky-life layer" was misleading post-this-fix — both are now opt-in. Replaced with a single power-user paragraph noting that ?artfx=soft|vivid|noir is the trigger and the plain bitmap art reads cleaner without it.

v0.25.152 MapleStory chibi sprite skins

feat3 hand-painted MapleStory-style chibi hero sprites + Q-hotkey picker

Generated three sophisticated 1:2 head-to-body chibi sprites via ludo.ai matching the classic Korean side-scrolling MMO aesthetic — soft cel-shading, massive expressive anime eyes, clean crisp line art, gentle two-tone gradients, white background, 3/4 isometric facing right. Files live at Sprites/character/hero/msx_*.webp:

  • Adventurer — brown chunky-spike hair, white tee, indigo jeans, brown sneakers. The default chibi boy.
  • Warrior — bronze hair w/ red headband, polished steel breastplate, golden filigree, glowing crystal-blue broadsword, golden lion shield, crimson cape.
  • Mage — flowing silver-platinum hair, midnight-blue moon-and-star wizard hat, indigo constellation robe, glowing turquoise staff, leather grimoire, magical aura.

feat"Fix pixels to head" anchor pipeline (head-pin alignment)

Each sprite gets its alpha channel scanned on load to compute four anchors: bbox (minX/minY/maxX/maxY), centroid X (alpha-weighted mass centre), and the topmost-opaque pixel Y (the "head pin"). At draw time the renderer scales the source bbox to fit player.h * 0.9 exactly and positions the sprite so the head pin lands at the player's bbox top — meaning the head stays at a fixed on-screen Y across all sprite swaps, while feet still align to the ground line. _drawMsxHero mirrors honour player.facing via centred X-flip and falls back to the vector hero if the sprite hasn't decoded yet, so first-frame loads never render blank.

featQ-hotkey Character Studio: Sprite Skin picker

Press Q to open the studio. New section Sprite Skin sits below Hair, with four pickers: Vector (default — falls through to the existing vector hero), Adventurer, Warrior, Mage. Selecting a sprite updates the live preview canvas immediately and writes player.lookCustom.msxId on Apply. Sprite skins override the skin/hair pickers (those still control the vector renderer when Sprite Skin = Vector). Persisted across saves via the existing PLAYER_SAVE_FIELDS.lookCustom entry.

v0.25.151 UI VFX sprite integration

feat4 painterly UI sprites wired into the live HUD

The v0.25.139 ludo-generated UI sprites were sitting unused on disk. Wired four of them in as decorative backdrops via CSS background-image, with the existing dynamic UI layered on top so nothing breaks:

  • Skill slot — Sprites/ui/skill_slot.png (painterly gold frame around a dark void) becomes the backdrop for every .skill-slot in the bottom-centre dock. The dark void in the middle keeps the skill icon readable; the conic-gradient cooldown sweep and the existing border-color state cues (cyan = ready, red = cost-too-high, desat = locked) still draw on top.
  • Modal panel — Sprites/ui/menu_panel.png stretched across .modal as the new gold-trimmed backdrop. The lore modal keeps its parchment-tan override.
  • NPC dialog — Sprites/ui/dialog_box.png replaces the purple dialog box with the painterly parchment scroll. Body text re-themed to dark brown so it reads against cream parchment instead of white-on-purple.
  • Dialog options buttons — Sprites/ui/button.png skins the response buttons inside #dialog .options; the old purple flat button is gone, replaced with the painterly gold button + drop-shadow text.

Skipped: hp_bar.png, mp_bar.png, exp_bar.png (frame and gem are baked into a single sprite, so they need a full bar redesign rather than a drop-in skin) and skill_slot_cooldown.png (the existing conic-gradient sweep already covers cooldown). Will revisit in a follow-up if you want.

v0.25.150 Head mirror + face bias + MapleStory hair

bugHead silhouette + shading mirrored to match reference orientation

v0.25.149's head ended up flipped relative to the user's reference image (shadow on the wrong side, chin nub on the wrong corner). Mirrored every X-coordinate in the head pipeline: HERO_VEC_PARTS.head now puts the cheek bulge on the left and the chin nub on the lower-right, the warm-brown shadow ellipse moves from x=+13 to x=-13 (back-of-head when facing right), the upper-light highlight + specular pip move from the upper-left to the upper-right (toward the facing direction).

featFace features biased toward facing direction (subtle 3/4-view feel)

Eyes, nose hint, and mouth now shift +2 px in canvas-X via a single FACE_DX constant. Because the canvas is mirror-flipped when player.facing < 0, that constant always pushes the face toward whichever direction the hero is looking — right-shift when facing right, left-shift when facing left. The pure front-on silhouette stays intact; this just nudges the features forward enough to read as a slight head-turn instead of dead-on.

feat'Anime' hair rebuilt MapleStory-style

The default anime hair Path2D went from a curved crown plus an angular zigzag bottom (L-line fringe) to a smooth flowing silhouette: rounded crown traced with quadratic beziers, one small upward tuft on top, and three chunky scalloped bang lobes across the forehead. The longer left-side bang reads as the "swept" side. Other hair styles (short / spike / bowl / bun / pigtails) untouched; pick them in the Character Studio (Q) if you prefer the older look.

v0.25.149 Vector head reshape

polishHead silhouette + shading rebuilt from user reference

The vector hero's head was a perfect r=20 circle with 3-tone cel-shading + a rim crescent + cheek blush + 2× gloss pips. Reshaped to match a user-supplied reference: HERO_VEC_PARTS.head is now an organic egg silhouette (~21h × 20w) traced with quadratic beziers, with a subtle right-cheek bulge and a gentle chin nub on the lower-left. Shading switched from 3-tone cel to a clean 2-tone soft pass — cream/ivory base, warm-brown right-side shadow via a clipped ellipse that fades toward centre, and a soft upper-left highlight. Rim crescent and cheek blush removed; a single specular pip remains. Outline also bumped to STROKE_W + 0.6 px on the head only so the bold black contour reads cleanly at small scales without thickening every other body part.

v0.25.148 VFX + projectile sprite refresh

feat6 painterly VFX/projectile sprites brought up to v0.25.138 standard

The leftover Apr 29 batch sat at much lower fidelity than the v0.25.138 / v0.25.139 painterly refresh pass. Regenerated all six via ludo.ai in matching Genshin/Hollow Knight hand-painted style: Sprites/vfx/frost_beam.webp (cyan crystalline burst with sparkles), Sprites/vfx/gravity_well.webp (violet vortex pulling stardust), and the four monster projectiles in Sprites/projectiles/ — mdark.webp (purple shadow orb with rim glow), msplinter.webp (faceted ice crystal shard), mspore.webp (golden dandelion-pollen puff), mtoxic.webp (bubbling acid-green ooze). Drop-in replacement — same filenames, same dimensions, no code changes. Loaded by LX_VFX at line 3954 and the _loadProjSprite registry around 3224.

v0.25.147 Performance

polishAmbient + projectile-trail low-FX gating

Merged a stashed perf pass from a Codex collaborator session that pre-dated v0.25.140's overlay-cache work. Three hot loops now respect the existing _perfLowFx() heuristic: updateAmbient caps total ambient particles at 45% of MAX_AMBIENT in low-FX, drops spawn chance to 35%, and trims overflow when the cap is hit; drawAmbient skips the additive lighter-blend halo passes around embers, fireflies, and wisps; emitProjectileTrails frustum-culls projectiles outside an 80 px screen-edge margin and only emits trails on every other frame in low-FX. Net result on heavy boss/cave maps: visible particle count drops >50% on phones without changing the high-FX desktop look.

cleanupRemoved orphan .png.png + duplicate pillar tiles

Deleted four unused Sprites/skills/<class>_fx.png.png double-extension files (~25 MB) and two duplicate backgrounds/tiles/pillar_*_b.webp tiles. Nothing in maple_game.html referenced them; only legacy prompt notes in Sprites/Prompts.txt mention the (correctly-named) .png form, which is preserved.

v0.25.146 Early map cleanup

polishRemoved early-map decor overlay

The extra early-zone decorative overlay has been removed from Emerald Thicket, Fungal Hollow, Sunset Coast, Slime Cave, and Elderwood Grove. Those maps keep their platform layout variants, but the added canopy/logs, mushrooms/spores, tide pools/palms, and elder trunk/rune foreground props no longer draw over the existing biome backgrounds.

v0.25.145 Vector attack swing

polishCommitted arm swing attacks

The vector hero attack pose now uses a full windup, strike, and follow-through instead of a small weapon-arm flick. The front arm sweeps through a much wider arc, the back arm counter-swings, the torso leans into the hit, quick attacks keep a short one-shot visual timer, and the slash trail is widened so the swing reads as actually reaching toward monsters.

v0.25.144 Vector hero cleanup

polishCleaner face, hair, and walk cycle

The vector hero now uses simpler black-and-white eyes, softer head shading, lighter face accents, and cleaner hair silhouettes across the Character Studio hair options. Walking was toned down with smaller arm and leg swings, reduced head bob, less body squash, and a slower cycle so the character feels calmer in motion.

v0.25.143 Early map variety

polishLess standard low-level zones

Early progression maps now roll named layout variants on load instead of relying only on generic platform jitter. Emerald Thicket, Fungal Hollow, Sunset Coast, and Elderwood Grove gain distinct set-piece routes such as canopy bridges, fallen-log runs, spore rings, tide pools, shell cliffs, elder ruins, and hanging groves.

v0.25.142 Vector hero animation polish

polishSharper hair, darker eyes, livelier motion

The vector hero rig now has a snappier weapon swing with anticipation, fast follow-through, and a wider motion trail; walking gets stronger arm/leg overlap plus head bob; jumping now poses differently on rise versus fall. Hair silhouettes were redrawn with more layered bangs, side locks, curls, and sharper profiles, while eyes are now mostly black with smaller coloured iris glints and tiny highlights.

v0.25.141 Vector hero art polish

polishChatGPT Image-style character pass

The canvas vector hero gets a more polished illustration read while staying fully code-native: coloured glossy irises, visible ears, a tiny nose, stronger hair ribbons, outfit collar/belt accents, little hands, and boot soles. Because this lands inside _drawVectorHero, the in-game player and the Q Character Studio preview update together without adding bitmap assets.

v0.25.140 Performance

polishOutdoor overlay cache

Outdoor fog now reuses one cached canvas gradient per sky palette instead of rebuilding it every frame, and optional god rays are skipped while the adaptive low-FX mode is active. This cuts repeated full-screen canvas work in busy maps without changing combat, hitboxes, or enemy AI.

polishCooler cooldown UI

The skill dock now caches cooldown text and conic-fill percentages, so active cooldowns only write to the DOM when the visible rounded value changes. Combat timing and skill readiness are unchanged; this just removes unnecessary per-frame style and text churn.

Phase 1 Foundation

Save / load — versioned localStorage

  • saveState() / loadState() / clearSave() / hasSave() with explicit field whitelists.
  • SAVE_VERSION = 1 gate — future schema changes either migrate or fall back cleanly.
  • Autosaves every 15 s of wall time, plus on class-select, level-up, boss-kill, respawn, tab-hide, and beforeunload.
  • Continue-from-save always lands in town with clean transient state — never loads into hp ≤ 0 or a mid-boss killbox.
  • Phase-2 placeholder fields (achievements, dailyState, prestige, comboRecord, muted) pre-added to the schema so follow-up features don't need a version bump.

Web Audio — synthesized, no assets

  • 4 SFX via AudioContext oscillator envelopes:
    • Hit — 240 Hz square blip
    • Crit — 520 / 780 Hz two-tone
    • Level up — C-E-G triangle arpeggio
    • Death — 180 Hz sawtooth slide
  • Initialized on first user gesture (class-select click, keydown, or pointerdown) to satisfy Chrome/Safari autoplay policy.
  • M toggles mute. Mute state persists in the save.

Phase 2 Retention hooks

🏆Achievements + codex (press N)

  • 12 milestones tracked in game.achievements, persisted via the Phase 1 schema.
  • Modal shows unlocked + locked rows, live kill counter, and best-ever combo (game.comboRecord).
  • Hooks fire from killMonster, the level-up loop, bumpCombo, and attemptEnhance.

🌅Daily login + rotating challenge

  • Deterministic UTC-day rotation — Math.floor(Date.now() / 86400000) % 4. Four challenges: 50 kills, reach level 15, enhance once, 30-hit combo.
  • Login bonus: +200 × min(7, streak) Lumens.
  • HUD banner (top-right) shows the current challenge, progress bar, and streak.
  • Rolls on new-game class-select and on every load.

⟳Respec (button inside the attributes modal, U)

  • Cost formula: 2000 × max(1, level − 5) Lumens.
  • Refunds all allocated AP to skillPoints and resets milestonesUnlocked.
  • Live cost + "you have X" preview rendered every frame while the modal is open.

✨Prestige / Ascension

  • Auto-offered when the player reaches level 50.
  • Each ascension: +30 % XP, +30 % damage, +1 permanent starting AP — all stackable.
  • Resets level / exp / attributes / job / master / inventory / defeated-boss set.
  • getAtk() applies game.prestige.dmgMult. All XP gains (normal + super-boss) apply game.prestige.xpMult.

⚡Combo milestone buffs (inside bumpCombo)

  • Cross 50 hits → +50 % ATK for 8 s.
  • Cross 100 hits → next 3 crits guaranteed.
  • Cross 150 hits → +100 % XP for 10 s.
  • Timer buffs decay via the existing player.buffs tick loop. The guaranteed-crit counter is tracked on player._guaranteedCrit so it doesn't decay as a timer.

Phase 3 Juice pass

Per-hit impact flash

Every swing now fires an extra screen flash — flash(0.1) on basic hits, flash(0.35) on crits — on top of the existing shake / hit-stop / audio / particles.

Damage-scaled feedback

  • Shake now scales with finalDmg: addShake((isCrit ? 5 : 1.8) + min(6, finalDmg/200)).
  • Damage-number font size scales with damage for both normal and crit, so a 500-damage crit visibly towers over a 40-damage jab.

Drop-rarity theatrics

  • emitRarityBurst(x, y, rarity) fires rarity-keyed bursts on every loot site (normal kill, mini-boss, boss extras, super-boss pile):
    • Rare 14 blue particles + small flash.
    • Epic 24 purple particles + flash(0.18) + addShake(2.5).
    • Legendary 40 gold particles + flash(0.35) + addShake(5) + level-up chime.
  • emitNearMiss(x, y) teases 6 gray sparkles when a drop roll failed by < 4 % margin.

Enemy squash-stretch on hit

  • hitMonster sets m.scaleX / m.scaleY — 1.22 / 0.74 on crit, 1.14 / 0.82 on normal.
  • updateMonsters eases them back to 1.0 at 22 %/frame.
  • The drawMonster call site wraps in ctx.save / scale / restore, anchored at the sprite's feet so the entire monster pops without floating.

Boss phase transitions

  • Aetherion phase 2 + 3 now call addHitStop + audio.play('crit') for cinematic punch.
  • Gravitos (v0.9.x addition) gets the same treatment — phase 2 and phase 3 both carry a hit-stop + audio cue.

Patches Follow-ups

Reset button

Destructive option inside the attributes modal (U), below Respec. Double-confirms, calls clearSave(), and reloads to class-select. Sets game._resetting = true first so the autosave / tab-hide / beforeunload handlers don't rewrite the save during the reload window.

Also surfaced on the HUD as a small red ☠ Reset pill next to the help button (bottom-right), so a friend loading the build can wipe the save without digging into the attributes menu. Reuses the same resetSave() flow. The pill sits at z-index: 60 so it stays reachable even while the class-select modal (.modal-overlay, z-index 50) is open.

Codex keybind fix — C → N

Skills bind to fixed slot letters ['d','s','a','e','w','q','c','x'], so C triggers a skill cast for any class with a c-slot skill. The codex shortcut was firing in parallel with the skill cast, opening the modal mid-combat. Moved codex to N; no collision.

✦Juicy damage numbers

Dopamine-driven pass on enemy damage popups so every hit lands as a tiny reward. All the effects live in drawDamageNumbers() and the main hitMonster push, so secondary pushes (EMPOWERED, ECHO, VOID!, EXEC, etc.) inherit the juice automatically via field back-fill.

  • Pop-in overshoot. easeOutBack scale from ~0.4x to 1x over 8 frames — each number punches onto screen instead of appearing flat.
  • Shrink-and-fade tail. Final ~14 frames shrink while fading so numbers "poof" out cleanly, closing the micro-reward loop.
  • Scatter. Random horizontal vx (with drag) plus a short rotation wobble on spawn so stacked hits don't read as a single column.
  • Tiered colour ramp. Non-crit tiers by damage — <80 white → <200 warm → <500 orange → 500+ hot red. Crits stay gold; 500+ crits shift to amber. Magnitude is readable pre-attentively before the eye parses the digits.
  • Embossed crits. Crits render with a coloured shadowBlur glow and an inner #fff7b0 stroke over the black outline — the "gold foil" look that telegraphs a big hit.
  • Comma formatting. finalDmg.toLocaleString() — 1,234 reads bigger than 1234, and four-figure hits now feel like a milestone.
  • Linger on big hits. Life bumped from 46 → 52 (tier ≥ 2) / 58 (crit) so the player has time to admire the number.

Hotkey 0 — change job / unlock mastery (v0.9.9)

Hotkey 0 now acts as a shortcut to the advancement flow so players don't have to wait for the automatic modal to re-fire.

Master skill bar fix — level-20 X slot

At level 20 every master advancement unlocks an ultimate skill bound to the x slot (Grand Warcry, Apocalypse Swing, Shadow Clones, Meteor Shower, One Shot One Kill, etc.). renderSkillBar was calling skillsForClass(player.cls, player.job) — missing the third master argument — so the filter at skillsForClass silently dropped any skill scoped to a master, leaving the X slot stuck on its locked placeholder. Casting also effectively failed because the player never saw the icon to know it was ready. Same bug fixed in the NPC skill-trainer modal (openSkillsModal).

v0.12.1 Endgame pass · identity · feel

Eight-item release: a unique sniper skill, cooldown tuning across every class, cel-shaded Dragon Quest-style mob art, stronger knockback, name + cosmetic picker, silent-reward feedback, cosmetic unlocks, and an infinite-floor tower mode.

✦Sniper S — Railshot

Sniper-specific override for the archer S slot. Instant piercing rail in a flat line from the player; every hit empowers the next by +30% damage (escalating chain). Thick beam, electric sparks on impact, muzzle burst, shake. Cooldown 1300 ms, MP 16. Triggers snipe_railgun entry in SKILL_FNS; selection happens through the new skillBySlot() specificity scorer (master > job > class).

Cooldown rebalance

Full tuning pass across every skill definition in SKILLS. Rogue combat feels faster, mage skills recast cleaner, warrior heavy swings breathe. Master signatures trimmed 5–15% except lich_harvest (60s, spec-designed).

ClassRepresentative CDs (ms)
WarriorSlash 360 · Power 720 · Slam 1000 · Rush 900 · WarCry 7000
RogueStab 150 · Backstab 650 · Dagger 650 · Dash 750 · Flurry 900
MageBolt 210 · Fireball 800 · Ice 650 · Blink 650 · Burst 1400
ArcherArrow 260 · Multi 700 · Charged 950 · Evade 750 · EagleEye 7000

✦Dragon Quest-style mob art

Full rewrite of the grunt renderer (drawCuteMob) to cel-shaded 2-tone style. Every mob now gets an iconic silhouette with hard-edge lighting, a thick 2 px outer contour, and glossy anime-style eyes with a large upper-left highlight.

  • 2-tone cel-shading. _celFillPath paints the base color, clips to the silhouette, and fills a diagonal polygon wedge in the shade tone — crisp, no gradients. Light source implied upper-left.
  • 2 px outer stroke. _celStroke with rounded joins / caps for the signature DQ "confident contour" feel.
  • Glossy anime eyes. _celEye — white sclera, vertical-oval pupil shifted by facing, large primary highlight + small secondary gloss. Evil variants get a red iris core and a soft red glow halo.
  • Per-type iconic silhouettes. Slime (teardrop), snail (round shell + antenna stalks), mushroom (dome + polka dots), horned (bone-triangle horns + fangs), stump (barrel + wood rings + leaf sprout), zombie (drippy cap + X eyes + drool), mummy (bandage wraps + one slit covered), skeleton (skull shape + ribcage + spine), wraith (robed ghost + wavy tail + glow halo), scorpion (segmented carapace + pincer claws + curled stinger).
  • Unified dispatch. drawMonster routes all grunts through drawCuteMob; bosses (king slime, mushmom, aetherion, gravitos) keep their signature per-type renderers.

Knockback +35%

Global × 1.35 multiplier applied inside performMelee / performAround, plus direct-site bumps on warrior smash (10 → 14), rogue V-slash (4 → 6), ground slam (7 → 10), misc front-facing skill hits (3 → 5). Enemies fly further on impact without feeling unfair.

✦Character name + cosmetic picker

Class-select modal now includes a name input (#hero-name-input) and three swatch rows (#swatch-hair / #swatch-skin / #swatch-eye). Selecting a swatch writes to player.look and auto-computes complementary tones via _mixHex (e.g. picking a hair color also sets hairHi; picking a skin color sets skinHi + skinShd). The chosen name renders as a gold-bordered tag above the player's head in-game via _drawPlayerNameTag, alongside their level.

Silent-reward feedback pass

Closed dopamine leaks on previously-silent rewards. New Web Audio envelopes in audio.play: potion_hp, potion_mp, meso, mp_refund, cd_refund, chest_open, pickup.

  • Potion pickup. Color-tinted particle burst + HP/MP toast + envelope sfx.
  • Meso pickup. Large meso drops (≥ 40) now play a chime; huge drops (≥ 120) also toast with rarity color.
  • MP refund (Mana Font milestone) plays a rising cue; CD refund (Spellweaver) plays a short recast cue + -1s CD number.
  • Chest open. 3-note chime, rising sparkle column, tier-scaled shake + flash. Gold/silver chests also layer the levelup cue.

✦Cosmetic unlock system

COSMETICS catalog for hair / cape / weapon skins earned through trackPickup hooks on kills, chests, boss kills, and tower floors. Bestiary counts persist via game.bestiary; unlocks persist on player.cosmetics.

  • Hair — Flame Tips (50 mushrooms), Mint Frost (30 slimes), Twilight (20 wraiths), Royal Gold (5 gold chests).
  • Cape — Shadow (25 horny), Ember (10 scorpions), Frost (tower floor 10), Astral (tower floor 25).
  • Weapon — Crystal Blade (kill Aetherion), Void Edge (kill Gravitos), Sunfire (tower floor 15), Heirloom (10 silver chests).

Unlocks announce with an epic toast + levelup cue; checkCosmeticUnlocks() fires on every trackPickup call, saving automatically.

✦Tower of Ascension

New infinite-floor map (MAPS.tower) with a permanent portal from town (MAPS.town.portals). startTower sets up wave state; killing all enemies on a floor advances to the next. HP scales +18%/floor, ATK +12%/floor. Best floor persists on game.towerBestFloor.

HUD overlay (#tower-hud) shows floor / modifier / cleared / best. Floor clear heals 15% HP + 20% MP. Modifiers rotate every 3 floors.

Entry point. Town → rightmost bazaar portal (↑) → Tower of Ascension.

v0.12.2 Polish · art · difficulty

Follow-up to v0.12.1. Player sprite now matches the enemies' DQ-style cel-shading, Tower of Ascension becomes a cramped subway carriage with tougher mobs, monster names go full plush-toy, and damage numbers get a chunky gold-foil upgrade.

✦Player cel-shading + stroke upgrade

The procedural chibi renderer now matches the enemies' Dragon Quest look. The chibi transform gets a subtle vertical stretch (scale 1.19, 1.06 up from 0.97) so the player reads as slightly taller without breaking proportions.

  • Torso silhouette. Factored out into a reusable torsoPath() closure. First pass strokes the path at 3 px for the outer contour, second pass fills the body color, third pass clips to the silhouette and drops a hard diagonal shadow wedge in cc.bodyShd, fourth pass lays a 1 px inner stroke for the outline-over-fill look.
  • Head. Outer ring goes from hr + 1 to hr + 2; the old crescent shadow is replaced with a hard polygon clipped to the head circle so the light/dark boundary reads as one crisp line.
  • Legs + boots. Each leg and boot now has its own dark outline rect before the fill so the bottom half has the same confident contour as the top.

✦Carriage of Ascension (tower rework)

The tower becomes a cramped subway carriage — feels like an endless train ride where each stop is a fresh wave of fares refusing to let you off. World width drops 1500 → 760; two drop-through benches and one overhead handrail replace the old platform layout.

  • Custom backdrop. New drawCarriageInterior() paints a full train car interior: parallax tunnel streaks outside the windows, overhead fluorescent strip with glow, windowed wall with individual panes + glowing tunnel streaks behind the glass, rivet rows, floor grooves + yellow safety line, two sliding side doors with EXIT / NEXT signs, and hanging handholds that bob with the train.
  • Tier pools tougher. Early carriage floors skip snails/slimes entirely — you fight slime/mushroom on floor 1 and horny variants by floor 4. Later tiers lean into wraiths, scorpions, and mummies.
  • HP/ATK scaling harder. HP +28%/floor (was +18%), ATK +18%/floor (was +12%). Wave cap at 8 mobs so the small carriage doesn't turn into a soup.
  • Rename. Portal, toasts, and HUD updated: "🚇 Carriage of Ascension", floors renamed Stop 1, Stop 2 ….
