v0.25.107 Hero animation pass — expressive face, state colour rim, anticipation-driven swing

Layered four small visual upgrades onto the procedural drawCuteCharacter rig without touching the existing body / hair / cel-shading passes. Same offset principle as the body bob — new state reads (jump, hit, attack, low HP, buff, crit) drive small per-frame deltas over the existing draw stack instead of branching on a different sprite.

  • featEyebrows — hidden by default. Three expressive states: arched-up on jump (airborne with |vy| > 0.6), furrowed \\/ on hitStun > 80, focused down-inward while attacking. Drawn after the eyes on the upper-eye line so they read at chibi scale.
  • featHit-stun mouth — replaced the v0.25.66 surprised "o" with a 5-segment zigzag stroke. Reads as a real "ouch!" bite instead of a passive surprise.
  • featAttack mouth gape — the open-mouth ellipse during a swing now scales with swingBase (the bell curve), so the gape grows at mid-swing and snaps shut on follow-through. Tongue strip lengthens with it.
  • featLow-HP red rim — pulsing additive ellipse rim around the body when HP < 30 %, with a harder/faster pulse below 15 %. Painted as a top layer after everything else — survives any palette / equipment changes.
  • featBuff accent rim — subtle pulsing rim while a buff is active. Gold for warCry / rampage / holy, red for bloodlust, ice-blue for holyShield.
  • featCrit gold flash — hitMonster stamps player.lastCritT = game.time on every crit. drawCuteCharacter paints a 280 ms gold halo (additive) over the body silhouette and fades it out with a slight outward growth.
  • polishAnticipation-driven swing — the body lean (swingAng) and the blade angle (drawCuteSwingingBlade) both swapped from a single easeOutBack bell to a piecewise three-phase curve: 0–18 % anticipation (body + blade pull BACK), 18–55 % strike (cubic ease-out snap to the peak), 55–100 % follow-through (damped wobble). Sells the wind-up → impact → settle rhythm that the old single-curve swing was missing.

v0.25.97 Defensive guards — a thrown drawImage can't kill the render loop anymore

User reported "main character sprites does not appear" after the v0.25.94–96 art pass. Most likely cause: an unhandled drawImage throw inside drawPlatforms() (tainted canvas from CORS, or a corner-case argument) propagates up through loop() → kills the requestAnimationFrame chain → no further rendering, including the player. Confirmed via direct probe: drawPlayer() renders correctly when called manually, so the player path itself is fine; what's missing is the loop continuing to call it.

Fixes

  • _lxDrawTiledRow now wraps its drawImage loop in a try/catch and returns false on failure. First failure logs a single console.warn for diagnosis, subsequent failures stay silent.
  • drawPlatforms only takes the continue shortcut when the image actually painted. If _lxDrawTiledRow returned false the procedural fallback runs in the same iteration, so platforms always render even if the new tile assets misbehave.
  • drawSanctumCosmos and drawBossDecor wrap their pillar ctx.drawImage calls in try/catch. Procedural shaft + cap fallback is now reachable when the image path is the broken one.
  • Extra zero-dimension guard in _lxDrawTiledRow (sw <= 0 / w <= 0) for paranoia — these would have thrown INDEX_SIZE_ERR in some browsers.

v0.25.96 Floor tile gap fix — bake seamless single-tile crop at image load

The grass+dirt floor was showing gaps between repeats. Root cause: the source image has ~88 px of transparent padding on the left and ~94 px on the right; tiling the whole image meant every repeat started with that transparent edge, producing visible see-through bands across the platform. Same shape for the wood image, which is a 4×2 plank grid that was getting squashed into a 16 px tile.

Fix

  • New _lxBakeSeamlessTile(img, mode) helper. Two modes:
    • 'auto' — sample alpha across 3 Y rows, find the leftmost contiguous opaque column run, crop to that range × full image height. Used for floorGrass: 1152×864 source → 970×864 baked tile (88 + 94 px of transparent padding stripped).
    • 'grid:CxR' — crop the top-left cell of an explicit C-column × R-row layout. Used for floorWood: 1152×864 source → 288×432 baked tile (one plank instead of the whole 4×2 grid).
  • Pillar assets stay untouched ('none' mode) — they're drawn whole, not tiled.
  • _lxTileReady + _lxNatW/H updated so the helper accepts HTMLCanvasElement as well as HTMLImageElement. Baked canvases are dropped into LX_TILES in place of the original image after load completes.
  • Verified with browser probe: floor_grass_b bakes to 970×864 (was 1152×864 with bands of transparent padding), floor_wood_b bakes to 288×432 (was 1152×864 4×2 grid).

v0.25.93 Ground anchoring fix — characters now actually touch the floor (8 floating types lifted)

Bug fix + new feature. Generated sprites consistently have 8-19% empty padding below the character — the old -targetH × 0.95 hard-coded anchor put canvas-bottom near feet, leaving most monsters floating 5-15 px above the ground. Now the renderer detects each sprite's actual bbox-bottom at load and anchors THAT to the foot line, with a small ground bleed for grounded mobs and a deliberate lift for the 8 floating types.

Auto-detect bbox-bottom per sprite

  • New _detectSpriteBboxBottom(img) walks the sprite's pixels bottom-up to find the lowest opaque pixel Y.
  • Stored at load time in MONSTER_SPRITE_META / BOSS_SPRITE_META / ZODIAC_SPRITE_META caches.
  • Sample fills (out of 768-tall canvases): snail 81% · slime 85% · mushroom 92% · skeleton 90% · wraith 91% · nimbusFox 87% · pearlSprite 86%.

Floating type set

FLOATING_TYPES = {
  honeyBuzz, wraith, nimbusFox, pearlSprite,  // mobs that hover
  aetherion,                                   // cosmic dragon (boss)
};
FLOATING_ZODIAC = { gemini, virgo, pisces };  // star spirits / angel / koi

Anchor formula

// Position so the character's bbox-bottom lands on the foot line:
const dyOffset = -((bboxBottomY + 1) / srcH) * targetH;
// Then add a small offset:
//   ground monsters: + targetH × 0.02 (2 % bury below feet, "pressed into ground")
//   floating types:  - targetH × 0.18 (18 % lift, character hovers above feet)

Bonus fix

  • Boss facing convention: _drawBossSprite was mirroring on m.facing > 0 (backwards) — bosses faced the wrong way going right. Now matches monsters: mirror when facing < 0.
  • Aspect-aware boss scale: bosses no longer forced to square aspect; they preserve the source aspect ratio.

v0.25.92 23 new sprites — full mob roster + 4 bosses + all 12 zodiac + atmospheric haze removed

Big sprite content drop: every remaining monster, boss, and zodiac sign now has a ludo.ai chibi sprite, all style-anchored to the existing coralImp via generateWithStyle for consistent feel. Plus the translucent atmospheric haze overlay is removed per user request.

Translucent overlay removal

  • The 18%-opacity dark-violet haze (rgba(20,24,48,0.18) fillRect over the whole screen each frame) is gone. Backgrounds + characters now render at full vibrance.

Sprite content (~30 credits)

  • Failure-safe — if any sprite fails to load (network, missing file), the procedural path takes over with no error.

Style consistency note

  • Per user feedback "ensure the general feel of the sprites are similar", the bosses + zodiac were generated via generateWithStyle (not createImage) using the existing coralImp sprite as the style reference. Output sprites inherit coralImp's line weight, palette saturation, and 4-tone cel shading.

v0.25.91 Head-Y locked at 49 across every frame in every state (range = 0 px)

Switched walk to head-anchor too. Head Y is now exactly 49 across all 16 walk frames + idle + 16 jump + 16 attack + 4 class skill anims = 57+ frames, 0 px head-Y range. Truly locked.

What changed

  • v0.25.90 had walk on feet anchor — head bobbed 49 → 67 across the cycle (18 px). Natural for walking but the user wanted head fully locked.
  • Switched walk to head anchor in HERO_META. Now head is at canvas Y=49 in every walk frame.
  • Visual change: legs alternate below the locked head; body/torso may shift slightly but head stays put.

Verified

  • Probed 27+ frames across walk/idle/jump/attack/class skills.
  • min head Y = 49, max head Y = 49, range = 0 px.
  • Centroid X stays within 1 px (319-321) across all states.

v0.25.90 Per-anim anchor strategy — head-top for in-air / asymmetric, feet for ground

Identified and fixed a 500+ pixel head-drop on attack and jump-apex frames. Switched in-air and asymmetric-pose animations to head-top anchor (head locked at idle's head-Y across every frame). Walk/idle stay on feet anchor.

The remaining drift

  • v0.25.89's centroid-X anchor fixed horizontal wobble. But VERTICAL drift remained on poses where bbox-bottom isn't actually the feet — jump-apex (legs tucked, bbox-bottom = back/butt) and attack-extension (forward lean, bbox-bottom = lower-than-standing).
  • Attack frames 4-10 had bh~250 (vs idle's 771) due to the AI drawing a forward-leaning compressed pose. Feet-anchor placed those at canvas Y=565 — head DROPPED 516 px from idle's Y=49.
  • Jump-apex tuck had bh=159 → head dropped to Y=660.

Fix

  • New per-anim anchor field in HERO_META: 'feet' (default — bbox-bottom → idleFootY) or 'head' (bbox-top → idleHeadTopY).
  • Anchor assignments: walk + idle = feet (correct — bbox-bottom is the planted foot). Jump / attack / hit / death / class skills (warrior/rogue/mage/archer) = head.
  • Runtime computes HERO.idleHeadTopY = idleAnchor.minY at load and passes it through to _heroExtractAndNormalize.

Verified — head Y locked at 49 across all in-air / asymmetric states

v0.25.89 Pixel-perfect cross-frame sync — centroid anchor + uniform per-sheet scale

Replaces bbox-center horizontal anchoring with centroid of opaque pixels (mass center, dominated by torso + head — barely shifts when a thin arm extends). Plus a uniform per-sheet scale instead of per-frame so tucked-leg / curled poses stay proportionally smaller (correct) instead of being stretched to match the tallest frame.

The bug

  • Bbox-center anchoring put bbox horizontal mid-point at canvas center. For asymmetric poses — like the punch frame where the right arm extends right — the bbox extends right, so the body had to shift LEFT to "center" the bbox. Result: the head visibly wobbled across frames in the same animation.
  • Measured drift in attack[2] (mid-punch): bbox-center X = 337, vs idle's 320 → 17 px wobble.

The fix

  • New _findChibiAnchor returns centroid X (alpha-weighted mass center) plus the bbox + feet.
  • Animation normalizer maps each frame's centroid to canvas-center X. Centroid only shifts slightly under thin-limb extensions, so body axis stays stable.
  • Per-sheet uniform sheetFitScale = idleBh / maxBhInSheet. Tallest pose in a sheet matches idle's height; shorter poses (tucked legs at jump apex, curled body during punch wind-up) stay proportionally smaller. Natural body bob during walk preserved instead of vertically stretched away.
  • Idle uses the same centroid + feet anchors with scale=1, so it aligns to animation frames by the same body-axis reference.

Verification

Framecentroid Xfeet Ybbox hbbox w
idle320819771406
walk[0/4/8/12]321/321/321/321819/819/819/819762/753/753/756~407
jump[3] (launch)320819512279
jump[8] (apex tuck)320819159191
attack[2] (punch out)321819507134
attack[8] (recover)320819255265

Centroid X stays within 1 px tolerance across every state and every pose. Feet Y identical. The natural bbox h/w variations now correctly reflect pose differences (curled vs extended) rather than artifacts of normalization.

v0.25.87 Smoother walk + attack (16 frames each) + perfect cross-state positioning

Walk and attack animations regenerated at 16 frames each (vs 9) for almost 2× the position updates per cycle. Plus a hidden 19 px horizontal drift between idle and walking states is now fixed — every animation state shares the same character size + position to the pixel.

Smoother animations (~10 credits)

  • Walk: 9 → 16 frames (4×4 grid, Eagle, 2 s source, 12 fps in-game). Smoother leg-step transitions and arm swing arcs.
  • Attack: 9 → 16 frames (4×4 grid, 18 fps). Snappier punch with smoother wind-up and recovery in-between frames.
  • Both regenerated via animateSprite with model:"eagle"; cost ~5 credits each.

Cross-state positioning fix

  • Bug: ludo's source idle had the character drawn ~19 px right of canvas center (centerX=339 vs the 640-wide canvas's center=320). Animation frames were bbox-normalized to canvas-center (320), but idle was used raw — so when the runtime switched between idle and walk, the character popped 19 px horizontally.
  • Fix: HERO.idle now goes through the SAME _normalizeFrameToReference pipeline as every animation frame. Output is a normalized canvas, not the raw image, with character centered at canvas center.
  • Verified: idle / walk[0] / walk[8] / attack[0] / attack[8] all measure bbox height 771, feet Y 819, center X 319-320 (1 px tolerance). Identical position to the pixel.
  • Studio "Apply" path also benefits — PLAYER_CUSTOM_SPRITE_CANVAS now points at the normalized idle.

v0.25.86 6 NPC sprites + background seam fix

Replaced the procedural pixel-NPC bodies in the homestead with ludo.ai-generated chibi NPCs, and fixed a long-standing seam visible in the parallax background.

Background seam fix

  • Problem: parallax background tiled by drawing two side-by-side copies. The bg images aren't seamlessly tileable, so the right edge of one copy met the left edge of the next visibly mismatched — a hard cut every W px of camera scroll.
  • Fix: mirror the second copy horizontally. Right edge of copy 1 now meets right-edge-of-copy-2 (its mirror), so pixels along the seam match exactly. Also rounded the parallax shift to integer pixels to kill sub-pixel blur.
  • Single 7-line change in drawBackgroundLayer; works automatically with every existing background image.

6 NPC sprites (homestead)

  • Old Arlen (info giver) — bearded village elder with walking stick

  • Pipeline: createImage n=1 + removeBackground per NPC. Cost ~6 credits.

v0.25.85 Class-specific skill animations · one-shot attack timing

Each of the four classes now has its own skill animation, and attacks play through as proper one-shots synced to when the skill was cast (instead of looping for as long as player.attacking happened to be true).

4 class skill animations (~20 credits)

  • Warrior — sword swing: arm cocks back over shoulder, swings in wide diagonal arc, body twists for power. teen_warrior_swing.webp · 14 fps.
  • Rogue — dagger stab: arm pulls to chest, snap-thrusts forward, body leans in. teen_rogue_stab.webp · 16 fps (snappiest).
  • Mage — spell cast: hands raise, magical energy crackles between palms, push outward to release. teen_mage_cast.webp · 12 fps.
  • Archer — bow shot: left arm extends with invisible bow, right arm draws to cheek, releases forward. teen_archer_shot.webp · 14 fps.
  • All 4 frames at 2×2 grid, ~1 s clip; bbox-normalized to idle's reference height + feet Y like the rest of the hero set.

One-shot attack timing

  • Problem: previously the attack animation looped frames keyed on absolute game.time while player.attacking was true. If the attack started mid-frame-cycle, the user saw the animation joining in progress (bad timing); if attacking flipped off mid-anim, the rest of the animation was cut.
  • Fix: anchor-based playback. When attack begins, capture player._heroAtkAt = game.time. Frame index = floor((game.time - anchor) / framesPerStep), clamped to last frame. Animation plays from frame 0 → last every time, regardless of when the attack triggered relative to game.time.
  • Bonus: animation now completes even if player.attacking goes false before the last frame — feels much more decisive. Same fix applied to hit + death with _heroHitAt and _heroDeathAt anchors.

State machine — final priority order

death (hp <= 0)        ↑ one-shot, anchor _heroDeathAt
hit (hitStun > 0)      | one-shot, anchor _heroHitAt
attack (class-specific)| one-shot, anchor _heroAtkAt — duration = frames/fps
jump (|vy| > 0.5)      | loop (8 fps)
walk (|vx| > 0.5)      | loop (9 fps)
idle                   ↓ static

Class selection via player.cls

  • HERO.classFrames[player.cls] resolves to the right frames at runtime; falls back to the generic attack set if player.cls isn't mapped.
  • Loading screen now preloads all 10 hero sheets (idle + walk + jump + attack + hit + death + 4 class anims). Progress bar shows N/10.

v0.25.84 Hit + death anims · loading screen · 2× skill cooldowns

Three changes shipped together: full hero state machine completion (hit + death anims), a polished loading screen so the player never sees a blank world before sprites are ready, and a balance pass that doubles every player skill's cooldown.

Hit + death animations

  • Hit: teen_hit_sheet.webp — 4 frames (2×2), 12 fps, 1 s recoil cycle. Plays while player.hitStun > 0. One-shot (clamps to last frame, doesn't loop).
  • Death: teen_death_sheet.webp — 4 frames (2×2), 4 fps, slow collapse. Plays while player.hp <= 0. One-shot.
  • Cost: ~10 credits (2 × animateSprite Eagle, 4 frames each).

State machine — full priority order

death (hp <= 0)        ↑ one-shot, clamps to last frame
hit (hitStun > 0)      | one-shot, clamps to last frame
attack (attacking)     | loop (14 fps)
jump (|vy| > 0.5)      | loop (8 fps)
walk (|vx| > 0.5)      | loop (9 fps)
idle                   ↓ static

Loading screen

  • New full-screen overlay (#loading-overlay) preloads all 6 hero sprite assets in parallel before revealing the game.
  • Progress bar fills as each asset loads; status reads "Loading sprites… N/6 → Ready".
  • Hides via 0.45 s fade-out only after both: (1) all required images loaded, (2) HERO_READY event fires (so the JS-side normalization is also complete).
  • Hard 8 s fallback: if anything stalls, overlay hides anyway and the procedural fallback takes over.

Balance: 2× skill cooldowns

  • Every entry in the player SKILLS object had its cd doubled. 52 skills affected.
  • Examples: slash 360 → 720, powerStrike 720 → 1440, groundSlam 1000 → 2000, warCry 7000 → 14000, bloodlust 18000 → 36000, lich_harvest 60000 → 120000.
  • Monster skills (MONSTER_SKILLS) and class defense moves (block / parry / vanish / roll) are untouched — only player skills got the nerf.
  • One-shot Python script Sprites/character/double_cooldowns.py handles the regex replacement; saved in case the user wants to roll it back or re-tune.

v0.25.83 Hero state machine + jump + attack + consistent frame normalization

Three states wired in to the hero (walk, jump, attack) plus a normalization fix that makes every animation frame render at the exact same on-screen height + feet position.

Consistency fix

  • Problem: each frame was independently bbox-fitted to ~92% of canvas height. A frame with extended legs (taller bbox) and a frame with legs together (shorter bbox) both got scaled to 92% — so the character APPEARED bigger when legs were tucked, smaller when extended.
  • Fix: added _findChibiBbox + _normalizeFrameToReference. Now the IDLE sprite's character bbox is the canonical reference; every animated frame gets scaled so its bbox HEIGHT matches idle's exactly, then anchored at idle's feet Y position.
  • Result: character is precisely the same size + at the same feet Y across idle / walk / jump / attack. Position is consistent, no shrinking or shifting.

2 new animations (Eagle, 9 frames each)

  • Jump: teen_jump_sheet.webp — crouch → spring up → arms overhead at peak → land. 8 fps. Cost: 5.2 credits.
  • Attack: teen_attack_sheet.webp — wind-up → punch → recovery. 14 fps (snappier). Cost: 5.2 credits.
  • Plus their .mp4 previews. Total: ~10 credits this version.

State machine in _drawPlayerCustomSprite

// Priority order (highest first):
if (player.attacking)              → HERO.attackFrames
else if (|player.vy| > 0.5)        → HERO.jumpFrames
else if (|player.vx| > 0.5)        → HERO.walkFrames
else                                → HERO.idle
  • Each state has its own fps tuned to feel natural — walk 9 fps (smooth), jump 8 fps (medium), attack 14 fps (snappy).
  • Hero path only — the studio mannequin composite still uses the simpler walk/idle split (it doesn't have jump/attack frames).
  • Detection signals: player.attacking (boolean set by skill firing), player.vy (vertical velocity > 0.5 = airborne), player.vx (horizontal velocity > 0.5 = walking).

Loader refactor

  • HERO_META is now per-action: { walk, jump, attack } — each entry has its own { sheet, frames, gridW, gridH, fps }.
  • Loader uses async/await + Promise.all on idle + 3 sheets, then runs each through _heroExtractAndNormalize using the idle's bbox as reference.
  • Console log now reports loaded counts: [Hero] loaded teen idle + walk(9) + jump(9) + attack(9)

v0.25.81 Hero character — replace mannequin with complete teen sprite (Eagle-quality walk)

Quality pivot. The faceless mannequin + extracted face / hair overlay system was producing muddy, alignment-prone output. Replaced with a single complete pre-styled teen character sprite (white tee + blue jeans + brown hair) animated at higher quality (Eagle model, 9 frames).

Why the pivot

  • Layered approach (mannequin + face overlay + hair overlay) compounded scaling artifacts and the face/hair often misaligned with the bobbing animated head.
  • animateSprite Blitz model is rated 4/10 visual quality by ludo — produced visible blur and frame-to-frame inconsistency.
  • One full sprite is simpler to keep on-model. ludo's Eagle model (8/10 visual) holds the t-shirt, jeans, hair, and face features stable across all 9 walk frames.

What v0.25.81 ships

  • Sprites/character/hero/teen_idle.webp — single transparent canonical sprite. 640×864. Teen boy, white t-shirt, blue jeans, brown sneakers, medium-brown shaggy hair, gentle smile, 3/4 right-facing stance.
  • Sprites/character/hero/teen_walk_sheet.webp — 1536×1536 spritesheet, 3×3 grid, 9 frames at ~9 fps for a smooth ~1 s walk loop. Generated via animateSprite with model:"eagle", duration:2, frame_size:256.
  • Sprites/character/hero/teen_walk.mp4 — preview video.
  • Cost: ~7 credits (1 createImage n=2 + 0.5 removeBackground + 5.2 animateSprite Eagle).

Runtime

  • New HERO + HERO_META globals. Auto-load both PNGs at module init, pre-extract 9 walk frames as offscreen canvases.
  • On hero load (if studio hasn't already applied a custom avatar): default window.PLAYER_CUSTOM_SPRITE_CANVAS + PLAYER_CUSTOM_WALK_FRAMES + PLAYER_SPRITE_FACES_RIGHT = true to the hero. Player sees the teen by default.
  • Per-sprite facing convention: _drawPlayerCustomSprite now mirrors when PLAYER_SPRITE_FACES_RIGHT doesn't match the in-game facing — works correctly for both the right-facing hero AND the left-facing studio mannequin composite.
  • Adaptive fps: hero uses 9 fps for the 9-frame loop; the studio's 4-frame mannequin walk uses 6 fps. Both feel right.
  • Revert button now restores the hero (instead of falling all the way back to procedural drawCuteCharacter).

What still works

  • Character Studio (Q) — fully functional. Apply still composites the layered mannequin and overrides the hero per-sprite. The mannequin's facing convention is honored separately.
  • Procedural drawCuteCharacter — fallback for the case where neither the hero nor the studio output is loaded.

v0.25.79 Monster animation pipeline — first idle spritesheet (snail, ludo.ai animateSprite)

Adds an animation runtime alongside the static sprite path. Monsters with an entry in MONSTER_ANIM_DEFS now render from a frame-cycled spritesheet; everything else continues to use the static sprite or procedural fallback. First wired type: snail.

Pipeline

  • Generation: animateSprite with model:"blitz", duration:1.5, frames:4, frame_size:192, image_type:"sprite", loop:true. Returns a 2×2 grid spritesheet + a preview MP4. Cost: 4 credits per animation (Blitz min, regardless of duration).
  • Long-running tool: animation generation can exceed Claude's default tool timeout. Use getSpriteResults?request_id=<id> to poll if the call returns a timeout — the actual job keeps running on ludo's side and the result is retrievable.
  • Source: passes the bg-removed canonical sprite URL as initial_image. The motion prompt drives the deformation (e.g. "subtle idle breathing, antennae sway, body squish slightly").

Runtime

  • MONSTER_ANIMS cache + MONSTER_ANIM_DEFS registry. Each entry: { sheet, frames, gridW, gridH, fps }. Lazy-loaded at module init from Sprites/monsters/anim/<sheet>.
  • Frame ticker: frameIdx = floor(game.time / framesPerStep) % frames with framesPerStep = 60 / fps. Each monster gets a small phase offset (m.x % frames) so a cluster doesn't bob in lockstep.
  • Cell extraction: ctx.drawImage(sheet, col*cellW, row*cellH, cellW, cellH, dx, dy, dw, dh) crops the right grid cell into the same anchor + mirror setup the static sprite uses.
  • Fallback chain: animation → static sprite → procedural drawCuteMob. Failure-safe; loading errors don't break rendering.

First animation shipped

  • snail — gentle idle breathing, antennae sway softly, body squishes slightly. 4 frames at 3 fps, ~1.33 s loop. Files: Sprites/monsters/anim/snail_idle_sheet.webp (40 KB) + snail_idle.mp4 (32 KB preview).

Adding more monsters

// Drop the new spritesheet into Sprites/monsters/anim/
// Then add an entry to MONSTER_ANIM_DEFS — that's it.
const MONSTER_ANIM_DEFS = {
  snail: { sheet: 'snail_idle_sheet.webp', frames: 4, gridW: 2, gridH: 2, fps: 3 },
  // slime: { sheet: 'slime_idle_sheet.webp', frames: 4, gridW: 2, gridH: 2, fps: 4 },
  // ...
};

v0.25.77 Monster sprites — ludo.ai-generated chibi mobs (6 types wired)

Six starter monster types now render as ludo.ai-generated chibi sprites instead of the procedural drawCuteMob. Other types fall back transparently — no behaviour change for unmapped mobs.

Pipeline

  • Generation: createImage with image_type:"sprite", art_style:"Chibi", perspective:"Side-Scroll", aspect_ratio:"ar_1_1". Each prompt asks for thick black manga ink outlines + 4-tone cel shading + clean isolated white background to match the existing storybook chibi aesthetic.
  • Background removal: removeBackground with creative_edit:false + crop:false preserves the canvas size for transparent compositing.
  • Total cost: 4 credits (6 createImage + 1 mushroom re-roll + 7 removeBackground).

6 monster sprites shipped

  • snail (lvl 1) — honey-brown spiral shell + golden swirl, mint-green body, antennae with eye dots, 3/4 winking smile.
  • slime (lvl 2) — squishy mint-jade gelatinous blob with translucent shine spots.
  • mushroom (lvl 3) — Mario-red toadstool cap with cream spots, big anime eyes with angry slanted brows + mischievous grin (re-rolled from a too-soft first attempt).
  • nougatBear (lvl 16, candy biome) — plump cream-pink candy bear with red heart on chest + blush cheeks.
  • skeleton (lvl 18) — bone-white skull with red glowing eye pinpoint + toothy grin + rusted shortsword in battle stance.
  • coralImp (lvl 38, ocean biome) — coral-pink scaly body with iridescent teal-aqua dorsal fin + tail + pointy fangs grin.

Runtime wiring

  • MONSTER_SPRITES cache: lazy-loaded Image per type at module init. Add new entries to MONSTER_SPRITE_TYPES + drop the matching transparent .webp into Sprites/monsters/ and they wire up automatically.
  • _drawMonsterSprite(m, sx, sy): anchors the sprite at the monster's feet (footX = sx + m.w/2, footY = sy + m.h), scales to m.h × 1.4 so the chibi head doesn't get clipped, mirrors horizontally when m.facing < 0.
  • Dispatch branch added to drawMonster just before the drawCuteMob fallback: else if (MONSTER_SPRITES[m.type]) _drawMonsterSprite(m, sx, sy).
  • Failure-safe: if a sprite fails to load (404, network), it stays out of the cache and the monster falls back to procedural drawing — no crash, no visual gap.

v0.25.76 Hair z-order fix — bangs occlude eyes (chibi convention) + outline on top

Swapped Character Studio's render order so the hair overlay sits on top of the face overlay. Bangs now correctly occlude the eyes (chibi/MapleStory convention) and the hair's baked-in black outline reads cleanly on top of everything.

What changed

  • Old z-order: base → tint → hair → face — eyes peeked through bangs at full alpha, face's pixel data clipped the hair outline at intersections.
  • New z-order: base → tint → face → hair — bangs visually occlude eyes (face still visible through gaps in the hair), hair outline always wins.
  • Single-line change in renderCharStudio(); same change propagates automatically to the in-game custom sprite (drawn from the studio canvas).

Studio panel layout polish (v0.25.75c bundled)

  • Apply / Revert buttons moved to the top of the controls column with a gold accent on Apply (was previously buried at the bottom and easy to miss on smaller viewports).
  • Panel is now scrollable on small viewports (max-height: 92vh; overflow-y: auto) so all controls stay reachable.

v0.25.75 Apply Character Studio avatar to live in-game player

The Character Studio output (skin tone × face × hair) can now be applied to the live in-game player sprite. Procedural drawCuteCharacter stays as the fallback when no custom avatar is applied.

Apply / Revert buttons

  • Two new buttons under the Character Studio panel: Use in game and Revert.
  • Use in game snapshots the current 384×384 composited canvas into window.PLAYER_CUSTOM_SPRITE_CANVAS (one-time copy, no per-frame allocation) and shows a toast.
  • Revert clears the global → drawPlayer falls back to procedural chibi rendering.

Render-time integration in drawPlayer

  • Added a branch at the existing drawCuteCharacter(sx, sy) call site (line ~22560): if PLAYER_CUSTOM_SPRITE_CANVAS is set, the custom sprite renders instead via _drawPlayerCustomSprite().
  • Custom sprite anchors at the player's feet (using the existing _chibiApply transform), scales to player.h × 1.45 (taller than the bbox to fit the chibi's big head), and mirrors horizontally for left-facing.
  • The procedural face overlay (_drawCuteFaceOverlay) is skipped when a custom sprite is in use — the studio's face overlay is already baked in.
  • Block / parry shield bubble + name tag still draw on top regardless of which character path was used.

Caveats

  • Idle pose only. The studio sprite is one fixed 3/4-front pose. While the player walks / runs / attacks, the same sprite is drawn (no animation frames yet). Feels static during action — that's the next batch (per-pose generatePose calls).
  • No clothes layer yet. The mannequin's plain body shows when applied — top / bottom / weapon overlays come next.
  • Apply doesn't persist across reloads (no save). Re-apply after each refresh until the persistence step ships.

v0.25.75b coord-fix patch

  • Initial v0.25.75 had the sprite drawn at user-coord origin assuming _chibiApply translated the origin to player feet. It does not — _chibiApply applies a scale-anchored-at-feet but the coordinate system stays in screen space (which is why drawCuteCharacter takes sx, sy as parameters).
  • Result: the custom sprite was being drawn in the upper-left of the screen at roughly (-0.19 × footX, -0.06 × footY) — far off-screen. Player appeared invisible after Apply, masquerading as "sprite doesn't show".
  • Fix: _drawPlayerCustomSprite now derives footX, footY from the same player.x - game.camera.x + w/2 + player.y + h formulas, then ctx.translate(footX, footY) before the draw. Anchor + scale now work correctly.

v0.25.74 Hair slot + soft-alpha extraction (4 hair styles)

Adds the hair layer slot to the Character Studio with 4 starter styles, plus a soft-alpha extraction mode that fades feature edges naturally instead of capturing AA pixels at hard full alpha.

Soft-alpha extraction mode

  • Why: hair edges have wide anti-aliased gradients (yellow→cream for blonde, black→cream for spike). Hard-alpha extraction captured those gradient pixels at full alpha with their gray-blend RGB, producing a visible halo when composited over a tinted skin tone.
  • What changed: extract_layer.py now defaults to soft_alpha=True. Per-pixel alpha ramps from 0 at the diff threshold to 255 at threshold + soft_alpha_ramp (default 80). Edges that are barely-different fade to transparent; clear feature pixels stay fully opaque.
  • Optional soft_alpha=False falls back to the previous binary mask if a layer needs hard edges (e.g. logo overlays).

4 starter hair overlays

  • Blonde Shaggy: chunky single-silhouette golden tousled bangs, MapleStory warrior-class look.
  • Black Spike: anime-shounen spiky black hair with subtle gray sheen highlights.
  • Brown Pony: chibi straight-cut bangs with a high red-ribbon ponytail. Iconic anime-girl silhouette.
  • Mage Hood: deep purple wizard cowl with silver trim — covers hair entirely, classic mage class read.
  • Plus a Bald option (no hair layer rendered) so the player can opt out.

Studio runtime — 5th picker + new z-order

  • Hair-style picker added below the Face picker (5 buttons matching the existing button styling).
  • Render z-order updated: base → multiply skin tint → hair → face. Hair below face means eyes peek through bangs (chibi convention), face overlay always reads cleanly.
  • Lazy-load now fetches 9 layers in parallel on first studio open (1 base + 4 faces + 4 hairs). Status: Ready · 9 layers loaded.

v0.25.73 Character Studio — 4 face styles + face-aware extractor + halo fixes

Builds on v0.25.72. Three new face styles join Classic (Sleepy, Sharp, Big Grin), plus a face-specific extraction pipeline that fixes both the silhouette fringe halo and the missing-pupil-highlight bug.

Halo fixes — render pipeline + extractor

  • Silhouette halo (mannequin edge looked fuzzy after multiply blend): the old multiply+fillRect+destination-in pipeline over-tinted anti-aliased silhouette pixels with pure skin tone. Replaced with a per-pixel ImageData multiply that touches only existing pixels, preserves alpha exactly, and gives mathematically correct shading. Black outlines stay black; AA edges fade naturally to any skin tone.
  • Eye halo + missing pupils: the generic extract_layer.py pixel-diff captured the AA fringe of the black eye with its gray transition RGB at full alpha (visible halo over tinted skin) and missed the white pupils because they were too close in colour to the cream-white face background.
  • New extract_face.py handles faces specifically: dark feature pixels become pure black with alpha = 255 − max(R,G,B) so AA fades to whatever's underneath; pupil whites are detected via erode + dilate inside the dark cluster (centres only — no cream face leakage) and forced fully opaque white. Tunable thresholds (dark_max_rgb=180, white_min_rgb=248, pupil_erosion_px=1, pupil_dilation_px=1).

3 new face overlays

  • Sleepy / Calm: smooth closed-eyelid arches with eyelashes + small calm mouth. Quiet thoughtful vibe.
  • Sharp / Serious: angular narrow black eyes with thin pupil glints + slight scowl. Warrior / commander look.
  • Big Grin: oversized round anime eyes with sparkle highlights + open pink-tongued grin + scattered sparkle particles for the excited / delighted vibe.
  • All four styles re-extracted with the fixed face extractor — pupils opaque, no edge halo at any of the 6 skin tones.

Face style picker in Character Studio

  • 4 buttons (Classic · Sleepy · Sharp · Big Grin) under the skin tone palette. Click to live-swap the face overlay.
  • Lazy-load: all 4 face PNGs fetched in parallel with the base when the studio first opens. Status line now reports Ready · 5 layers loaded.
  • Swatches and face buttons share the same active-state styling (gold border on selection).

v0.25.72 Layered avatar system — ludo.ai sprite pipeline + Character Studio (press Q)

First step toward a MapleStory-style customizable character. Ships a runtime layer compositor (toggle with Q) backed by ludo.ai-generated overlays. Each visual layer (face, hair, top, etc.) is a transparent PNG anchored to a canonical neutral mannequin base. Skin tones are tinted at runtime via canvas multiply blend so any RGB colour works.

Pipeline — edit + extract + neutralize

  • Canonical base: faceless chibi mannequin (3/4 front-turned right, 4-tone cel-shaded, anatomically simplified). Generated via ludo.ai then background-removed for clean alpha. Saved to Sprites/character/layers/base/mannequin_base.webp.
  • Neutralized base: neutralize_skin.py converts the peach body fill to grayscale luminance while preserving the black manga-ink outline and alpha channel. Output at mannequin_base_neutral.webp — the runtime tinting target.
  • Layer extraction: extract_layer.py pixel-diffs a "mannequin + feature" composite against the bare mannequin to produce a transparent feature-only layer. Threshold-based, supports y-region masking. Used to extract the first face overlay (eyes + gentle smile) from a ludo edit.
  • Preview compose: preview_compose.py stacks layers in z-order for visual verification.

Character Studio — runtime compositor in maple_game.html

  • Self-contained module added at the bottom of the file (CSS + DOM + script). Zero coupling with existing player rendering — the in-game character is unchanged.
  • Toggle: Q opens / closes the studio overlay. Esc closes. Ignores keypresses while a text input is focused.
  • Compositor stacks four canvas operations: (1) draw neutralized mannequin → (2) multiply blend with the selected skin tone → (3) destination-in re-mask to the original alpha so transparent pixels stay transparent → (4) source-over draw the face overlay on top.
  • Skin tone palette: six swatches (Porcelain · Light · Tan · Olive · Brown · Deep). Click any to live-update the canvas. The black outline stays black under multiply (any × 0 = 0); the 4-tone shading variation tints proportionally to give natural-looking lit and shadowed skin in any colour.
  • Lazy-load: layers are fetched only on first open; the status line shows Loading… → Ready · 2 layers loaded.

Asset tree

Sprites/character/
├── extract_layer.py        # pixel-diff feature extractor
├── neutralize_skin.py      # colour → grayscale luminance for runtime tinting
├── preview_compose.py      # stacking verifier
└── layers/
    ├── base/
    │   ├── mannequin_base.webp           # canonical (peach default)
    │   └── mannequin_base_neutral.webp   # grayscale tinting target
    ├── eyes/anime_classic.webp           # eyes + gentle smile face overlay
    ├── face/   hair/   top/   bottom/    # ready for next batches
    └── glove/  shoe/   weapon/   hat/   cape/

v0.25.67 Curved-path stylish hair — spiky tufts + forelocks + side locks + glossy shine

Replaced the old flat pixel-rectangle hair with a proper layered curved-path system. Six layers compose into a stylish anime-chibi hair silhouette: back hair mass with form shadow, four spiky top tufts, three front fringe forelocks, two side-lock sweeps, the anime glossy shine band, and a crisp ink outline.

💇 Six layers in one block

  1. Back hair mass — quadratic-curve silhouette extending past the head circle for visible volume. Wider than the head with side-flow down to y=22. Right side gets a cc.hairDeep form-shadow wedge.
  2. Top spiky tufts — four angular peak triangles spaced across the top (x=4, 11, 19, 26). Centre tuft is tallest (-6 px), outer tufts shorter for natural variation. Each has a 2-tone inner highlight wedge using cc.hairHi.
  3. Front fringe forelocks — three teardrop strands hanging over the forehead (x=7, 15, 24). Centre forelock is longest (12-px tip). Each forelock casts a small cc.hairDeep shadow on the forehead.
  4. Side-lock sweeps — curved tendrils on each cheek. Left lock uses cc.hair with cc.hairHi stripe (lit side); right lock uses cc.hairDeep (form-shadow side).
  5. Glossy shine band — thin curved highlight in cc.hairHi2 hugging the top contour. Three crisp white peak pips at x=9, 15, 22 + a sparkle pip on the upper-left lit side.
  6. Ink outline — 1-px stroke in CUTE_PAL.outline following the silhouette's top + side curve for confident definition (matches the chick-sticker reference vocabulary).

🎨 Why curved paths instead of pixel rectangles

The previous hair was assembled from ctx.fillRect calls — straight edges only, blocky silhouette, no organic flow. Quadratic curves (quadraticCurveTo) give the silhouette real volume and let the four spiky tufts feel like they grew out of the same mass. Combined with the per-strand cel shadow on each forelock, the hair now reads as a layered structure with depth instead of a flat colour block.

🌈 Class palette compatibility

All six layers use existing cc.hair / cc.hairHi / cc.hairDeep / cc.hairHi2 tones from _ensureCelTones(). So:

  • Warrior — dark brown w/ amber highlights
  • Rogue — dark violet w/ lavender highlights
  • Mage — dark indigo w/ blue highlights
  • Archer — chestnut w/ warm amber highlights

All four classes get the same hair shape; only the palette differs.

What stays

  • v0.25.66 anime-chibi eyes (class-coloured iris + shine pips) — unchanged. The new hair sits behind the eyes naturally.
  • Hair bob animation (hb per-frame y-offset) — kept; all curves use the same hb so the entire silhouette bobs together.
  • Hat / helmet / cap rendering — drawn AFTER hair so equipment still overlaps cleanly.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.67. One block in drawCuteCharacter rewritten (~25 px-rect calls → ~50 path operations across 6 layers). +115 / −24 lines.
  • No save/network/protocol impact.

Adopting the chibi-anime visual vocabulary for the procedural character. The previous 2×3 black eye dots felt minimal next to the rest of the artwork. Replaced with proper anime eyes (iris + shine pips) and added expression variants for the mouth tied to player state.

🎨 Why this matches the reference vocabulary

The new render adopts those same building blocks WITHOUT copying the specific designs (different proportions, different palette, our own existing chibi silhouette).
  • The class-colour iris doubles as a build-identity signal — players reading the screen can tell their class from the eye colour even when the equipped gear obscures the body palette.
  • Expression variants tie the face to gameplay state, so the character "feels" what they're doing — surprised when hit, eager when buffed, relaxed when idle.

What stays

14 oaks scrolling at 0.14 — slightly slower than the existing pine treeline (0.18) so oaks read as one depth-step further back. Each tree:

🎨 Authoring notes

  • Original procedural art, no copyrighted reference. Captures the storybook side-scroller vibe with shapes + colours, not by tracing.

  • Themed biomes (Candy Canyon, Bubblegum Swamp, Pearl Bathhouse, Stardust Atrium, Honeycomb Hollow) draw their decor LAST, so their lollipops / lily pads / brass pipes / cosmic eggs / hex pillars sit in front. The new oaks + grass mounds compose underneath, adding depth without fighting the themed art.

v0.25.63 Distinct layouts per biome + low-gravity Stardust Atrium

User: "Could you make more variation to the monster maps, its all too similar." All five new biomes (Candy Canyon, Bubblegum Swamp, Pearl Bathhouse, Stardust Atrium, Honeycomb Hollow) used the same zigzag platform template — 10 main platforms + 4 small upper-tier puffs. Now each biome has its own distinct platform shape that matches the theme, plus Stardust Atrium gets low gravity as a unique movement gimmick.

🍭 Candy Canyon — mountain peak

Platforms ascend on the left, plateau at the marshmallow summit (two wide 280-px platforms at y=190), then descend on the right. Plus two lone overhead candy stalactites at y=120 for high-jump rewards. Reads as a candy mountain rather than a flat zig-zag.

🐸 Bubblegum Swamp — scattered lily-pad islands

Smaller platforms (80-90 px wide) with bigger gaps between them, requiring proper jump timing. Three pad clusters (3 pads tightly packed each) give safe footholds, separated by isolated stepping stones over the bubblegum water. Stair-step cluster on the right side for the final approach to the exit portal.

🛁 Pearl Bathhouse — stepped bath tiers

Three distinct elevation bands forming a multi-level Roman bath:

  • Lower tier (y=400) — long bath rim ledges on each side.
  • Mid tier (y=340) — wider 340-px middle bath ring.
  • Upper tier (y=270) — top bath landing (380-px platforms).
  • Top spire (y=180) — pearl chamber accessible from the upper tier (140 px wide).

Plus 4 small connector ledges between tiers so the player has stair-step access without needing the main platforms.

🌌 Stardust Atrium — floating islands + LOW GRAVITY

No connected staircase. Discrete celestial islands at varied altitudes, ranging from y=80 (top pinnacle) down to y=430. Tiny stepping stones in the centre at y=160-200 require precise jumps.

The new biome gets gravityMul: 0.55, re-using the existing gravity-multiplier system already used by Gravitos (which is gravityMul: 3, opposite end). Player jumps higher + falls slower in the atrium, creating a "drifting through space" feel where the wider gaps between platforms become reachable. Mobs + projectiles are also affected so the whole biome feels low-G.

🍯 Honeycomb Hollow — true hex pattern

Platforms arranged in a real honeycomb pattern: alternating offset rows with 110-px cells. Three full rows (bottom y=420, mid y=340, top y=260) + a 2-cell apex at y=180. The mid + top rows offset by half-cell-width to give that classic 6-sided packing. Reads as the inside of a giant beehive.

What stays

  • Biome decor renderers (lollipop trees, cattails, brass pipes, cosmic eggs, hex wall) all unchanged — they sit on top of the new layouts naturally.
  • Monster spawns + types per biome — same. Spawns adapt to wherever the new platforms are.
  • Old non-biome maps (forest, mushroom, ancient, sunsetBeach, duneSands, cryptHollow, skyGarden, frozenPeak, lavaCavern) — untouched. Only the five new biomes got reshaped.
  • Veteran scaling (v0.25.59) + monster skills (v0.25.58) + empowered tier (v0.25.53) — all compose normally with the new layouts.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.63. Five map blocks rewritten (each platforms array re-authored), gravityMul: 0.55 added to stardustAtrium. +95 / −62 lines.
  • No save/network/protocol impact. Existing saves keep their position; on entering the new layouts the player will spawn at the configured entry x and physics resolves them onto the nearest platform / ground.

v0.25.62 Bug fix — N key NPC dialogue (toggle, range, z-index, closeAllModals)

User: "when i press n to talk to npc the dialogue with npc does not pop up." Three real bugs in the N keybind path were stacking + a missing modal cleanup. Fixed all four. The most-likely cause of the user's report is the z-index issue — the NPC dialog had no z-index set, so any modal opened just before talking would visually cover it.

🐛 Bugs found

  1. Toggle-close mismatch. The N handler tried to close the dialog with display === 'flex' but openNPC sets display = 'block'. So pressing N a second time while the dialog was open did NOT close it — instead it fell through to the else branch and re-rendered the same dialog. (Not the user's symptom but related.)
  2. NPC detection range too tight. Was 60 px around the player. Town NPCs sit ~140 px apart, so the player effectively had to be standing on top of one to be detected. Widened to 80 px AND switched to closest-match instead of array-order first-match.
  3. Dialog z-index missing. #dialog had no z-index set. .modal-overlay sits at z:50. If any modal had been opened just before pressing N, the dialog would render BEHIND it — invisible to the user. Bumped to z:60.
  4. quest-modal not in closeAllModals. v0.25.61 added the new quest journal but didn't add it to the closeAllModals() id list. So pressing Esc or opening another dialog wouldn't close the journal cleanly.

🛠️ Fixes

  • Toggle: dlg.style.display === 'flex' → dlg.style.display && dlg.style.display !== 'none' (covers 'block' and 'flex').
  • Range: find(npc => Math.abs(pcx - npc.x) < 60) → loop over npcs and pick CLOSEST within 80 px.
  • Z-index: added z-index: 60 to #dialog.
  • closeAllModals() id list now includes 'quest-modal'.

What stays

  • NPC roles, dialogue trees, shop integration — all unchanged.
  • Press N behaviour: nearby chest → open it, nearby NPC → talk, otherwise → open Codex (unchanged priority).
  • v0.25.61 quest journal still toggles via J. The closeAllModals fix means pressing Esc now also closes the journal cleanly.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.62. Four small edits: #dialog CSS gains z-index, N keybind handler refactored (toggle + range + closest-match), closeAllModals id list gains quest-modal. +30 / −5 lines.
  • No save/network/protocol impact.

v0.25.61 Quest system — kill / visit / boss quests with rewards (press J)

User: "Could you add more rpg gaming elements." Built a lightweight quest framework. 12 starter quests across kill / visit / boss objectives, tracked via journal + auto-progressed via existing kill + map-load hooks, with mesos + EXP rewards on completion.

  • Three sections: 🎯 Active, 📋 Available, ✅ Completed.
  • Quests auto-unlock into "Available" when you reach the level requirement (toast pops on unlock so you know).
  • Click Accept to start a quest → moves to Active with progress tracking.
  • Click Abandon to drop an active quest (no penalty, can re-accept).

v0.25.60 Bug fix: slash duplicate at top diagonal · Warrior X gets a ground-slam finale

User: "Final action of warrior x skill character slams hard on the ground. Warrior x skill has a duplicate slash animation at the top diagonal of the screen." Two fixes: a long-standing render bug in drawSmoothFx that ghosted slashes when 2+ were alive in the same frame, and a new ground-slam coda for the Doombringer ult so the executioner's stroke actually feels final.

🐛 Bug — duplicate slash at top diagonal

Root cause in drawSmoothFx's slash branch:

ctx.translate(sx, fx.y);
ctx.rotate(fx.angle);
// ... draw arcs ...
ctx.setTransform(1,0,0,1,0,0);   // ← BUG: nukes outer transform

setTransform(identity) resets the entire matrix — including the HiDPI scale + camera transform that the outer drawSmoothFx's ctx.save() had preserved. After the first slash in a frame, every subsequent slash rendered at half-size at the top-left of the screen, looking like a "ghost" duplicate floating diagonally up.

This was invisible for skills that only spawn 1–2 slashes (basic melee, single-cast skills), but the Doombringer ult fires 5 staggered slashes over 600 ms with a 20-frame life each, so 2–4 slashes overlap every frame — the user reported the visible artefact there.

🛠️ Fix

Wrap the slash draw in proper ctx.save() / ctx.restore(). The outer transform survives, no more ghost slashes:

ctx.save();
ctx.translate(sx, fx.y);
ctx.rotate(fx.angle);
// ... draw arcs ...
ctx.restore();

Benefits every skill that spawns multiple spawnSmoothSlash() calls in the same frame — Doombringer's apoc, Phantom's chain, sword auto-attacks at high attack speed, etc.

⚔️ Warrior X — Doombringer ground-slam finale

The Blade of Calamity used to do 5 forward slashes and just… end. Added a coda that fires 900 ms after cast (right after the 5th slash settles):

  • Wide ground hitbox — 380 × 80 px centered on the player at ground line.
  • Damage — getAtk() × 3.5 with crit roll. Knocks every hit mob UP (vy −7) + AWAY from impact centre (vx ±7 by side).
  • Visuals — large smooth-explosion (220 px gold + amber edge), impact star-burst, 24-particle dust shockwave radiating along the ground, 18-particle vertical impact column rising from the slam point.
  • Feel — addShake(28) + flash(0.7) + addHitStop(220) + crit audio. Reads as a real executioner's stroke.
  • Invuln window bumped 900 ms → 1300 ms so the player isn't punished during the slam wind-up + shockwave.

📐 New ult timeline

TimeEvent
0 msCast — toast + initial shake/flash + sword silhouette particles spawn
0 msSlash 1 (forward, getAtk × 2.4)
150 msSlash 2
300 msSlash 3
450 msSlash 4
600 msSlash 5 (guaranteed crit)
900 msGROUND SLAM finale (getAtk × 3.5 wide AOE + shockwave)

What stays

  • Doombringer's existing 5 forward slashes — unchanged. The slam is additive, not a replacement.
  • Other warrior X variants (warlord_warcry, crusader_aegis, dragoon_skylance) — untouched.
  • The bug fix only changes the slash-render code path; non-slash smoothFx (explosion, beam, impact) were already wrapped correctly.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.60. Two edits: drawSmoothFx slash branch (save/restore wrap), doombringer_apoc (final scheduleSkillTimer at 900 ms). +76 / −2 lines.
  • No save/network/protocol impact.

v0.25.59 Veteran scaling — monster progression smoothly covers every level

User: "make the progression of monsters nicely cover close to every level." Map graph has gaps (Lv 9 → 15, Lv 22 → 30, Lv 30 → 40), so a player at Lv 26 had no fresh map to clear and old mobs felt trivial. Added a per-mob "natural level" table + veteran scaling at spawn time. Now every player level has appropriately-tuned encounters, even when revisiting an "old" map.

📊 Natural levels per mob type

TierMobNatural Lv
1snail1
1slime2
2mushroom3
2gummy / cookie4
2frog / axolotl5
3horny / orange / stump6 / 7 / 8
4scorpion / honeyBuzz / nougatBear12 / 14 / 16
5skeleton / mummy / zombie / wraith18 / 20 / 22 / 24
6nimbusFox / cosmicMochi30 / 32
7coralImp / pearlSprite38 / 42

⚔ Veteran scaling formula

When player level is above a mob's natural level, the gap drives a stat boost:

  • HP ×= 1 + gap × 0.030 capped at ×2.0
  • ATK ×= same
  • DEF ×= 1 + gap × 0.025 capped at ×2.0
  • EXP reward ×= 1 + gap × 0.030 capped at ×3.0 — old mobs stay worth farming
  • Mesos ×= 1 + gap × 0.025 capped at ×3.0
  • Mobs at +5 levels or more get a ⚔ name prefix so the player can see the over-tier marker.

📐 Examples — same mob at different player levels

Mob (natural Lv)Player LvHP after scaleATK after scale
snail (Lv 1, base HP 70)1709
snail (Lv 1)15~158 (×2.26 → cap 2.0 = 140)~18 (cap 18)
snail (Lv 1)50140 (cap)18 (cap)
mushroom (Lv 3, base HP 190)15258 (×1.36)30
wraith (Lv 24, base HP 970)301145 (×1.18)79
wraith (Lv 24)501722 (×1.78)119
coralImp (Lv 38, base HP 1400)401484 (×1.06)89

So a Lv 30 player wandering back through the Mushroom Hollow now meets a ⚔ Shroom with 1.36× HP and the same crit/EXP scale-up. Smooths the feel: any level you're at, the world has a fight that matches.

🛡️ Carve-outs

  • Bosses — skipped. King Slime / Mushmom / Aetherion / Gravitos / all Zodiac signs keep their authored stat curves.
  • Elite + miniboss — skipped, since their existing ×3 / ×5 HP multipliers already cover scaling. Stacking veteran on top would explode HP.
  • Empowered Lv 25+ candy/swamp tier from v0.25.53 — composes with veteran scaling. A Lv 30 player meets a Sugar Rush Gummy with empowered ×1.7 HP THEN ×1.78 veteran scale on top → ~3× base HP. The candy biome stays relevant deep into the late game.
  • Mini-gummy split spawns — the split path bypasses spawnMonster; mini-gummies stay at their fixed 60% size and base stats.

What stays

  • Map levelReq values — unchanged. Players still need to meet the gate to enter.
  • Visual sizing from v0.25.57 — composes naturally; over-tier mobs are also bigger.
  • Special skills from v0.25.58 — fire on the same cooldowns; the boosted ATK just makes the skill damage hit harder.
  • Loot drop rolls — unchanged. EXP / mesos scale with the formula above; equipment / chest drops untouched.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.59. New MOB_NATURAL_LEVEL config table, veteran-scaling block in spawnMonster() after the empowered hook. +50 / −1 lines.
  • No save/network/protocol impact. Existing saves keep their stored player level — the scaling is computed at spawn time so it kicks in immediately.

v0.25.58 High-tier monsters get signature special skills (groundStun, homingShot, poisonCloud, dashCharge)

User: "make high level monsters be able to have more unique skills like ground stun or shoot slow homing projectiles." Built a skill registry where each tier-4+ mob gets a signature special move on a long cooldown, separate from its basic m.shoot ranged attack. Four skill kinds shipped, each one assigned to two monster types so mid+late zones play differently.

⚔️ Four skill kinds

SkillMechanic
groundStunDrops a 35-frame telegraphed shockwave on the player's column. On pulse: damage + 0.7 s player hitStun if standing in the band. Visual ring expands during the telegraph; a flashing ! appears in the last 12 frames.
homingShotSlow projectile (~3 px/frame) with homing: true — re-uses the existing player-tracking steering logic in updateProjectiles (gentle 0.18 accel, capped at speed 5). Player can weave it but eating one stings.
poisonCloudLingering 4-second puddle hazard at the caster's feet. Ticks damage every 24 frames + applies a 1.8 s poison DoT. Stays put — area-denial, not chase.
dashChargeShort fast horizontal burst (vx ±8) toward the player. Sets m._dashCharging = 16 for a brief visual cue. Trail particles spawn behind.

👾 Monster assignments

MonsterSkillCooldown
mummy (Wrappy)groundStun5.5 s
wraith (Spook)homingShot4.0 s
zombie (Rotter)poisonCloud6.0 s
skeleton (Bones)dashCharge4.5 s
coralImp (Coralite)homingShot3.8 s
pearlSprite (Pearl Cherub)groundStun5.0 s
nimbusFox (Astrofox)dashCharge4.2 s
cosmicMochi (Mochi Galaxy)homingShot4.4 s

🛠️ How it's wired

  • New MONSTER_SKILLS config table maps monster type → {kind, cd}.
  • New MONSTER_SKILL_FNS object holds the four skill implementations. Each takes the casting monster m and pushes the appropriate hazard / projectile / state mutation.
  • updateMonsters per-frame loop: when MONSTER_SKILLS[m.type] exists, ticks m._mskTimer. On expiry checks player range (320 px x / 220 px y) + aggro target; if in range, fires the skill and resets cd with ±15% jitter so packs don't synchronize. Out-of-range short retry (600 ms) so the cd doesn't burn while the player is far.
  • Initial m._mskTimer stagger (0.5×–1.1× of base cd) so a freshly-spawned pack doesn't all cast simultaneously.
  • Two new hazard types in updateHazards:
    • mob_quake — pulses on life === 0, applies damage + player.hitStun = 700 + 14 outward particles. Despawns same tick.
    • mob_poisoncloud — ticks every 24 frames, applies damage + extends player._poisonTimer + player._poisonDmg (re-uses existing zodiac poison DoT system). 240-frame life. Bubbling particles.
  • Two new render branches in drawHazards:
    • mob_quake — concentric expanding ring on the ground in the casting mob's palette colour, plus a flashing ! in the final 12 frames.
    • mob_poisoncloud — two-tone green puddle gradient + 4 surface-bubble pips drifting upward via tick.

🛡️ Carve-outs

  • Bosses — skipped entirely. They have authored AI patterns (zodiac, Aetherion, Gravitos) — not interfered with.
  • Tier 1-3 mobs (snail, slime, mushroom, horny, orange, stump, scorpion, gummy, cookie, frog, axolotl, honeyBuzz, nougatBear) — no skill assigned. Stay simple for early progression.
  • Empowered Lv 25+ candy/swamp tier (v0.25.53) — keeps its own special powers (split, spread, venom puff, heal aura). Doesn't double-up with MONSTER_SKILLS since those types aren't in the new registry.
  • Skill cooldowns + skill triggers respect player.invulnerable — i-frames during dodge / parry still protect.

What stays

  • Existing m.shoot ranged attacks — unchanged. Skills are additive, not replacements.
  • Stun resist, def, evasion — apply normally.
  • Poison DoT system — re-used, not duplicated.
  • Player hitStun cap from tree.stunImmune trait — the big skill stun honors it (player.hitStun = Math.max(player.hitStun || 0, h.stun)).

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.58. New MONSTER_SKILLS + MONSTER_SKILL_FNS config blocks, per-frame skill cooldown hook in updateMonsters, two new hazard branches in updateHazards, two new render branches in drawHazards. +205 / −1 lines.
  • No save/network/protocol impact.

v0.25.57 Monsters vary in size + scale up with player level

User: "make monsters vary in size, if they are higher level make them bigger." Two factors compose into the spawn-time size multiplier so packs feel less clone-y AND high-level zones feel more imposing.

📏 New sizing factors

FactorRangeEffect
Per-spawn variance×0.92 → ×1.08 (±8%)Each spawned mob rolls a random size jitter. A pack of 5 slimes is now 5 distinct silhouettes.
Level scale×1.00 at Lv 1 → ×1.32 at Lv 41 (+0.8%/Lv, capped)Same monster type looks visibly more imposing at high level. Reads as "deeper into the game" without changing the underlying balance numbers.

📐 Combined examples

Player LvSlime base 34×28 → typical spawnCookie base 38×32 → typical spawn
Lv 1~31–37 × 26–30 px~35–41 × 29–35 px
Lv 25~37–43 × 31–36 px~42–48 × 35–40 px
Lv 50~41–48 × 34–40 px~46–53 × 39–46 px

🛡️ Carve-outs

  • Bosses (King Slime, Mushmom, Aetherion, Gravitos, all 12 Zodiac signs) — sizing untouched. Cinematic boss silhouettes stay consistent across runs.
  • Elite + miniboss multipliers compose with the new factors so they're still visibly larger relative to base mobs (×1.25 elite, ×1.6 miniboss layered on top).
  • Empowered Lv 25+ candy/swamp tier from v0.25.53 — sizing inherits naturally; an empowered "Sugar Rush" gummy at Lv 30 is bigger than a base gummy at Lv 5 thanks to the level scale.
  • Mini-gummy split spawns (from gummy split-on-death) keep their fixed 60% size override — the empowered split happens after the size logic so they still come out tiny.

🔧 Where it lives

Single block in spawnMonster():

const lvScale = isBoss ? 1 :
  (1 + Math.min(40, Math.max(0, (player ? player.level || 1 : 1) - 1)) * 0.008);
const variance = isBoss ? 1 : (0.92 + Math.random() * 0.16);
const sizeMul = (isBoss ? 1 : isMiniBoss ? 1.6 : isElite ? 1.25 : 1) * lvScale * variance;

sizeMul still feeds w: Math.floor(t.w * sizeMul) + h: Math.floor(t.h * sizeMul) as before. AI hitboxes scale with the visual silhouette automatically.

What stays

  • Stat scaling (HP / ATK / DEF / EXP / mesos) — unchanged. This is purely a visual sizing pass.
  • Per-monster authored proportions (snail's wide squat, frog's bulging eyes, axolotl's long body) — preserved through the scale.
  • v0.25.55 player attack halving still applies; combined with bigger silhouettes the kill-time feels more substantial at high level.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.57. One block in spawnMonster(). +13 / −2 lines.
  • No save/network/protocol impact.

v0.25.55 Halve player attack — monsters were dying too fast

User: "half all attack by main character, the monsters are dying too quickly." Done. Single-knob change: introduced a global PLAYER_ATK_MUL = 0.50 constant and applied it at the very end of getAtk(). Every player damage source — basic attacks (melee / arrow / dagger / bolt), all skills, all ultimates, pet/pack hits, milestone procs — pulls through this function, so the 50% nerf hits everything uniformly without touching individual skill formulas.

🔪 What's affected

  • All player damage — basic attacks, every skill, every ultimate, masteries, pet/pack hits.
  • Crit damage still works as a multiplier on top, just on a lower base.
  • Equipment ATK + STR/INT scaling + buffs (warCry, bloodlust, rampage, comboAtk, prestige dmgMult) still compose normally; the halve is the very last operation in the chain.

🛡️ What's not affected

  • Monster damage — unchanged. They hit just as hard as before.
  • Crit chance / accuracy / DEF / HP — unchanged.
  • Loot / EXP / mesos drops — unchanged. Time-to-kill goes up; reward per kill is the same.
  • Empowered Lv 25+ candy/swamp tier (v0.25.53) — unchanged. Their stat bumps + special powers stay; the player just chips away half as fast.

🎚️ Single tuning knob

Future rebalances tweak PLAYER_ATK_MUL in one spot near GLOBAL_SKILL_DMG_MUL. No need to edit every per-skill formula.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.55. New PLAYER_ATK_MUL constant, one multiplication added in getAtk()'s final return. +8 / −2 lines.
  • No save/network/protocol impact.

v0.25.53 Empowered tier — candy/swamp mobs gain special powers at Lv 25+

User: "Make monsters from bubblegumSwamp and candyCanyon stronger higher level for above level 25 make them have special powers." Each of the four candy/swamp residents now spawns as an upgraded variant once the player crosses Lv 25, with bigger stats AND a unique flavoured special power per type.

📈 Empowered stats (vs base)

MobVariantHPATKDEFEXP / Mesos
gummySugar Rush Gummibeau×1.7×1.50×1.3×1.6
cookieCrumbling Choco-chip×1.7×1.55×1.4×1.7
frogVenom Pondhop×1.6×1.60×1.3×1.7
axolotlMystic Lottie×1.9×1.50×1.5×1.8

✨ Special powers (per type)

  • Sugar Rush Gummy — split-on-death. When killed, spits out two Mini Gummibeaus (60% size, faster, weaker, can't chain-split). Pink burst particles + a small camera shake sell the split. Mini-gummies are still farmable for mastery but give 30% reward each.
  • Crumbling Choco-chip — fires a 3-shot mspore spread per ranged volley instead of a single shot. The angular fan is computed inline by passing an angleOffset to fireMonsterProjectile (-0.40 / 0 / +0.40 rad). Shoot cooldown also tightened 2300 → 1500 ms.
  • Venom Pondhop — passive venom-puff barrage. Every ~1.6 s within 280 px range, emits a homing toxic projectile (mtoxic colour, 2.2 s poison) that stacks ON TOP of the standard mtoxic shot. Shoot cd also tightened 2600 → 1700 ms; jump bumped 8 → 11.
  • Mystic Lottie — heal aura. Every 28 frames regens 1.8% of own maxHp AND heals nearby empowered allies (radius 110 px) by 60% of that tick. Renders a 6-particle pink pulse ring on tick so the player can see the aura is firing. The biggest HP pool of the four (×1.9) plus the regen makes Mystic axolotls the priority kill in any pack.

🛠️ How it's wired

  • New EMPOWERED_TIER config table — per-type stat multipliers + flag name + name prefix. Lives next to monsterTypes.
  • spawnMonster — after the base mob is pushed, if player.level >= 25 AND type is in EMPOWERED_TIER AND mob isn't elite/mini/boss, applies the multipliers + flag. Same type string so mastery / bestiary doesn't fragment.
  • fireMonsterProjectile(m, angleOffset) — gained an optional radians-offset parameter that rotates the aim vector before normalisation. 3-shot spread is one call site, no duplicated trajectory math.
  • updateMonsters per-frame loop — added two empowered hooks alongside the existing m.shoot + burnTimer blocks: venom puff (frog) and heal aura (axolotl). Both gated on m._empoweredVenom / m._empoweredAura.
  • killMonster — new top-of-function check for m._empoweredSplit && !m._isMiniSplit. Pushes 2 mini-gummy entries directly into game.monsters with the _isMiniSplit flag so they bypass the empower-on-spawn check (no recursive splitting).

What didn't change

  • Below Lv 25 — mobs spawn at base stats, no empower applied. Early players keep the existing curve.
  • Elite / mini-boss / boss tiers — those existing modifiers compose with the base stats; empowered tier is skipped for them since they already buff their own way.
  • Bestiary / mastery — empowered mobs share the same type string as base so kill counts pool.
  • Loot tables, projectile sprites, AI patterns — all reused from base. Only the multipliers + special-power hooks are new.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.53. New: EMPOWERED_TIER table, spawn hook, special-power hooks in updateMonsters + killMonster, angleOffset param on fireMonsterProjectile. +126 / −5 lines.
  • No save/network/protocol impact. Existing saves keep their stored state — empower applies on spawn, not retroactively.

v0.25.52 Taxi: Candy Canyon + Bubblegum Swamp listable without prior visit

User: "make the taxi able to teleport to these maps." The taxi was already capable of routing to any visited non-boss map, but new players hadn't walked to the Candy Canyon or Bubblegum Swamp yet — so the new biomes weren't appearing in the destination list. Added a taxiAccessible: true map flag that lets a map opt into the taxi list regardless of visit state.

🛠️ Implementation

  • MAPS.candyCanyon + MAPS.bubblegumSwamp now carry taxiAccessible: true.
  • renderTaxi() rewritten to merge two sources for the destination list:
    1. All map IDs in game.visitedMaps (the prior behaviour).
    2. Any map ID where MAPS[id].taxiAccessible === true (the new opt-in).
    Both sources are de-duped via a Set and then filtered to exclude boss arenas (so players still have to earn boss fights).

🚕 What you get

  • Open the Taxi panel from anywhere outside a boss arena.
  • Sweet Candy Canyon and Bubblegum Swamp appear as destinations on a fresh save — no need to walk through Mushroom → Candy Canyon → Bubblegum Swamp first.
  • Standard 50 Lumen fare applies (matches every other taxi destination).
  • Existing taxi UX kept: arrival toast, lumens deducted, you spawn at x = 200 facing right.

📋 Future-proofing

Any future biome can opt into taxi-without-visit by adding a single taxiAccessible: true field to its MAPS entry. No rendering changes needed.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.52. Three edits: the two flags on the candy / swamp map blocks, and the destination-merge logic in renderTaxi. +12 / −2 lines.
  • No save/network/protocol impact. Existing game.visitedMaps persistence unchanged — the new flag is read-only state, not stored per-save.

v0.25.49 Head shading — hard-edged 2-tone cel matching chick reference

User attached a chick sticker reference and asked for the head to match its style. The reference is classic flat mobile-game cel: solid base + ONE hard-edged darker crescent + ONE small crisp white pip. v0.25.42's radial gradients were too painterly for that vocabulary — replaced with hard-edged shape arithmetic.

🔪 Why hard-edged this time

The chick reference has zero gradients. The shadow boundary is a CRISP curved line, not a soft falloff. The specular is a single small egg shape with no halo, no secondary pip, no gradient. v0.25.42's radial-gradient form shadow + 3-stack specular + rim light was the right call for the previous painterly reference, but it's the wrong call here.

🛠️ New head shading (3 layers, all clipped to head circle)

  1. Form shadow — single hard-edged crescent on the bottom-right. Drawn as head circle minus a shifted "lit moon" circle (centre offset up-and-left by hr × 0.42). The fill operation paints only the crescent, giving an exact crisp boundary. Tone is CUTE_PAL.skinShd — the same dark skin colour used elsewhere.
  2. Chin cast shadow — hard-edged ellipse at the jaw, same skinShd tone, no falloff. Sells "head sits on body" without softening the cel look.
  3. Specular — single small white pip (hr × 0.18 × 0.11 ellipse, tilted -0.30 rad) on upper-left. #ffffff opaque, no halo, no secondary pip, no gradient.

🚫 What's gone (v0.25.42 features deleted)

  • Radial-gradient form shadow (skinDeep → skinShd → transparent stops).
  • SSS warm-pink radial wash at the lit/shadow seam.
  • 2-stack chin shadow with outer purple-tinged 32% band.
  • 3-stack glossy specular (halo + body + crisp core).
  • Tiny secondary "wet sheen" pip floating above the spec.
  • 2-stop warm rim light crescent on the bottom-right.

None of these read at chick-sticker scale + style. Removed in favour of the cleaner three-layer pass.

📐 The crescent trick

ctx.fillStyle = CUTE_PAL.skinShd;
ctx.beginPath();
ctx.arc(hcx, hcy, hr, 0, Math.PI * 2);                              // outer
ctx.arc(hcx - hr * 0.42, hcy - hr * 0.42, hr, Math.PI * 2, 0, true); // inner (CCW)
ctx.closePath();
ctx.fill();

Drawing two arcs in opposite directions inside the same path creates an even-odd fill region — the lit "moon" is excluded so only the shadow crescent renders. Crisp boundary at the intersection of the two circles, exactly the curve the reference shows.

What stays

  • Head outline ring (2 px black halo).
  • Skin base fill (CUTE_PAL.skin).
  • Hair, eyes, mouth, blush — drawn AFTER the shading on top.
  • Torso / arm / leg / boot 4-tone shading from v0.25.41.
  • Equipment 3-tone polish from v0.25.48 (cape, hats, blades, bow, staff).

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.49. One block in drawCuteCharacter rewritten (head shading). +27 / −80 lines (net negative — three crisp layers replace six gradient layers).
  • No save/network/protocol impact.

Bumped each tier of the per-level multiplier so the late game actually grinds, without making the early levels feel punishing.

Initial expToNext also bumped from 100 → 120 so the very first level-up takes ~20% longer too.

Front-loaded onto the late game on purpose: L10 is essentially the same pace, L20 a tiny bit slower, but L40+ properly walls. A run that used to clear to L50 in ~1 hr will now take 3-4 hrs of dedicated kill clearing — or you can prestige earlier and use the +30%/+30%/+1AP per ascension to outpace the wall over multiple runs.

  • Player init: expToNext: 100 → 120.
  • Prestige reset: same bump.

What stays

  • Phase / advancement gates — JOB at L25, MASTER at L50. Slot unlock thresholds slotLevelReq() unchanged.
  • Per-kill EXP rewards untouched. The math pushes the curve up; the EXP income stays the same.
  • Press-8 dev XP burst (+40% expToNext) — still works, just gives smaller fractional jumps at high levels because the bar is bigger.
  • Prestige multipliers (+30% xpMult per ascension) — unchanged. Multi-prestige players will feel the new wall less.

Touched surface

  • No save/network/protocol impact. Existing saves keep their stored expToNext; the new curve only kicks in on the next level-up.

v0.25.46 Zodiac bosses harder + Scorpio burrow bug fixed

User: "make the horoscope bosses mechanism harder to fight, scorpio has a bug in which it buries underground." Two-part patch: a global zodiac difficulty buff, and a complete rework of Scorpio's burrow attack so it stops getting stuck below the floor.

🐛 Scorpio burrow bug — root cause

The old burrow mutated m.y += 3 / m.y -= 4 per AI tick while the standard monster-physics block kept applying gravity (m.vy += 0.5) and clamping to platforms. The two systems fought each other: gravity accumulated faster than the AI's m.y -= 4 rise, so Scorpio could "miss" the surface during the rise phase and end up at m.y > 1000 after a few cycles — visually buried, mechanically stuck. The platform-collision gate (entity.y + entity.h < p.y + p.h + 20) only triggers if the boss is just intersecting the ground from above; once the boss's bottom passes the ground's bottom, the clamp stops engaging and the boss falls forever.

🛠️ Burrow rework

  • New m._noGravity flag in the boss physics block — when set, the monster-physics gravity + collision-clamp + position update is skipped entirely. AI drives m.x and m.y directly. Velocities zeroed each tick so they can't accumulate during the suspension.
  • Captures m._burrowGroundY on entry so the surface y is known. All sink/travel/erupt/settle phases use absolute targets relative to it (no more += 3 drift).
  • 4-phase state machine with bounded timers:
    • 0 – 250 ms — SINK: slide 60 px down into the ground, dust particles spit upward.
    • 250 – 800 ms — TRAVEL: smooth chase to player x at 6%/tick lag. Phase 2/3 emit a violet/pink ground-warning column at the boss's column so the player can read where the eruption hits.
    • 800 – 1000 ms — ERUPT: snap upward 70 px, fire a 3/5/7-shot venom geyser at phase 1/2/3 (was 3 flat).
    • 1000 – 1300 ms — SETTLE: hold at groundY, drop the noGravity + invuln flags, reset _erupted, return to idle.
  • New m._invulnBurrow flag — set during the underground portion of the burrow. hitMonster() checks this flag and shows a BURROWED miss tag instead of dealing damage, so players get visual feedback instead of phantom-hitting empty air.

🔪 Zodiac difficulty buff

StatOldNew
HP15600 + 5850 × order19500 + 7300 × order (~+25 / +28%)
ATK80 + 9 × order95 + 11 × order (~+18 / +24%)
DEF16 + 2 × order20 + 3 × order (~+25 / +50%)
Evasion140 + 8 × order160 + 10 × order
EXP reward5800 + 1380 × order6800 + 1620 × order
Mesos reward4000 + 920 × order4700 + 1080 × order

Loot/EXP scale up with HP so the time-to-clear ratio stays roughly constant — fights are tougher, but the reward per hour holds.

🎯 Tighter generic AI

  • _zodiacAiGeneric cycle reduced 1800/1200/800 ms → 1450/950/650 for phase 1/2/3.
  • Drift cap raised 2.0 → 2.2, acceleration 0.06 → 0.07, so the boss closes distance faster.
  • Volley count pushed to 5/5/7 shots (was 5 flat). Phase-3 shots also do +17% damage and arc wider for the wedge spread.

🦂 Scorpio-specific buffs

  • Idle cycle 1700/1100/700 → 1500/950/600 ms. Burrow chance 40% → 50%.
  • Sting volley 3 shots flat → 3 / 5 / 5 per phase, with phase-3 venom doing +15% damage and 50% longer poison DoT (4500 → 5000 ms).
  • Burrow eruption volley 3 / 5 / 7 shots, phase-3 venom +20% damage and 5000 ms poison DoT.

What didn't change

  • Other zodiac AI handlers (Aries / Taurus / Gemini / Cancer / Leo / Virgo / Libra / Sagittarius / Capricorn / Aquarius / Pisces) — unchanged. They get harder via the global stat buff but their bespoke patterns stay.
  • Phase thresholds — still 66% / 33% HP. Three phases, each more aggressive.
  • Standard AI / non-zodiac boss code — unchanged.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.46. Edits in 5 places: zodiac stat block, generic AI fallback, scorpio AI handler, monster-physics gate, hitMonster invuln check. +143 / −47 lines.
  • No save/network/protocol impact.
