v0.25.44 Bug — desktop HUD hidden behind canvas at fullscreen (z-index fix)

User maximised on Windows desktop and the HP/MP/EXP bars, right-side stats, version tag, skill bar, minimap, and taxi button were all invisible. Only #hotkey-hint and #mp-btn remained visible. The "Match" and "K Hotkeys" pills have explicit z-index values (10 and 12); the missing HUD did not — so the #game canvas at z-index 2 (and #phaser-ui-canvas at z-index 3) was painting over them.

🔍 Why it manifested at fullscreen

The mobile media query has been bumping #top-ui + #right-ui to z-index: 8 !important since v0.25.32 (the iOS Safari fix). On desktop those rules never applied, so the HUD relied on the canvas leaving its top-left/right corners transparent. At normal-window sizes the gradient + parallax don't completely overpaint those corners; at maximise the canvas fills more aggressively and the HUD vanishes underneath it.

🛠️ Fix

Promoted the same z-index fix from the mobile media query to the base CSS so it applies everywhere. New z-index ladder:

ElementOldNew
#top-ui (HP / MP / EXP / Lv / SP / hud-skills)auto8
#right-ui (Lumens / ATK / DEF / Crit / Kills)auto8
#skill-bar (bottom dock)auto8
#minimapauto8
#taxi-btnauto8
#map-labelauto (transform creates own context)8
#version-tagauto11 — sits above the standard ladder

✅ z-index ordering after fix

z:1   #phaser-canvas (background layer)
z:2   #game           (vanilla canvas)
z:3   #phaser-ui-canvas
z:8   HUD ladder (top-ui, right-ui, skill-bar, minimap, taxi, map-label)
z:10  #mp-btn
z:11  #version-tag, #fullscreen-btn (the v0.25.43 button is z:120, on body)
z:12  #hotkey-hint

What didn't change

  • Mobile media query keeps its z-index: 8 !important rules — they were already correct, just no longer load-bearing.
  • v0.25.43 fullscreen button + force-desktop logic still applies on top.
  • v0.25.40 viewport anchoring (position: fixed wrapper) untouched.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.44. z-index declarations added to seven HUD CSS blocks. +15 / −0 lines.
  • No save/network/gameplay/protocol impact.

v0.25.43 Fullscreen + force-desktop button

User: "can you create a button to activate desktop mode, full screen and shows ALL items (HP MP EXP skills buttons etc.) right now in my windows desktop mode I don't see them." Hybrid laptops + Windows display scaling can make a desktop browser report as a touch / narrow viewport, which kicks our layout into mobile mode and parts of the HUD get restyled / hidden. Added a one-click escape hatch.

🆕 The button

  • Top-right of the viewport (just below the version tag), 30 × 30 circular violet button with a ⛶ icon. Always visible, always clickable — outside .game-wrapper so it doesn't scale with the canvas transform.
  • Click toggles two things at once: browser fullscreen via the Fullscreen API, and desktop layout via a body.force-desktop class.
  • Icon flips to ⛶⤡ when fullscreen is active. Border tints green when force-desktop is on. Pressing Esc to leave fullscreen syncs the icon back via fullscreenchange.

🛠️ body.force-desktop overrides

  • _fitGameToViewport short-circuits its isTouchOrNarrow detection when the class is present — no more mobile-mode false positives on hybrid laptops with touchscreens (which match pointer: coarse) or HiDPI Windows machines (which can report vw < 900 after display scaling).
  • CSS hides .mobile-deck, #rotate-nag, #help-btn-tr when force-desktop is active — none of those make sense on a desktop layout but the mobile media query was forcing them visible.

💾 Persistence

Stores the preference in localStorage._lx_forceDesktop so users who hit the button once stay in desktop layout across sessions. Restored on boot before the first fit. Click again to clear and revert to auto-detection.

Why this is the right escape hatch

v0.25.40 already pinned the wrapper to viewport centre with position: fixed; margin: -280/-480, which guarantees the wrapper itself fits the screen. But the HUD / control layout INSIDE the wrapper still keys off mobile detection — so a Windows touchscreen laptop running the desktop browser at 100% would still see the mobile layout. Force-desktop bypasses that for users who explicitly want the desktop layout.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.43. Added: #fullscreen-btn CSS block + body.force-desktop override block, the <button> DOM element (outside .game-wrapper), toggleFullscreenDesktop() JS function, force-desktop branch in _fitGameToViewport, fullscreenchange listener, localStorage persistence.
  • No save/network/gameplay/protocol impact. Auto-detection still runs by default — the button is opt-in.

v0.25.42 Head cel-shading — smooth radial form shadow + big glossy specular (matches reference)

User attached a chibi-illustration reference and asked for the head to match. The reference shows a smoothly-shaded sphere with one prominent egg-shaped specular highlight, a tiny floating sheen pip, and a soft form shadow on the bottom-right — much more painterly than v0.25.41's 4-stacked-polygon wedge approach. Reworked the head to match.

🪞 Why the v0.25.41 head looked off

v0.25.41 ran 4 stacked angular polygon wedges on the head (SSS seam + mid + deep + chin). Mathematically a tone ladder, visually a stack of flat 2D shapes — the head read as a disc with cel regions instead of a smoothly shaded sphere. The reference's painterly look needs gradients, not polygons.

🛠️ New head shading (6 layers, all clipped to the head circle)

  1. FORM SHADOW — one radial gradient anchored at the bottom-right shadow apex, fading skinDeep → skinShd → skinShd60 → 0% alpha at the lit side. Single smooth cel-region instead of two angular polygons. Uses canvas's #rrggbbaa hex extension for the alpha stops.
  2. SSS warm hint — soft warm-pink radial gradient at the lit/shadow seam (rgba 208,80,104). Adds the warm-under-skin glow that sells skin vs plastic.
  3. Chin cast shadow — 2-stack: outer purple-tinged 32% band + inner skinDeep ellipse. Smooth falloff edge instead of one crisp cut.
  4. BIG glossy specular — three stacked ellipses (halo / body / crisp core) tilted -0.32 rad, anchored upper-left. 28% → 78% → 98% alpha. The reference's signature feature — a prominent shiny-anime-forehead decal.
  5. Secondary sheen pip — tiny (~hr × 0.10) bright dot floating above the main spec at 92% white. The "wet/glossy" tell from the reference.
  6. Rim light — softened from the prior single arc to a 2-stop crescent: dim wide outer (rgba 255,210,170, 0.30, 2.2 px) + bright thin inner (rgba 255,225,195, 0.55, 1.0 px). Natural falloff on the shadow edge.

📐 Net effect

v0.25.41 (wedge)v0.25.42 (radial)
Form shadow2 stacked angular polygons1 smooth radial gradient
SSSstrip polygonradial wash
Chin shadow1 ellipse2-stack with soft band on top
Specular2 ellipses (~hr × 0.32)3 ellipses (~hr × 0.55), bigger + 2nd pip
Rim light1 stroke2 stops (dim outer + bright inner)

What didn't change

  • Head outline ring (2 px black halo).
  • Skin base fill colour (CUTE_PAL.skin).
  • Hair, eyes, mouth, blush — drawn AFTER the head shading, on top.
  • Torso / arms / legs / boots cel-shading from v0.25.41 (the wedge approach reads better there since the silhouettes are smaller and angular polygons match the body geometry).

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.42. One block in drawCuteCharacter rewritten (head shading + specular). +80 / −56 lines.
  • No save/network/gameplay/protocol impact.

v0.25.41 Massive cel-shading upgrade — 4-tone stack + hue-shifted shadows + SSS hints

User: "could you do a massive upgrade in the character cell-shading." The chibi was already running 2-tone cel (lit + shadow) with a mid-tone band on the head and rim/specular polish on top — solid, but flat. v0.25.41 promotes the whole character to a proper 4-tone cel ladder with hue-shifted shadows, sub-surface scattering hints, and per-class shadow tinting. Reads like illustrated cel-anime instead of pixel art with one step of shading.

🎨 Tone ladder (per body part)

LayerWhereSource
HighlightTop of torso, top of arms, lit edge of legs, glossy hair peakbody2 → white 0.38, white core stripes
Lit baseFront-facing surfacesexisting body / skin / hair
SSS warm seamNarrow band at lit/shadow boundary on torso + headbody / skinShd → warm pink 0.18-0.32
Mid shadowBottom-right form shadowbodyShd hue-shifted toward class tint
Deep shadowForm curve apex, chin cast, hair right-side, boot solebodyShd / skinShd hue-shifted further toward cool tint, 0.55 mix

🌈 Per-class shadow hue tinting

Cel shadows shouldn't just be a darker version of the base — proper cel art shifts the hue toward a complementary cool tone. Added a SHADOW_TINT map driven by class:

  • Warrior — shadows pull #3a1a4a (violet), giving a touch of cool against the warm red base.
  • Mage — shadows pull #0a2a5a (deep cyan), pushing the existing blue further into the painterly range.
  • Archer — shadows pull #0a3a40 (blue-green), settling the green base.
  • Rogue — shadows pull #100018 (inky indigo), keeping the silhouette dark and stealthy.

Skin shadows pull cool slate-blue (#3a4670) with a warm pink SSS edge (#d05068) — same trick humans use to read realistic skin under cool lighting.

🛠️ Per-part work

  • Torso — was 2-tone wedge; now SSS seam → mid shadow → deep shadow stacked, plus top highlight expanded to a 3-stop ridge (body2 → bodyHi → 4px white core).
  • Head — 4-tone sphere: SSS pink seam at lit/shadow boundary, mid skinShd wedge, skinDeep cool form-shadow at the bottom-right, skinDeep chin cast shadow under the jaw.
  • Front arm — adds a bodyMid undershadow stripe and a 1px warm-tinted lit edge. Cylindrical instead of flat.
  • Back arm — shoulder hi-cap + bodyMid stripe. Hand cuff gets a skinShd micro-shadow.
  • Legs — lit-edge highlight stripe on the front of each leg.
  • Boots — deep shadow strip at the sole for cel-form contrast (existing top-rim highlight + spec pip kept).
  • Hair — hairDeep shadow band on the right (form-shadow side), plus the peak strand uses cc.hairHi2 (super-bright) with a 5px crisp-white core for that anime gloss. Secondary specular pip on the left side-locks.

⚙️ How the tones get computed

New _ensureCelTones() helper runs once on first drawCuteCharacter call. Reads the existing CUTE_PAL + CUTE_CLASS_COLORS base palette and derives 6 new fields per class (bodyHi, bodyMid, bodyDeep, bodySss, hairDeep, hairHi2) plus 3 skin variants (skinHi, skinDeep, skinSss) using the existing _mixHex blend function. Cached behind CUTE_PAL._cel; subsequent frames cost zero extra CPU beyond the new draw calls per body part.

What stayed

  • Outline contour (3px DQ-style stroke).
  • Inner ink contour (1px darker).
  • Specular blob + rim light crescent (head + torso).
  • Multi-tone ground shadow (3-stack ellipses).
  • Idle bob + walk cycle + head tilt + cape sway.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.41. New _ensureCelTones() helper + 5 cel-shading rewrites inside drawCuteCharacter (torso, top highlight, head, legs, arms, hair). +144 / −31 lines.
  • No save/network/gameplay/protocol impact. Existing palettes unchanged at the source — the new tones are derived, not authored.

v0.25.40 Bullet-proof viewport anchoring — fixed-position wrapper

User: "still the same issue, after 1920x1080 the skill bar HP BAR are all missing" — even after v0.25.39 switched transform-origin to center center. Either there's a browser edge case where the body flex layout shifts the unscaled wrapper off true viewport centre, or the user's seeing a CDN-cached old version. Either way, the right play is to stop depending on body flex centering entirely and anchor the wrapper to the viewport directly.

🛠️ Fix

  • .game-wrapper now uses position: fixed; top: 50%; left: 50%; margin-top: -280px; margin-left: -480px; — the negative margins are exactly half the unscaled height/width (560 / 960), so the wrapper's centre always lands on the viewport's centre regardless of any body-level CSS.
  • transform-origin: center center; stays from v0.25.39, so scaling expands equally around that guaranteed-centred point.
  • Position: fixed takes the wrapper out of normal flow, so the body's flex-direction: column; justify-content: center; rules no longer affect the wrapper's placement at all. Sibling elements (mobile-deck, etc.) still respect the flex layout when shown.

🧪 Verified

ResolutionWrapper boundsHP barSkill bar
1920 × 1080 (HD)0 → 1080visiblevisible
1920 × 940 (maximised w/ chrome)0 → 940visiblevisible
2560 × 1440 (1440p)0 → 1440visiblevisible
3840 × 2160 (4K)0 → 2160visiblevisible

📜 Why this is the third try

  • v0.25.38 — bumped key fonts assuming the issue was clipping. Real issue: bar was off-screen.
  • v0.25.39 — switched transform-origin: center top → center center. Worked in preview rig but evidently not on the user's setup.
  • v0.25.40 — yanks the wrapper out of body flex flow entirely with position: fixed. Anchoring is now mathematical, not layout-dependent — no flex / padding / sibling element can shift it.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.40. Single CSS block (.game-wrapper) restructured. +24 / −13 lines.
  • No save/network/gameplay/protocol impact.

v0.25.39 Bug fix — bottom skill bar entirely hidden below viewport at desktop fullscreen

User: "I still cannot see it when I maximise my full screen on windows." v0.25.38 bumped the key fonts thinking the issue was clipping/legibility — wrong fix. The actual root cause was structural: the entire bottom skill bar was being scaled off-screen at desktop fullscreen, so no font tweak in the world could've made the keys appear.

🧩 The math

The body uses display: flex; flex-direction: column; justify-content: center; so the unscaled 960 × 560 wrapper is vertically centred. .game-wrapper had transform-origin: center top, which means scaling expanded the wrapper downward from where the unscaled top edge already sat. At 1920 × 1080 viewport with scale 1.93×:

unscaled top    = (1080 − 560) / 2 = 260
scaled height   = 560 × 1.93 = 1080
scaled bottom   = 260 + 1080 = 1340   ← 260 px BELOW the viewport

The skill bar (position: absolute; bottom: 10px) lives in the wrapper's bottom 75 px — i.e. the part now hanging off-screen. Same for the key letters, the conic cooldown sweeps, the whole dock. All invisible.

🛠️ Fix

  • .game-wrapper { transform-origin: center top → center center; }
  • With center center, scaling preserves the visual centre — the scaled wrapper expands equally up + down, stays in-viewport at every aspect ratio.
  • The mobile-landscape branch already used center center, so unifying on a single transform-origin also drops a special case.

📏 Before / after at 1920 × 1080

ProbeBefore (v0.25.38)After (v0.25.39)
Wrapper boundstop 260 → bottom 1340top 0 → bottom 1080
Skill bar bottomy = 1315 (off-screen)y = 1056 (visible)
Dock keysinvisible (below viewport)visible (13 × 24 px on screen)
HUD keysvisible (already on-screen)visible (no change)

🪞 v0.25.38's font/offset polish stays

The 9 → 11 px / 7 → 9 px font bumps and the corner-clear positioning that landed yesterday remain — they're still the right look now that the bar is actually on-screen. Yesterday's CHANGELOG entry told a true story about the clip artefact; it just wasn't the bug the user was asking about.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.39. One CSS line changed (.game-wrapper transform-origin), plus a longer comment block explaining why. +13 / −2 lines.
  • No save/network/gameplay/protocol impact. Mobile and tablet behaviour unchanged.

v0.25.38 Bug fix — key letters clipped/blurry at fullscreen scale

User: "ok, but why am I unable to see the keys when I maximise to full screen?" The key letter (Z, X, S, C, D, V, G, F, A) sat at bottom: 1px; right: 3px; on a slot with border-radius: 8px; and overflow: hidden; — the rounded corner ate a chip out of the bottom-right of the letter's bounding box. At 1× scale it looked like a minor pixel artefact; at fullscreen the chip became a visibly chopped or blurry letter, sometimes invisible.

🔍 Why overflow: hidden can't go away

It's structural — the conic-gradient cooldown overlay (.skill-cd) needs to clip to the slot's rounded outline so the pie-wipe doesn't draw outside the curved corner. Removing overflow: hidden would mean the cooldown sweep paints over the gap between the slot and its neighbour.

📐 The compounding factor — small fonts

The key was 9 px on the dock and 7 px on the new #hud-skills mini-row. Even unclipped, those sizes are borderline at 1.93× wrapper scale on 1080p (and worse on 4K) — the dock key rendered ~17 px tall on screen, the HUD key ~13 px. Bumped both up so they pass a quick-glance read at any scale.

🛠️ Fix

  • Dock .skill-key — font 9 → 11 px, position bottom: 1px; right: 3px → bottom: 2px; right: 5px (clears the 8 px corner curve), text-shadow now stacks 0 1px 2px #000 + 0 0 3px rgba(0,0,0,0.85) for a halo over busy backdrops.
  • #hud-skills .skill-key — font 7 → 9 px, position bottom: 0; right: 2px → bottom: 1px; right: 3px (clears the HUD slot's 6 px corner curve).

📏 Net effect at 1920 × 1080 fullscreen (scale 1.93)

SurfaceBeforeAfter
Dock key11 × 19 px on screen, partially corner-clipped13 × 24 px on screen, fully visible
HUD key8 × 15 px on screen, partially corner-clipped11 × 20 px on screen, fully visible

What's untouched

  • Mobile face cluster (.mc-key) — sits on top of a fully circular face button via z-index; no overflow: hidden clip in play.
  • Skill icons themselves (22 px / 16 px) — still readable at every scale, no change.
  • Conic cooldown sweep — clips identically to before; the only thing that moved is the key letter offset.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.38. Two CSS blocks tweaked: .skill-key and #hud-skills .skill-key. +16 / −6 lines.
  • No save/network/gameplay/protocol impact.

Mirror the same row into a compact strip directly under the HP/MP/EXP bars so cooldowns are readable next to the vitals.

v0.25.36 Strip dead character-sprite scaffolding + delete chibi_nude.png

User: "you're running the character sprite by mistake, delete the character sprite, we are not supposed to use sprite." Even though drawLayeredCharacter returned false unconditionally since v0.25.29, the boot path was still calling _loadCharLayer('base_chibi', 'Sprites/character/chibi_nude.png') on every page load — quietly fetching ~1.9 MB of PNG that no draw call ever consulted. Plus ~150 lines of dead asset-loader / frame-picker / layered-renderer code lying around with stale comments. All gone.

🪦 What was removed

  • Block 1 (former lines 16880-16955) — CHARACTER_ASSETS map, _loadCharLayer, _drawCharFrame, _currentCharFrame, CHAR_FRAMES_X / CHAR_FRAMES_Y constants, and the auto-load _loadCharLayer('base_chibi', 'Sprites/character/chibi_nude.png') that ran on every boot.
  • Block 2 (former lines 19953-20065) — ASSETS map, SPRITE_FRAME_W / SPRITE_FRAME_H / SPRITE_SCALE constants, loadSprite, loadCharacterAssets (the ~30-PNG todo list pointing to Sprites/character/overlays/ — never invoked), currentCharacterFrame, drawFrame, and the drawLayeredCharacter stub with its preserved-for-the-future block comment.
  • drawPlayer branch — if (drawLayeredCharacter(sx, sy)) { ... } early-return is gone; drawCuteCharacter is invoked directly.
  • BOOT comment + commented loadCharacterAssets() call replaced with a short tombstone explaining the sprite system is removed for good (not just disabled).

📦 Tree changes

  • Sprites/character/chibi_nude.png deleted (was tracked, 1.9 MB).
  • Sprites/character/{base_female.png, base_male.png, overlays/*} deleted (were untracked, never referenced from gameplay code).
  • The whole Sprites/character/ directory is gone.
  • Other Sprites/ subtrees (skills/, vfx/, ui/, items/, equipment/) untouched — they live under different code paths and weren't part of this removal request.

🎨 Canonical character renderer

drawCuteCharacter is the only character renderer — procedural chibi pixel art using CUTE_PAL and per-class CUTE_CLASS_COLORS, with the v0.25.30 illustrative shading pass on cape / weapon / hat / face / skin. No PNG asset fallback to reinstate; if a future iteration wants sprite-driven character art it should be designed from scratch.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.36. Net change: +27 / −271 lines. Two big deletion blocks, one short branch simplification in drawPlayer, two comment refreshes.
  • No save/network/gameplay/protocol impact. SPRITE_W and SPRITE_H (the player hitbox dimensions, used at the player object init) are kept — those are gameplay constants despite the name.

v0.25.35 Desktop skill bar redesign — small icons + corner key badges + conic cooldown

User: "for full screen on an open windows, could you also do the same thing, but make the icons small." The mobile face cluster (v0.25.33 sweep + v0.25.34 icons) read better than the legacy desktop layout — same template now drives the desktop #skill-bar too, just with tighter slots so seven keybinds fit comfortably across the bottom-centre dock.

🧭 What changed visually

  • Slot shrunk from 52 × 64 (column-stacked text) to 44 × 44 square, 2 px border, 8 px radius, overflow: hidden so the cooldown sweep clips inside the rounded corner.
  • Skill icon centered in the slot at 22 px (smaller than the mobile button's 26 px to stay compact on desktop), with a soft drop-shadow for readability over busy backdrops.
  • Key letter moved from a separate row to a 9 px monospace corner badge at bottom: 1px; right: 3px; — same treatment as the mobile .mc-key badge.
  • MP cost line hidden on the compact slot. The full text (e.g. "Magic Bolt — 8 MP") is still readable on hover via the slot's existing title= tooltip.
  • Locked-state legibility — when a slot is gated by level (renderSkillBar swaps the icon for "Lv N"), the icon span drops to 13 px / bold so the gating string fits the smaller slot. Locked opacity bumped 0.30 → 0.45 so the underlying icon stays scannable.

🥧 Cooldown — height fill → MOBA pie-wipe

Old .skill-cd was a vertical bar pinned to the bottom that filled upward as the cooldown counted down — fine but visually different from the mobile face cluster. Now both surfaces use the same overlay:

  • .skill-cd is a full-slot conic-gradient overlay, position: absolute; inset: 0; border-radius: inherit.
  • Driven by a single --cd-pct CSS variable on the slot root (0..100) — the gradient stop is calc(var(--cd-pct, 0) * 3.6deg), so 100 → 360°.
  • Centered 0.0 seconds-remaining label inside the overlay, white text + drop-shadow for legibility against the wedge.
  • Per-tick: renderSkillBar sets root.style.setProperty('--cd-pct', pct) instead of the old cdEl.style.height = pct + '%'. removeProperty on cooldown clear so the overlay disappears cleanly.
  • Display toggle 'block' → 'flex' to match the new centered layout (icon-and-text horizontally + vertically centered).

🤝 Why unify desktop with mobile

v0.25.33 / v0.25.34 shipped well on touch — the icon-first composite reads at a glance, the pie-wipe communicates "X seconds left" without forcing the eye to a number readout. Carrying the same visual language to desktop means: (a) one design vocabulary across surfaces, (b) the existing mobile-tested CSS patterns get re-used (no new visual styles to learn), (c) --cd-pct hits the GPU compositor like the mobile .mc-cd already does — should be cheaper than the per-frame height write the old bar did.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.35. .skill-slot CSS block fully rewritten (~50 lines). renderSkillBar's block-slot branch + skill-slot loop both swap cdEl.style.height for root.style.setProperty('--cd-pct').
  • No save/network/gameplay/protocol impact. Mobile face cluster unchanged. Slot wiring (_sbBuild / _sbSlots[]) unchanged — the same DOM works for both old and new visuals because the icon, key, and cd children were already separate spans.

v0.25.34 Skill icons on mobile face buttons (with corner key badges)

User asked for skill icons + cooldown timers on the gameplay screen. The cooldown timers were already on the mobile face buttons (v0.25.33's pie-wipe sweep). Missing piece: the buttons were just Z / X / S / C / D / V / G letter labels — no indication of what skill each fired. The poll loop in _wireMobileCooldownSweep() already resolved each button's skill every 50 ms; now it also pushes the matched skill's def.icon into the .mc-icon span. Icons auto-track class pick / job advance / master pick — no extra event hookup needed.

🚪 Empty-slot fallback

V (job ult) and G (master signature) start empty until the player advances. Buttons detect this via missing icon and set data-empty="1", which falls back the .mc-key style to centered-larger letter — i.e. the original letter-only look — so the button is still readable as "press G" until G unlocks. Once a master is picked, the icon swaps in and the key badge shrinks to the corner.

F stays letter-only

F is intentionally skipped (still has data-dynamic="f-block"). Its dispatch is dynamic (interact / portal / Q-cast / block depending on context); a static icon would be wrong for at least one of those modes.

v0.25.33 Bring back MOBA-style cooldown pie-wipe sweep

User changed their mind: "I would like MOBA-style cooldown pie-wipe sweep and skill face buttons." Reverts both v0.25.31 reverts in one shot — the conic-gradient cooldown sweep on the mobile face cluster (Z/X/S/C/D/V/G) is back, along with the iOS-compatible <span> DOM rewrite that makes it actually render on iOS Safari.

↪️ What's restored

  • MOBA-style cooldown pie-wipe sweep. Conic-gradient overlay on each circular face button draws a clockwise dark wedge whose angle equals the remaining cooldown fraction. Greys out the button and shows a seconds-remaining label while cooling, snaps back to full saturation the instant the cooldown hits zero.
  • Real <span class="mc-cd"> child element instead of the original ::after pseudo-element. iOS Safari has long-standing quirks rendering pseudo-elements on <button> elements with display: flex parents — the conic-gradient simply didn't paint. The real <span> renders reliably across iOS / Android / desktop.
  • Top-right "?" help button (#help-btn-tr). Sits at top: 38px, right: 12px, opens the existing Controls modal via openHelp(). Mobile-only; desktop CSS hides it. The pre-existing top-left #help-btn stays as well, and the #hotkey-hint chip from v0.25.28 still works as the K-panel tap target.

🛡️ z-index hardening preserved

Both v0.25.32's surgical z-index fix and the original 365d301 z-index hardening converged to #top-ui { z-index: 8 !important; } + #right-ui { z-index: 8 !important; }. Conflict resolved by keeping v0.25.32's version (without the redundant position: relative override that the original 365d301 added — z-index applies fine on the existing position: absolute base).

v0.25.32 Re-add iOS HUD z-index hardening — HP/MP/EXP bars back

User report after v0.25.31: "I don't see the Z X S C D V G skill bar... bring the HP MP EXP bar back as well." A live mobile preview confirmed the face cluster (Z/X/S/C/D/V/G) was actually still visible — but the HP/MP/EXP and right-ui (Lumens/ATK/DEF/Crit/Kills) bars had disappeared on iOS Safari. The defensive z-index hardening originally bundled into 365d301 got removed by the v0.25.31 revert. This release re-adds only that fix — no cooldown sweep, no DOM rewrite, no top-right help button.

🩹 The fix

@media (pointer: coarse), (max-width: 900px) {
  #top-ui   { z-index: 8 !important; }
  #right-ui { z-index: 8 !important; ...rest unchanged }
}

Position kept as base position: absolute (not promoted to relative as the original 365d301 did) — z-index applies fine on absolute-positioned elements, and there's no need to alter the existing top:10 left:10 absolute positioning relative to the wrapper.

🧠 Why this happens on iOS Safari

The Phaser UI canvas (#phaser-ui-canvas, z-index 3, added in v0.25.17 onward) sits on top of the same top-of-screen area as the HUD blocks. iOS Safari's GPU compositor can hide DOM siblings that share a stacking layer with a transparent canvas — even when the canvas is display:none by default. Pushing the HUD blocks to z-index: 8 puts them safely above and the bug goes away.

What's still gone (intentionally)

Per the v0.25.31 user request:

  • MOBA-style cooldown pie-wipe sweep on face buttons — still gone.
  • Cooldown DOM rewrite from ::after to real <span> — still gone.
  • Top-right help button — still gone.

The #hotkey-hint chip from v0.25.28 still works as a tap target for the K (Hotkeys / Skills / Level Up) panel.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.32. Two CSS lines added inside the existing @media (pointer: coarse), (max-width: 900px) block. No JS, no DOM, no other changes.

v0.25.31 Revert mobile cooldown sweep + DOM rewrite (restore old skill bar look)

User asked for the old skill-bar / cooldown look back. Reverts the two recent mobile-cooldown commits: 43179b0 (MOBA-style conic-gradient pie-wipe sweep on face buttons) and 365d301 (DOM rewrite from ::after to real <span> + HUD z-index hardening + top-right help button). Mobile face buttons now go back to plain solid-colour with no cooldown indicator.

  • Cooldown DOM rewrite — gone. The ::after pseudo-element approach is also gone (since the sweep itself is gone). No CD overlay element is rendered at all on mobile face buttons.
  • Top-right help button (#help-btn-tr) — gone. The pre-existing top-left #help-btn remains, and the #hotkey-hint chip from v0.25.28 also still works as a tap target for the K panel.
  • HUD z-index hardening on #top-ui / #right-ui for mobile — gone. These two blocks no longer get the z-index: 8 + position: relative defensive bump that was added because iOS Safari's GPU compositor was occasionally hiding DOM elements that share a stacking layer with the transparent #phaser-ui-canvas (z:3).

With it reverted, the HP/MP/EXP and Lumens/ATK/DEF/Crit/Kills blocks may disappear behind the Phaser UI canvas on iOS again. If that recurs in your testing, ping me and I'll re-add just the z-index fix as a one-line patch without restoring the cooldown changes.

None of the reverted commits touched the desktop skill bar — desktop view is identical to v0.25.30.

v0.25.30 Equipment + face/skin illustrative polish (cape / weapon / hat)

Continues the v0.25.29 illustrative-shading pass into the equipment and face/skin layers. Adds a procedural cape (which the procedural path was missing entirely), travelling specular gleam on blades, class-specific shine bands on hats, glossy double-catchlight on eyes, and a 3-tone skin shading band that bridges the lit/shadow step on the head.

🦸 Procedural cape (NEW)

Capes only existed in the disabled v0.25.26 layered-sprite system; the procedural path drew nothing. New _drawCuteCape renders a trapezoid silhouette anchored at the shoulders, draping to mid-thigh, with a sine sway that grows with walk speed. Class-coloured trim band along the hem (warrior gold / mage purple / rogue teal / archer silver) gives instant class identity. Drawn BEFORE the torso so the body silhouette overlaps it from the front.

⚔️ Weapon polish — travelling blade gleam

  • Travelling specular gleam — vertical 1×3-4 px near-white strip that scrolls along the blade as game.time advances. Modulo loop so it reads as a moving reflection. Different phase per blade variant (sword swing / sword idle / dagger) so multiple weapons on screen don't sync.
  • Tip pip — single bright pixel at the blade point.
  • Crossguard glint — warm-white pip on the gold guard.
  • Pommel highlight — small warm-white circle on the upper-left of the round pommel.

👑 Hat polish — class-specific shine bands

  • Mage wizard hat — sheen band on the brim + 3 fading cone-tier shine strips + brim glint pip.
  • Warrior helmet — metal sheen across the dome + glint pip + warm gold glints on the side plates + plume tip catches light.
  • Rogue bandana — cloth sheen across the band + white pip on the forehead gem.
  • Archer cap — cap sheen band + glint pip + white glint on feather tip.
  • Three reusable rgba constants (SHEEN / SHEENZ / RIM) at the top of drawCuteHat keep the polish language consistent.

👁️ Face overlay polish

  • Cheek blush picks up a brighter inner pip (1 px rgba(255,200,210,0.85) peak inside the 2×2 pink rect) — the hand-painted "rosy peak" instead of a flat colour patch.
  • Glossy anime double-catchlight on each eye: primary white pip top-left of pupil + secondary 60%-alpha catchlight bottom-right. The iconic "wet eye" gloss of high-end chibi art.
  • BIG fix — replaced the per-frame full-figure 'lighter'-blend wash glow with a small head-only radial. Old code brightened the WHOLE character every frame, which under the alpha pulse made the body / weapon / cape look hazy and low-contrast at the peak. New version reads as a class aura around the head without flattening contrast on the body.

🎨 Skin polish — 3-tone mid-band

Old: hard 2-tone step on the head (lit base → cel shadow). New: 3 px mid-tone strip along the shadow boundary, mixed 45% between base skin and shadow tone. Gives proper 3-tone shading:

  • Highlight (specular blob + pip from v0.25.29)
  • Lit base
  • Mid band ← new
  • Cel shadow
  • Chin cast shadow
  • Rim light (warm crescent on shadow side from v0.25.29)

Six distinct lighting bands on the head now — the standard for hand-painted chibi illustration. _mixHex-driven so future skin tone changes flow through automatically.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.30. New _drawCuteCape function (~85 lines). _drawCuteSword / SwordIdle / Dagger each pick up gleam + glint passes. drawCuteHat per-class blocks each get shine bands + glints (3 reusable rgba consts at top). _drawCuteFaceOverlay rewritten — eye double-catchlight + targeted head-only aura replacing the wash glow. drawCuteCharacter head section gets the mid-tone band.
  • No save/network/gameplay impact. Pure visual polish.

v0.25.29 Sprite removed — procedural chibi gets illustrative shading polish

Reverts the v0.25.26 sprite path (proportions / lighting / facing didn't read well in-game) and pushes the procedural drawCuteCharacter further toward an "illustrative cel-shaded" look — soft drop-shadow, anime specular highlights on head + torso, warm rim light on the back-shadow side, inner ink contour on the body, hair shine band, boot specular pip.

🚪 Sprite path disabled

drawLayeredCharacter returns false unconditionally again (as in v0.25.2). The whole CHARACTER_ASSETS infrastructure (loader / frame helper / slot dispatch) is preserved as a comment block — a future asset pass with proper lighting + matching equipment layers can flip it back on by removing the early return. chibi_nude.png stays in the repo as reference for what NOT to ship without lighting work.

🌑 Ground shadow — multi-tone soft falloff

Old: single 13×3.5 ellipse @ 35% alpha, hard ring with a visible edge.

New: three stacked ellipses for proper soft-drop-shadow falloff — outer 17×5 halo @ 10% alpha, mid 14×4 transition @ 22% alpha, inner 10×2.4 contact dot @ 42% alpha. Plus a subtle idle-only pulse (sin(idleT × 1.5) × 5%) so the shadow breathes when standing still and smooths to zero as movement ramps up.

👤 Head polish — specular + rim light

Three new passes inside the head circle clip:

  • Specular blob — soft white ellipse near the upper-left temple at 65% alpha. The classic anime "shiny forehead" highlight.
  • Specular pip — tighter brighter (95% alpha) core inside the blob for the wet/glossy peak.
  • Rim light — thin warm crescent (rgba(255,210,170,0.55)) traced along the lower-right shadow side, simulating back-light bouncing around the silhouette.

🧥 Torso polish — same lighting language as head

Mirrors the head pass for visual consistency:

  • Specular highlight on the upper-left chest (45% alpha ellipse).
  • Rim light warm crescent (45% alpha) traced from shoulder down to waist on the back-shadow side.
  • Inner ink contour — 30% black stroke offset inward by 1 px (via 0.5 px aliasing translate). Outline now reads as ink on top of paint, not a hard cut-out edge.

💇 Hair shine band

Thin near-white horizontal strip across the top of the hair mass. Two stops: 12 px @ 42% for the base sheen, 5 px @ 85% for the brighter middle peak. Replaces the flat hairHi rim with the iconic glossy-anime-hair band.

👢 Boot specular pip

Tiny 2×1 px white highlight (70% alpha) on the front of each boot. Walks with the existing wc leg-cycle offset. Sells the leather sheen.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.29. drawLayeredCharacter early-returns false (preserves the body as comment block). drawCuteCharacter picks up ~90 lines of new shading passes — ground shadow, head specular + rim, torso specular + rim + inner ink, hair shine band, boot specular pip.
  • No save/network/gameplay impact. All purely visual; flag-off and Phaser-on paths both see the same polished art.

Two small but visible polish items. A new persistent chip in the top-left corner reminds players that K opens the Hotkeys / Skills / Level Up panel (and is tappable on mobile, where the keyboard hint strip is hidden). The chibi sprite sheet's facing was inverted in v0.25.26 — fixed in v0.25.27 by flipping the mirror condition.

  • Level + class — already in #top-ui ("Lv.N "). No change.
  • Skill bar with cooldowns — already at bottom-center (#skill-bar) with per-slot cooldown sweep overlays. No change.
  • "Press K for hotkeys guide" — NEW as #hotkey-hint chip.

🆕 The K-Hotkeys chip

  • Persistent at top:80px / left:10px inside .game-wrapper, just below the existing HP/MP/EXP stack.
  • Visible on both desktop and mobile. The existing #controls hint strip (Enter/N/B/R/T/M) is hidden by display:none !important inside the mobile media query — mobile users had no entry point to the K panel without typing. The new chip survives the mobile rule.
  • Tap/click dispatches synthetic k keydown + keyup events, triggering the same panel handler as the physical key. Works as both a label AND a button.
  • Styled to match the rest of the dark/gold HUD chrome — dark plate, gold text, kbd-styled key indicator.

🧭 v0.25.27 sprite facing fix (folded into this release)

The chibi sprite sheet shipped in v0.25.26 natively faces LEFT, but my _drawCharFrame assumed RIGHT — visible result was the chibi moonwalking right while facing-left frames played, and vice versa. Flipped the mirror condition so the sprite now walks the same direction it's moving.

Touched surface

v0.25.26 Layered chibi sprite sheets — base body in, equipment slots wired

Reintroduces the layered-sprite-sheet pipeline disabled in v0.25.2, this time as a proper modular system designed for adding equipment incrementally without redrawing the base. The nude chibi base body is on screen now; hair / armor / cape / helmet / shield / weapon / boots slots are wired in but empty — drop a PNG matching the 4×4 pose layout into Sprites/character/<slot>/<id>.png and it appears.

🖼️ The asset

Sprites/character/chibi_nude.png — 1216×2312, 4×4 grid of 304×578 walk-cycle frames. Pre-loaded at boot via _loadCharLayer('base_chibi', ...). Other equipment slots load lazily on first lookup.

🧩 Why layered sprite sheets and not skeletal

The big concern with flat sprite sheets is equipment variety — every armor / helmet / cape would multiply the per-frame asset count. Layered sheets sidestep this: each equipment piece is its own per-pose PNG drawn to match the base's frame layout, transparent everywhere else. Composited at runtime, base + gear reads as one unified character. This is how MapleStory, Stardew Valley, and most chibi-2D MMOs handle the equipment problem — you draw each gear piece once across the same 16 poses, not once per body × armor × helmet × etc combination.

Skeletal animation (Spine / DragonBones) was the alternative — lower per-piece artist cost, but requires rigging the base, paid tooling, and weeks of pipeline work before anything ships. The layered-sheet path lets you ship the base today and add equipment one piece at a time without restructuring.

🛠️ How equipment will work

  1. Artist draws a gear piece across all 16 poses, matching the base sheet's pivot points (transparent where no gear).
  2. Save as Sprites/character/<slot>/<id>.png (slot ∈ hair / armor / cape / helmet / shield / weapon / boots).
  3. Set the relevant equipped item's spriteKey to '<id>'.
  4. Item appears on the character with zero code changes.

📐 Architecture

  • CHARACTER_ASSETS — module-level Map keyed by '<slot>_<id>'. Lazy-load on first access via _loadCharLayer; missing files silently no-op.
  • CHAR_FRAMES_X / CHAR_FRAMES_Y = 4 × 4 — frame grid layout, configurable per future sheet.
  • _currentCharFrame() picks frame index from player state. v0.25.26 implements idle (frame 0) + 4-frame walk cycle. Future iterations extend this with attack / jump / hurt rows.
  • _drawCharFrame(img, sx, sy, frame, facing) blits one frame of one layer with horizontal-flip support. Anchored to the player's feet so the figure stands on the ground regardless of source frame height.
  • drawLayeredCharacter orchestrates the layer stack: base → hair → armor → cape → helmet → shield → weapon → boots. Returns true on successful base draw so drawPlayer skips procedural fallback.

🔄 Fallback path preserved

drawPlayer's existing dispatch is unchanged: it tries drawLayeredCharacter first, falls back to procedural drawCuteCharacter if anything fails. If you delete the base PNG or the network blocks it, the game still renders via the procedural pixel art that's been there since v0.25.2.

⚖️ Known scope trades

  • Procedural face overlay still draws on top. The sprite has no facial details; _drawCuteFaceOverlay brings the character to life. If the eye position is off vs the sprite head, future polish can add face frames as a separate layer.
  • Frame layout assumed 4×4. If your future sheets use a different grid (e.g. 8 columns × 2 rows for a more granular cycle), tweak CHAR_FRAMES_X / Y or move to per-asset metadata.
  • Walk cycle uses row 0 only. Other rows in the current sheet may be different states — adjust _currentCharFrame() when you know the layout.
  • Procedural cape / weapon swing animations skipped when the sprite path is active. They were calibrated for the procedural body; sprite-based gear handles those visuals once the gear PNGs land.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.26. New CHARACTER_ASSETS map, _loadCharLayer / _currentCharFrame / _drawCharFrame helpers (~75 lines). drawLayeredCharacter rewritten from return false to the full slot composition (~50 lines).
  • New asset — Sprites/character/chibi_nude.png.
  • Vanilla / Phaser flag-off path unchanged.

v0.25.25 Phaser 3 migration — Phase 5b (boss banner + flash overlay)

Phase 5b closes out the HUD migration. The two remaining canvas-rendered HUD pieces — the super-boss top-of-screen banner and the white flash overlay — move to a new LXOverlayScene on the UI canvas at the topmost depth. Combined with Phase 5a's mob HUD migration, every canvas-2D HUD draw is now batched through Phaser when the flag is on.

⚡ LXOverlayScene

  • Flash overlay — single full-canvas Phaser.Rectangle (depth 100). Each frame setAlpha tracks game.flashOverlay. Replaces vanilla's per-frame fillRect(0,0,W,H).
  • Boss banner pre-built scene tree at create():
    • Plate backdrop (phase-coloured stroke, hyper-boss variants 3 px instead of 2 px)
    • Name label (16 px bold, phase-coloured, prefix "⚠ HYPER BOSS — " when m.hyperBoss set)
    • HP bar background (1.5 W full width, dark plum)
    • Phase tick marks at 33% and 66% (translucent white)
    • HP fill (single solid colour per phase — see scope trade below)
    • Shimmer highlight along top edge of fill
    • White inner border
    • HP/phase readout text ("currentHP / maxHP · PHASE n")
  • Hidden by default. Banner only visible when game.monsters contains a live m.superBoss. _setBossBannerVisible(v) toggles all 8 components in one call.

🚪 Decay split for flash overlay

Vanilla's flash block both painted the rect and decayed the alpha (game.flashOverlay *= 0.75). If the whole block were gated by Phaser, decay would stop and the overlay would stay at full alpha forever. The fix splits paint from state mutation: the gate only short-circuits the canvas paint; the decay step keeps running unconditionally so both renderers stay in sync.

⚖️ Scope trade — HP bar gradient

Vanilla's HP fill used ctx.createLinearGradient with a 2-stop horizontal gradient that varied per phase. Phaser Rectangle objects don't support per-frame gradients without per-phase pre-rendered gradient textures + a TileSprite. Phase 5b uses a single solid colour per phase as a first-pass approximation. If the bar reads as flat in play, follow-up polish can add the gradient back — but it's a 60 px-tall element only visible during boss fights, so the cosmetic loss is small.

🎯 What's left on vanilla

After Phase 5b, the remaining canvas-2D draws are:

  • Monster body silhouettes for non-blob types (humanoid mobs, bosses, zodiac bosses) — pending Phase 4d-3+
  • Hit-flash filter applied to monster bodies (vanilla wraps body in save/restore)
  • Burn FX (fire particles overlaid on monsters)
  • Mob chat bubbles (_drawMobChat)
  • Player character sprite + procedural weapons/cape — Phase 3b
  • A few projectile types (voidbeam) — Phase 4c-2 follow-up

Player stats panel, minimap, level-up modal, inventory, chat log, combo meter, low-HP vignette, level-up DOM toast — all DOM, never need Phaser.

📅 Migration roadmap

  • ✅ Phase 1-5a (v0.25.15 - v0.25.24).
  • ✅ Phase 5b. Boss banner + flash overlay (this release).
  • Phase 4d-3+ Remaining mob bodies (humanoids, bosses, zodiac).
  • Phase 3b. Character sprite.
  • Phase 6. Retire vanilla canvas.

How to try it

Append ?phaser=1 and trigger any boss fight (Aetherion, Gravitos, zodiac bosses). The banner now renders through Phaser. Take a hit to see the flash overlay. DevTools:

const s = window.__LX_PHASER_UI.scene.getScene('lx_overlay');
s._flash.alpha           // tracks game.flashOverlay
s._bbName.text           // boss name when banner visible
s._bbInfo.text           // "current / max · PHASE n"

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.25. New LXOverlayScene (~100 lines) added to UI scene: list. New _phaserHandlingOverlay() gate. Vanilla drawSuperBossBar early-return + main-loop flash block split (decay always, paint guarded).
  • No save/network/gameplay/protocol impact. Flag-off path unchanged.

v0.25.24 Phaser 3 migration — Phase 5a (mob HP bars + names)

Phase 5a opens the HUD migration: the per-monster HP bar + name label — the highest-fire-rate canvas HUD elements in the game — move to a pooled Phaser scene on the UI canvas. Every visible mob fired 5+ canvas-2D ops per frame on vanilla (bar bg, bar fill, measureText, name bg, name text); pooled rectangles + Text objects in Phaser collapse all of those into batched WebGL draws.

📊 LXMonsterUIScene

  • Four parallel pools — _bgBarPool, _fillBarPool, _bgNamePool, _namePool. Each pool batches independently; depth ordering keeps fills above backings.
  • Phaser GameObjects.Rectangle for the bars + name backing — no preload, no texture lookup. setSize() per frame mutates the in-place vertex buffer (cheap).
  • Phaser.Text pool for mob names. Text width readback (t.width) is cached internally by Phaser and only recalculates when the string changes — replaces vanilla's per-frame ctx.measureText.
  • HP bar fill colour matches vanilla's three-tier scheme: green > 50%, yellow 25-50%, red < 25%. setFillStyle per frame is a one-uniform update.
  • Boss differentiation — name labels render at 12 px bold orange for bosses, 10 px white for grunts. Both come from the same Text pool with per-instance setFontSize / setFontStyle / setColor.
  • Cull envelope matches vanilla (±40 px around viewport).

🚪 Gate

New _phaserHandlingMonsterUI() mirrors the existing pattern. drawMonster gets a single-line return between ctx.restore() and the HP bar block — short-circuits when the scene is up. Importantly, the gate fires after the body's save/restore + burn FX, so those continue to render on vanilla without disruption.

💡 Why this is the perf-impact pick for HUD migration

Most "HUD" elements in this game are DOM (player stats panel, minimap, level-up modal, inventory, chat log). The canvas-rendered HUD pieces are: per-mob HP bars + names (high count, every frame), boss banner (one per frame in boss fights), flash overlay (one per frame on hit). Per-mob HUD is the only one that fires > 1 per frame — and during boss arenas with 3-5 elites + a boss + their HP bars on screen, it's been measurable.

🤝 Combined with prior phases

With this release, monsters now flow through Phaser for:

  • Body (slime/snail/mushroom from Phase 4d-1/4d-2)
  • HP bars + name labels (every mob type — this release)

Future 4d-3+ types automatically get the HUD migration "for free" — the gate doesn't filter by mob type. Body ports are independent and additive.

📅 Migration roadmap

  • ✅ Phase 1-4d-2 (v0.25.15 - v0.25.23).
  • ✅ Phase 5a. Mob HP bars + name labels (this release).
  • Phase 5b. Super boss banner + flash overlay.
  • Phase 4d-3+ Remaining mob bodies (humanoids, bosses, zodiac).
  • Phase 3b. Character sprite.
  • Phase 6. Retire vanilla canvas.

How to try it

Append ?phaser=1 and engage any mob. HP bars and name labels are now Phaser-rendered. DevTools:

const s = window.__LX_PHASER_UI.scene.getScene('lx_monster_ui');
s._bgBarPool.length     // grows to peak visible-mob count
s._namePool.length      // same
s._fillUsed             // mobs currently showing damage

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.24. New LXMonsterUIScene (~110 lines) added to UI scene: list. New _phaserHandlingMonsterUI() gate. drawMonster gets a one-line early-return.
  • No save/network/gameplay/protocol impact. Flag-off path unchanged.

v0.25.23 Phaser 3 migration — Phase 4d-2 (snail + mushroom)

Phase 4d-2: two more blob mob types land on Phaser. Snail and mushroom (plus its orange variant) follow the slime template from 4d-1 — pre-rendered body texture at boot, dispatch via textureForMob(), vanilla drawCuteMob short-circuits via the existing _phaserHandlingMonsterBody(m) gate. No new architectural work; the slot of bench from 4d-1 is doing real work now.

🐌 Snail — 36×28 px texture

  • Wide squat oval body (foot) — white base for runtime tinting.
  • Round purple shell on top with two concentric spiral lines — not tinted (shells stay purple regardless of mob colour, matching vanilla).
  • Two antenna stalks with eye dots, body smile.
  • Shell sheen highlight, white-base body edge stroke.

🍄 Mushroom + orange mushroom — 30×32 px texture (shared)

  • Big red dome cap with 4 white polka dots — not tinted (caps are iconically red across all mushroom variants).
  • White-base stem with eye dots, sparkle highlights, smile, blush, and tiny black feet — tinted at runtime via setTint(m.color) so regular and orange mushrooms differentiate via the stem colour.
  • Both m.type === 'mushroom' and m.type === 'orange' route to this single texture.

🛠️ Plumbing

  • New addMob(key, w, h, draw) helper in preload — convenience wrapper around createCanvas + addCanvas so each new mob's texture stays a self-contained block. Reduces boilerplate as more types land.
  • New _texBaseSize(key) method returns natural dimensions per texture; the update loop now derives scale from m.w / m.h ÷ baseSize rather than hardcoded 28×22 from the slime port.
  • No new gates — vanilla drawCuteMob still short-circuits via the v0.25.22 _phaserHandlingMonsterBody(m) check, which calls into the scene's textureForMob dispatch. Adding new types is now a 2-line change (texture entry + dispatch case).

⚖️ Visual trades (per type)

  • Snail. No body squash; single static silhouette + bob. Antenna stalks are static (vanilla redraws them per-frame angled toward facing — minor difference).
  • Mushroom. Orange mushroom's grumpy frown collapses to the same smile as regular mushroom. Mood now reads via stem colour alone. Polka dot positions don't shift across spawns (vanilla's are deterministic so this matches).
  • HP bars / name labels / burn FX / hit-flash filter still vanilla on top of the Phaser sprite, same as 4d-1.

📅 Migration roadmap

  • ✅ Phase 1-4c-2 (v0.25.15 - v0.25.21).
  • ✅ Phase 4d-1. Slime monster (v0.25.22).
  • ✅ Phase 4d-2. Snail + mushroom (this release).
  • Phase 4d-3. Horny / stump / humanoid mobs (zombie / skeleton / mummy / wraith / scorpion).
  • Phase 4d-4. Bosses (king slime / mushmom / aetherion / gravitos).
  • Phase 4d-5. Zodiac bosses (12 of them).
  • Phase 5. HUD.
  • Phase 3b. Character sprite.
  • Phase 6. Retire vanilla canvas.

How to try it

Append ?phaser=1 and head to a wilderness map. Slimes, snails, and mushrooms (regular + orange) now render through Phaser. DevTools:

const s = window.__LX_PHASER_UI.scene.getScene('lx_monsters');
s.textureForMob({type:'snail'})     // 'lx_mob_snail'
s.textureForMob({type:'mushroom'})  // 'lx_mob_mushroom'
s.textureForMob({type:'orange'})    // 'lx_mob_mushroom' (shared)
s.textureForMob({type:'horny'})     // null (still on vanilla)

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.23. Two new texture blocks in LXMonsterScene.preload (~70 lines combined). New addMob helper + _texBaseSize dispatch in the scene. textureForMob grows from 1 type to 3 types (slime/snail/mushroom+orange).
  • No save/network/gameplay/protocol impact. Flag-off path unchanged.

v0.25.22 Phaser 3 migration — Phase 4d-1 (slime monsters)

First step into Phase 4d: the biggest remaining surgery. Monster bodies are procedurally rendered with squash/breathing animations, hit flashes, facing flips, and per-type silhouettes — far more state than projectiles or particles. This release ports the simplest mob (slime) end-to-end and lays the architectural groundwork for follow-up sessions to add more types incrementally without re-deriving the wiring.

🎯 Why such a narrow first slice?

A naive "port all monsters at once" approach would mean re-implementing 9+ distinct procedural draw functions (each 30-60 lines) plus boss variants and zodiac bosses. That's 2-3 sessions of work and the kind of monolithic change CLAUDE.md's scope guardrails explicitly warn against. Slime alone proves the full pipeline (scene → texture → pool → vanilla skip) and gives every later type a copy-paste template.

👾 LXMonsterScene

  • Pre-rendered slime body at preload — 28×22 px white-base teardrop with dark outline, eyes, smile, top sheen. Tint applied at runtime so each slime matches its m.color.
  • Sprite pool on the UI canvas at depth 2 (under the depth-5 particle pool — hit sparks correctly sit OVER the body).
  • Per-frame sync — position centered on hitbox with bob (sin(animTimer × 0.02) × 1.5 matching vanilla), scale derived from m.w / m.h, facing via setFlipX.
  • Hit flash reproduced via setTintFill(0xffffff) in the bright phase — approximates vanilla's ctx.filter = 'brightness(2.5)'.
  • Type filter via textureForMob(m) — returns 'lx_mob_slime' only for m.type === 'slime'; bosses and zodiac bosses always skip; everything else returns null → vanilla.

🚪 Vanilla skip

New gate _phaserHandlingMonsterBody(m) mirrors the projectile pattern. drawCuteMob's very first statement returns when true. drawMonster's outer wrapper still runs HP bar, name label, burn FX, and the hit-flash filter — only the silhouette is yielded.

⚖️ Scope trades

  • Squash/breathing animation lost — vanilla slime pulses via animTimer-driven width/height oscillation around the ellipse. The Phaser sprite has a static silhouette + bob, no width oscillation. Subtle visual regression.
  • Pink drip effect skipped — vanilla draws two tiny pink pixels below the slime every other 60-frame cycle. Could come back as a particle emission in future polish.
  • Burn FX still vanilla on top — when a slime is on fire and the flag is on, the orange burn flames render on the vanilla canvas underneath the Phaser sprite. Visible as flames "behind" the slime instead of in front. Cosmetic regression; documented for follow-up.

📅 Migration roadmap

  • ✅ Phase 1-4c-2 (v0.25.15 - v0.25.21).
  • ✅ Phase 4d-1. Slime monster (this release).
  • Phase 4d-2. Snail + mushroom + horny + stump (other "blob" mobs).
  • Phase 4d-3. Humanoid mobs (zombie / skeleton / mummy / wraith / scorpion).
  • Phase 4d-4. Bosses (king slime / mushmom / aetherion / gravitos).
  • Phase 4d-5. Zodiac bosses (12 of them — share _zBodyPath).
  • Phase 5. HUD.
  • Phase 3b. Character sprite.
  • Phase 6. Retire vanilla canvas.

How to try it

Append ?phaser=1 and head to a wilderness map. Slimes (the pink/blue/yellow blob mobs) now render through Phaser; every other mob still runs through vanilla. DevTools:

const s = window.__LX_PHASER_UI.scene.getScene('lx_monsters');
s.textureForMob({type:'slime'})         // 'lx_mob_slime'
s.textureForMob({type:'snail'})         // null (vanilla)
s.textureForMob({type:'slime', isBoss:true})  // null (king slime → vanilla)

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.22. New LXMonsterScene (~130 lines) added to UI scene: list. New _phaserHandlingMonsterBody(m) gate. drawCuteMob gets a one-line top-of-function early-return.
  • No save/network/gameplay/protocol impact. Flag-off path unchanged.

v0.25.21 Phaser 3 migration — Phase 4c-2 (full projectile port)

Phase 4c-2: the v0.25.20 arrow-only port grows to cover every projectile type except voidbeam. Two pieces of work — a refactor that splits side-effect particle emissions out of the render loop, and an expanded LXProjectileScene that pre-renders eleven projectile textures at boot and dispatches per-projectile through a single batched WebGL pipeline.

🔧 Refactor — emissions out of render

Vanilla drawProjectiles historically pushed trail / dust / sparkle particles inline inside its per-skill render branches. New emitProjectileTrails() function pulls every emission out byte-for-byte (same spawn math, same game.time % N cadence) and runs from the main update tick — guaranteed every frame regardless of which renderer draws the projectile shape. Affects:

  • fire — trail every frame
  • mspore — orange dust every 4 frames
  • mdark — purple sparkles every 3 frames
  • mtoxic — green drips every 4 frames
  • shard — violet trail every 2 frames
  • voidbeam — 2 plasma particles every 2 frames

🖼️ Pre-rendered texture set (11)

Each projectile archetype renders ONCE to an offscreen canvas at preload and registers as a Phaser texture. Runtime per-frame cost collapses to setPosition / setRotation / setScale / setTint on a pooled sprite — same sprite-batched WebGL pipeline as Phase 4a particles.

TextureMaps to
lx_arrowarrow / charged / deadeye / rainArrow / elemArrow (player)
lx_firefireball
lx_iceice spike
lx_daggerdagger
lx_boltplayer default magic bolt
lx_msporeenemy spore pellet
lx_mdarkenemy dark bolt
lx_msplinterenemy wooden splinter
lx_mtoxicenemy toxic blob
lx_shardenemy crystal shard
lx_enemyenemy default ellipse bolt

🔁 Per-projectile dispatch

The scene's update loop drives a unified pipeline:

  • Texture lookup via textureForProj(p) — also used by the vanilla skip gate so the two can't disagree.
  • Rotation — arrow / ice / dagger / msplinter rotate to match velocity (atan2(vy, vx)); shard spins continuously (+ game.time × 0.15); circles/blobs stay axis-aligned.
  • Scale — uniform p.w / texWidth for rotated rectangles; circles/blobs target a diameter of max(10, p.w × 1.8) so the bitmap diameter matches vanilla's radius-based render.
  • Tint — only arrows tint by p.color (vanilla re-colors the shaft); other textures are pre-rendered with their vanilla colors and stay tint=white.
  • Pool reuse — pool sprites swap textures via setTexture(key) when reassigned to a different projectile type; pool grows to peak count, never shrinks.

🚪 Gate

New _phaserHandlingProjectile(p) asks the scene whether it owns this specific projectile. A single early-out at the top of vanilla's render loop short-circuits any projectile Phaser handles. voidbeam (complex linear gradient + direction-dependent geometry) returns null → vanilla keeps drawing it for now.

📅 Migration roadmap

  • ✅ Phase 1. Scaffolding (v0.25.15).
  • ✅ Phase 2. Background (v0.25.16).
  • ✅ Phase 3a. Nameplate + two-canvas (v0.25.17).
  • ✅ Phase 4a. Particles (v0.25.18).
  • ✅ Phase 4b. Halos + damage numbers (v0.25.19).
  • ✅ Phase 4c. Player arrows (v0.25.20).
  • ✅ Phase 4c-2. Full projectile port (this release).
  • Phase 4d. Monsters — biggest surgery (atlas-gen per type).
  • Phase 5. HUD.
  • Phase 3b. Character sprite.
  • Phase 6. Retire vanilla canvas.

Touched surface

  • maple_game.html — version bump to v0.25.21. New emitProjectileTrails() function (~50 lines) wired into the main tick. LXProjectileScene grows to ~250 lines (preload generates 11 textures, update loop dispatches per-type with rotation / scale / tint logic, helpers textureForProj + _texBaseSize + _rotatesWithVelocity). New _phaserHandlingProjectile(p) gate; vanilla drawProjectiles gets a one-line top-of-loop early-out.
  • No save/network/gameplay/protocol impact. Flag-off path unchanged.

v0.25.20 Phaser 3 migration — Phase 4c (arrows)

Narrow Phase 4c: player-owned arrow projectiles render through a new LXProjectileScene on the UI canvas. Scoped deliberately tight — only arrows, not the variety-heavy magic / enemy projectile branches — because arrows are the only projectile type with no side-effect particle emissions baked into vanilla's render loop. Doing the rest properly needs a render/emit refactor that deserves its own session.

🏹 LXProjectileScene

  • Pre-rendered arrow texture generated at preload: a 32×8 canvas with white shaft, gray arrowhead triangle, brown feather bars. Registered as lx_arrow. Tinted per-projectile at runtime so arrows pick up the vanilla p.color field.
  • Sprite pool same pattern as particles / damage numbers. setRotation(atan2(vy, vx)) points the arrow along its velocity; setScale(p.w / 32) matches vanilla's per-projectile width.
  • Skill filter — skill ∈ {arrow, charged, deadeye, rainArrow, elemArrow}. All share the arrow visual in vanilla; Phaser does the same.
  • Owner filter — only p.owner === 'player'. Enemy arrows (if any) stay on vanilla.
  • ±60 px cull matches vanilla.

🚪 Gate

New helper _phaserHandlingArrows(). Vanilla drawProjectiles skips ONLY its arrow branch (continue) when true; every other projectile type continues to render normally through vanilla along with their side-effect emissions (fireball trail, spore dust, dark-bolt sparkles, toxic drips, etc.).

⚖️ Scope trades

  • Deadeye / charged / elemArrow glow overlay intentionally dropped — minor visual regression on those three skill variants' secondary glow rectangle. Can be restored in a follow-up pass with a second ADD-blend sprite per glow-arrow.
  • Fireball / ice / dagger / default-bolt / enemy projectile types stay on vanilla. Each has particle emissions inside the vanilla render branch — moving those to updateProjectiles is a separate refactor (Phase 4c-2, future session).

v0.25.19 Phaser 3 migration — Phase 4b (halos + damage numbers)

Phase 4b: restores the glow-halo pass that 4a intentionally dropped, and ports the per-frame floating damage-number render to a Phaser scene. Both land on the UI canvas (z:3) — same batching story as 4a. Flag-off path still byte-identical.

✨ Glow halos restored

  • Second sprite pool in LXParticleScene (_haloPool) with Phaser.BlendModes.ADD. For each bright particle (maxChannel > 200, matching vanilla _isBrightHex), a halo sprite is drawn behind the core at ~3× scale, 0.35 × life-alpha. Depth 4 (under the depth-5 core pool).
  • Still single-draw-call per batch. ADD-blend sprites batch separately from NORMAL-blend ones; both batches are single-draw regardless of count, so the halo pass is effectively free on GPU.
  • Cull envelope widened to ±30 px (from ±20) — halos are bigger than cores and drop off the visible edge later.

💥 LXDamageNumberScene

Pooled Phaser.Text objects on the UI canvas. Reproduces the bulk of vanilla drawDamageNumbers per-frame animation:

  • ✓ Elastic pop-in scale (first 10 frames, back-overshoot — crits overshoot harder).
  • ✓ Idle breathing bob during mid-life.
  • ✓ Tail shrink + fade in the last min(14, life × 0.32) frames.
  • ✓ Wobble rotation settling over the first 12 frames, sign per-number.
  • ✓ Black outline via setStroke — 6 px for crits, 4.5 px default.
  • ✓ Shadow glow via setShadow — crit blur 16, big blur 8, normal drop-shadow (2, 3).
  • ✓ Same ±80 / ±50 px culling envelope as vanilla.

⚖️ Scope trades

  • Vertical-gradient fill on crits / big hits → solid tint color. Phaser.Text has no native vertical gradient; reproducing it would need a per-number off-screen canvas re-render, defeating the batching. Crits still read punchier because of the heavier stroke and stronger shadow.
  • Two-pass thick outline + inner gold-foil stroke on crits → single setStroke at heavier thickness. Close visually; the gold-foil detail is lost.

🚪 Gate

New helper _phaserHandlingDamageNumbers(). Vanilla drawDamageNumbers returns immediately when it's true — no double-draw.

v0.25.18 Phaser 3 migration — Phase 4a (particles)

Phase 4a of the Phaser migration — the biggest perf target. The per-frame particle draw loop (up to 500 sprites on desktop, 200 on mobile) moves from vanilla Canvas 2D fillRect calls to a pooled Phaser sprite layer on the UI canvas. WebGL batches all same-blend-mode sprites into a single GPU draw call, so the marginal cost per particle drops sharply — this was the dominant per-frame vanilla cost during boss fights and combo bursts.

🎆 LXParticleScene

  • Lives on the UI canvas (#phaser-ui-canvas, z:3). Particles naturally render on top of vanilla entities (hit-sparks, damage numbers, etc.), so the UI-layer placement is correct visually.
  • Sprite pool of Phaser.Image objects backed by a generated 2×2 white texture. Each pool entry is tinted + scaled per-particle. Same-blend-mode sprites are batched by WebGL into a single draw call regardless of particle count.
  • Text pool of Phaser.Text for p.text particles (CRIT! popups and similar).
  • No allocation per frame. Sprites are reused from frame to frame — the pool only grows when the live particle count exceeds the previous high-water mark.
  • Life-based alpha fade (last 20 ticks) and ±20 px culling match vanilla exactly. Colors converted from '#rrggbb' → 0xRRGGBB via the scene's _parseColor helper.

🚪 Gate

New helper _phaserHandlingParticles() mirrors the Phase 2 / 3a pattern. Returns true when the UI Game is up and the particle scene is ready. Vanilla drawParticles returns immediately in that case — no double-draw.

⚖️ Scope trade-offs for 4a

  • Glow halos (vanilla pass 1) intentionally skipped — the additive-blend larger halos behind bright particles are a minor visual contribution. If they read as too flat in play, Phase 4b adds a second bright-particle sprite-per-entity at ADD blend mode for the halo.
  • Damage numbers, projectiles, monsters stay on vanilla for now. These land in Phase 4b/4c — each is smaller in count than particles but benefits from the same batching treatment.

📅 Migration roadmap

  • ✅ Phase 1. Scaffolding + proof-of-concept (v0.25.15).
  • ✅ Phase 2. Background image layer (v0.25.16).
  • ✅ Phase 3a. Two-canvas architecture + player nameplate (v0.25.17).
  • Phase 3b. Character sprite — deferred until after Phase 4.
  • ✅ Phase 4a. Particles (this release).
  • Phase 4b. Damage numbers + glow halos for bright particles.
  • Phase 4c. Projectiles (boss-fight batching win).
  • Phase 4d. Monsters (sprite atlas; biggest surgery).
  • Phase 5. HUD.
  • Phase 3b. Character sprite.
  • Phase 6. Retire vanilla canvas.

v0.25.17 Phaser 3 migration — Phase 3a (player nameplate)

Phase 3a of the Phaser migration. Establishes the two-Phaser-canvas architecture (BG under vanilla, UI over vanilla) and ports the first UI element — the player nameplate — to a Phaser scene. Small visible surface, but the architectural move is the important piece: future HUD migrations (level-up panel, inventory, chat) now have a clear home.

🏗️ Two-canvas architecture

Phaser renders to a single canvas per Game instance. To have content both under vanilla (BG) and over vanilla (UI), we need two Game instances while the migration is in flight. Once Phase 6 retires the vanilla layer, the two canvases merge back into one:

  • #phaser-canvas (z-index 1) — hosts __LX_PHASER_BG running the existing LXBackgroundScene.
  • #game (z-index 2) — vanilla entities, particles, effects (unchanged).
  • #phaser-ui-canvas (z-index 3) — new, hosts __LX_PHASER_UI running the new LXPlayerNameplateScene.

window.__LX_PHASER kept as an alias for __LX_PHASER_BG so any code still referencing the Phase 1 global name keeps working.

🏷️ LXPlayerNameplateScene

Reproduces the vanilla _drawPlayerNameTag look byte-for-byte:

  • Gold 0xffdc8c border at 0.55 alpha, 1 px stroke.
  • Dark 0x140e1e fill at 0.72 alpha.
  • Trebuchet MS bold 11 px, #ffeeaa text, center-aligned.
  • Falls back to title-cased class name when player.look.name is empty.
  • Hidden while paused, dead, or no name available.
  • Text measurement cached on the scene; recomputed only when the display string changes.

🚪 Gate

New helper _phaserHandlingNameplate() mirrors the Phase 2 _phaserHandlingBg() pattern. Returns true when the UI Game is up and the nameplate scene is ready. Vanilla _drawPlayerNameTag returns immediately in that case — no double-draw.

📅 Migration roadmap

  • ✅ Phase 2. Background image layer (v0.25.16).
  • ✅ Phase 3a. Two-canvas architecture + player nameplate (this release).
  • Phase 3b. Character sprite (procedural atlas-gen at boot, Phaser Sprite animated by player state).
  • Phase 4. Monsters, projectiles, particles — biggest perf payoff.
  • Phase 5. HUD (bars, inventory, level-up panel) → UI Phaser.
  • Phase 6. Retire the vanilla canvas; two Phaser Games merge.
